\section{Explicit Enriched Shell Basis and Canonical Core Block}

\subsection*{Short explanation}

The next nonredundant step is to stop speaking abstractly about
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\]
and to write it explicitly.

The correct \(4\)-dimensional Dirac-carrier candidate is the enriched opposite-valley shell space
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}
\otimes
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
sitting inside the truncated shell Bloch space
\[
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}
=
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(N)}
\oplus
\mathcal H_{\mathrm{rest}}^{(N)}.
\]

Once this basis is fixed, the projected block
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
:=
P_D^{(N)} H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p) P_D^{(N)}
\]
has an explicit \(2\times2\) valley-block form.
Its constant term gives the possible Dirac mass,
its pair-diagonal linear splitting gives the longitudinal slope,
and its pair-off-diagonal linear term gives the transverse matrices \(W^1,W^2\).

\section{Explicit definition of the enriched shell carrier}

Fix the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and choose a shell-adapted orthonormal frame
\[
\hat n:=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
(e_1,e_2,\hat n).
\]

Let
\[
\{\chi_1,\chi_2\}
\]
be an orthonormal basis of the shell-relevant enriched internal doublet.
Inside the truncated Bloch shell space, define the four basis vectors
\begin{equation}
|+,a\rangle := |G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
|-,a\rangle := |-G_*,\chi_a\rangle,
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:explicit_HD_basis}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the folded Bragg notation \(k_*=G_*/2\), one may write
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}^{(p)}(x)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}
e^{i(k_*+p)\cdot x}\chi_a,
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}^{(p)}(x)
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}
e^{i(k_*+p-G_*)\cdot x}\chi_a.
\label{eq:folded_explicit_basis}
\end{equation}

These span the \(4\)-dimensional enriched shell carrier
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle\}.
}
\label{eq:HDN_span}
\end{equation}

The corresponding orthogonal projector is
\begin{equation}
P_D^{(N)}
=
\sum_{\sigma=\pm}\sum_{a=1}^2
|\sigma,a\rangle\langle \sigma,a|.
\label{eq:PDN_def}
\end{equation}

\section{Projected core block}

In the ordered basis
\[
(|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle),
\]
the projected shell Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
P_D^{(N)}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)P_D^{(N)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+^{(N)}(p) & B^{(N)}(p)\\
B^{(N)}(p)^\dagger & E_-^{(N)}(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:Hcore_block}
\end{equation}
where
\[
E_\pm^{(N)}(p),\ B^{(N)}(p)\in\mathrm{Mat}_{2\times2}(\mathbb C).
\]

We now expand around \(p=0\):
\begin{align}
E_\pm^{(N)}(p)
&=
E_\pm^{(N)}(0)
+
p_i\,V_{\pm,i}^{(N)}
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:Epm_expand}
\\
B^{(N)}(p)
&=
M^{(N)}
+
p_i\,\mathcal W_i^{(N)}
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:B_expand}
\end{align}
with
\[
M^{(N)}:=B^{(N)}(0).
\]

\section{Canonical separation of constant and linear pieces}

Subtract the irrelevant common scalar energy
\begin{equation}
E_*^{(N)}
:=
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(0).
\label{eq:Estar_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)-E_*^{(N)}\mathbf 1_4
\]
contains three logically distinct pieces.

\subsection{Constant pair-mixing term}

The constant off-diagonal block \(M^{(N)}\) is the candidate Dirac mass source.
Under the little-group-scalar reduction on the doubled carrier, its symmetry-allowed scalar part is
\begin{equation}
M^{(N)}_{\mathrm{sc}}
=
m_1^{(N)}\,\tau^1\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
m_2^{(N)}\,\tau^2\otimes\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:M_scalar_mass}
\end{equation}
After a constant valley-phase rotation, one may always choose a gauge in which
\begin{equation}
M^{(N)}_{\mathrm{sc}}
=
m^{(N)}\,\tau^1\otimes\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
m^{(N)}:=\sqrt{(m_1^{(N)})^2+(m_2^{(N)})^2}.
\label{eq:M_gaugefixed}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit constant mass parameter is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^{(N)}
=
\left\|
\Pi_{\mathrm{scalar}} B^{(N)}(0)
\right\|.
}
\label{eq:mN_def}
\end{equation}

Hence the massless condition is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^{(N)}=0.
}
\label{eq:massless_condition}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Pair-diagonal linear splitting}

Define
\begin{equation}
\Delta E^{(N)}(p)
:=
\frac12\bigl(E_+^{(N)}(p)-E_-^{(N)}(p)\bigr).
\label{eq:DeltaE_def}
\end{equation}
Its shell-adapted scalar longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel^{(N)}
:=
\frac14
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\bigl(E_+^{(N)}(p)-E_-^{(N)}(p)\bigr)
\right]_{p=0}.
\label{eq:vparallelN_def}
\end{equation}

The minimal Dirac form requires
\begin{equation}
\Delta E^{(N)}(p)
=
v_\parallel^{(N)}p_\parallel\,\mathbf 1_2
+
O(|p|^2),
\qquad
v_\parallel^{(N)}\neq 0.
\label{eq:DeltaE_minimal}
\end{equation}

This contributes the valley-diagonal term
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel^{(N)}p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:longitudinal_term}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Transverse pair-mixing matrices}

Define the two transverse linear matrices
\begin{equation}
W^1_{(N)}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_1}B^{(N)}(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
W^2_{(N)}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_2}B^{(N)}(p)\right|_{p=0}.
\label{eq:Wi_def}
\end{equation}
Only their traceless Hermitian parts carry Dirac data:
\begin{equation}
\widetilde W^\alpha_{(N)}
:=
\frac12\Bigl(W^\alpha_{(N)}+W^\alpha_{(N)\!}^\dagger\Bigr)
-
\frac12\operatorname{tr}
\left[
\frac12\Bigl(W^\alpha_{(N)}+W^\alpha_{(N)\!}^\dagger\Bigr)
\right]\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Wtilde_def}
\end{equation}

Since every traceless Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrix is a Pauli vector,
there exist real coefficients \(w^\alpha_a\) such that
\begin{equation}
\widetilde W^\alpha_{(N)}=w^\alpha_a \sigma_a.
\label{eq:Walpha_Pauli}
\end{equation}

\section{Locked Pauli basis and explicit canonical form}

Choose the internal basis so that the two transverse matrices take the locked form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde W^1_{(N)}
=
\alpha^{(N)}\sigma_1+\beta^{(N)}\sigma_2,
\qquad
\widetilde W^2_{(N)}
=
-\beta^{(N)}\sigma_1+\alpha^{(N)}\sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:locked_W_form}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\{\widetilde W^1_{(N)},\widetilde W^2_{(N)}\}=0,
\qquad
(\widetilde W^1_{(N)})^2=(\widetilde W^2_{(N)})^2
=
\bigl((\alpha^{(N)})^2+(\beta^{(N)})^2\bigr)\mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:W_closure}
\end{equation}

Hence the transverse speed is
\begin{equation}
v_\perp^{(N)}
=
\sqrt{(\alpha^{(N)})^2+(\beta^{(N)})^2}.
\label{eq:vperp_def}
\end{equation}

Substituting everything into \eqref{eq:Hcore_block}, the projected core block becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
E_*^{(N)}(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m^{(N)}\tau^1\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel^{(N)}p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes
\Bigl(
p_1\widetilde W^1_{(N)}
+
p_2\widetilde W^2_{(N)}
\Bigr)
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\label{eq:Hcore_final}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:locked_W_form}, this is
\begin{align}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
&=
E_*^{(N)}(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m^{(N)}\tau^1\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel^{(N)}p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\tau^1\otimes
\Bigl[
(\alpha^{(N)}p_1-\beta^{(N)}p_2)\sigma_1
+
(\beta^{(N)}p_1+\alpha^{(N)}p_2)\sigma_2
\Bigr]
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Hcore_final_expanded}
\end{align}

This is exactly the canonical target form that was missing.

\section{Dirac-carrier conditions in explicit finite form}

The explicit finite conditions are now:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^{(N)}=0,
}
\label{eq:cond_m0}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel^{(N)}\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:cond_vpar}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha^{(N)},\beta^{(N)})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:cond_trans}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde W^1_{(N)},\ \widetilde W^2_{(N)}
\text{ are nonzero, traceless Hermitian, and linearly independent.}
}
\label{eq:cond_W_independent}
\end{equation}

Under these conditions, define
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^1:=\tau^1\otimes \sigma_1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2:=\tau^1\otimes \sigma_2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3:=\tau^3\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Gamma_core}
\end{equation}
Then
\[
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4,
\]
and after a constant transverse rotation the principal symbol is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N),\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
v_\perp^{(N)}p_1'\Gamma^1
+
v_\perp^{(N)}p_2'\Gamma^2
+
v_\parallel^{(N)}p_\parallel\Gamma^3.
\label{eq:Hcore_dirac_principal}
\end{equation}

Thus \(H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)\) is a genuine anisotropic massless Dirac carrier if and only if
\[
m^{(N)}=0,\qquad v_\parallel^{(N)}\neq 0,\qquad v_\perp^{(N)}\neq 0.
\]

\section{What is now closed and what remains open}

What is now explicitly closed is the exact form of the enriched shell basis and the canonical \(4\times4\) core block:
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}=\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle\},
\]
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
E_*^{(N)}\mathbf 1_4
+
m^{(N)}\tau^1\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel^{(N)}p_\parallel\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes(p_1\widetilde W^1_{(N)}+p_2\widetilde W^2_{(N)})
+
O(|p|^2).
\]

What is still not unconditionally closed is the final microscopic evaluation of
\[
m^{(N)},\qquad
v_\parallel^{(N)},\qquad
\alpha^{(N)},\qquad
\beta^{(N)}
\]
from the true refined locked \(+\) Class II Bloch operator of TECT.
That is now a finite symbolic/numerical extraction problem, not a conceptual one.

\section{Final Summary}

The explicit enriched shell Dirac carrier is
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
=
\mathrm{span}\{|+,1\rangle,|+,2\rangle,|-,1\rangle,|-,2\rangle\}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

With
\[
P_D^{(N)}
=
\sum_{\sigma=\pm}\sum_{a=1}^2 |\sigma,a\rangle\langle \sigma,a|,
\]
the core block is
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
P_D^{(N)}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)P_D^{(N)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+^{(N)}(p) & B^{(N)}(p)\\
B^{(N)}(p)^\dagger & E_-^{(N)}(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

After subtracting the common scalar piece and fixing the valley phase,
its canonical form is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
E_*^{(N)}(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m^{(N)}\tau^1\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel^{(N)}p_\parallel\,\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
\tau^1\otimes
\Bigl(
p_1\widetilde W^1_{(N)}+p_2\widetilde W^2_{(N)}
\Bigr)
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\]

In the locked Pauli basis,
\[
\widetilde W^1_{(N)}=\alpha^{(N)}\sigma_1+\beta^{(N)}\sigma_2,
\qquad
\widetilde W^2_{(N)}=-\beta^{(N)}\sigma_1+\alpha^{(N)}\sigma_2,
\]
so that
\[
(\widetilde W^1_{(N)})^2=(\widetilde W^2_{(N)})^2=
\bigl((\alpha^{(N)})^2+(\beta^{(N)})^2\bigr)\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\{\widetilde W^1_{(N)},\widetilde W^2_{(N)}\}=0.
\]

Therefore the explicit Dirac-carrier conditions are
\[
\boxed{
m^{(N)}=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel^{(N)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha^{(N)},\beta^{(N)})\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde W^1_{(N)},\widetilde W^2_{(N)}
\text{ are traceless Hermitian, nonzero, and linearly independent.}
}
\]

Under these conditions, defining
\[
\Gamma^1=\tau^1\otimes\sigma_1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau^1\otimes\sigma_2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau^3\otimes\mathbf 1_2,
\]
one obtains
\[
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4,
\]
and the principal core symbol is the anisotropic massless Dirac operator
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N),\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
v_\perp^{(N)}p_1'\Gamma^1
+
v_\perp^{(N)}p_2'\Gamma^2
+
v_\parallel^{(N)}p_\parallel\Gamma^3,
\qquad
v_\perp^{(N)}=\sqrt{(\alpha^{(N)})^2+(\beta^{(N)})^2}.
\]

Thus the remaining microscopic frontier is no longer the abstract existence of the carrier,
but the finite extraction of
\[
m^{(N)},\quad v_\parallel^{(N)},\quad \alpha^{(N)},\quad \beta^{(N)}
\]
from the refined locked \(+\) Class II Bloch operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Enriched Shell Basis and Canonical Core Extraction}

\section{Goal}

The current frontier is to make the enriched shell Dirac carrier explicit.
The correct task is not to reprove the abstract reduced Dirac theorem, but to:

\begin{enumerate}
\item fix an explicit \(4\)-dimensional enriched shell basis,
\item write the projected block
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p):=P_D^{(N)}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)P_D^{(N)},
\]
\item separate its constant and linear pieces,
\item identify the exact finite conditions for a massless Dirac carrier.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Explicit enriched shell basis}

Fix the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and define the Bragg quasimomentum
\begin{equation}
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\label{eq:kstar_def_core}
\end{equation}

Choose a shell-relevant orthonormal internal doublet
\begin{equation}
\xi_1,\xi_2\in \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\qquad
\xi_a^\dagger \xi_b=\delta_{ab}.
\label{eq:xi_doublet_core}
\end{equation}

In the constant-envelope branch, define
\begin{equation}
u_a(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\qquad a=1,2.
\label{eq:ua_const_core}
\end{equation}

Then the enriched shell-pair basis states are
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:explicit_shell_pair_basis}
\end{equation}

We define the \(4\)-dimensional enriched shell carrier by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
=
\mathrm{span}
\{\Psi_{+,1},\Psi_{+,2},\Psi_{-,1},\Psi_{-,2}\}.
}
\label{eq:HDN_explicit}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
\cong
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}
\otimes
\mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\label{eq:HDN_tensor_form}
\end{equation}

Let
\begin{equation}
P_D^{(N)}
=
\sum_{\sigma=\pm}\sum_{a=1}^2
|\sigma,a\rangle\langle \sigma,a|
\label{eq:PDN_def_core}
\end{equation}
be the orthogonal projector onto this carrier.

\section{Projected core block}

The shell-projected Hamiltonian is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Pi_{S_*}.
\label{eq:HshellN_def_core}
\end{equation}

Its restriction to the enriched carrier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
P_D^{(N)}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)P_D^{(N)}.
}
\label{eq:HcoreN_def_core}
\end{equation}

In the ordered basis
\[
(\Psi_{+,1},\Psi_{+,2},\Psi_{-,1},\Psi_{-,2}),
\]
the core block has the general \(2\times2\) valley-block form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_\pm(p),\,B(p)\in \mathrm{Mat}_{2\times2}(\mathbb C).
\label{eq:Hcore_block_general}
\end{equation}

\section{Constant and linear expansion}

Expand around \(p=0\):
\begin{align}
E_\pm(p)
&=
E_\pm(0)
+
p_i\,\partial_{p_i}E_\pm(0)
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:Epm_expand_core}
\\
B(p)
&=
B(0)
+
p_i\,\partial_{p_i}B(0)
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:B_expand_core}
\end{align}

The common scalar energy is
\begin{equation}
E_*(0):=
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(0).
\label{eq:Estar0_def_core}
\end{equation}

Subtracting the irrelevant common scalar shift, the physically meaningful constant part is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(0)-E_*(0)\mathbf 1_4.
\label{eq:constant_part_core}
\end{equation}

\section{Constant mass classification}

At the doubled shell-block level, the general little-group-scalar constant Hermitian operator is
\begin{equation}
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:K_scalar_space_core}
\end{equation}

Among these, the genuine constant Dirac-mass space is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:mass_space_core}
\end{equation}

Therefore the constant off-diagonal scalar part of \(H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(0)\) is the candidate Dirac mass.

Choose the valley phase so that this constant off-diagonal scalar part is aligned along \(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2\). Then
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(0)-E_*(0)\mathbf 1_4
=
\delta E_0\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
(\text{non-scalar internal part}).
\label{eq:constant_split_core}
\end{equation}

Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(\delta E_0\) is the opposite-valley energy mismatch,
\item \(m\) is the genuine constant Dirac mass.
\end{itemize}

Thus the exact massless condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m=0.
}
\label{eq:massless_condition_core}
\end{equation}

If the residual valley symmetry generated by
\begin{equation}
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\label{eq:QV_core}
\end{equation}
is exact on the isolated doubled shell block, then
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
\label{eq:mass_protect_audit_core}
\end{equation}
so \(m=0\) is symmetry-protected at shell-block level.

\section{Longitudinal linear piece}

The longitudinal Dirac channel comes from the odd valley splitting of the pair-diagonal blocks.
Define
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel
:=
\frac14
\operatorname{Tr}
\left[
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\bigl(E_+(p)-E_-(p)\bigr)
\right]_{p=0}.
\label{eq:vparallel_def_core}
\end{equation}

Then the pair-diagonal linear part is
\begin{equation}
\frac12\bigl(E_+(p)-E_-(p)\bigr)
=
v_\parallel p_\parallel \mathbf 1_2
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:longitudinal_split_core}
\end{equation}
hence contributes
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:longitudinal_tau3_core}
\end{equation}

The nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:vpar_nonzero_core}
\end{equation}

\section{Transverse linear piece}

The transverse Dirac channel comes from the linear off-diagonal block \(B(p)\).
Define
\begin{equation}
W^1:=\frac12\left[
\partial_{p_1}B(0)+\partial_{p_1}B(0)^\dagger
\right]_{\mathrm{trl}},
\qquad
W^2:=\frac12\left[
\partial_{p_2}B(0)+\partial_{p_2}B(0)^\dagger
\right]_{\mathrm{trl}},
\label{eq:W12_def_core}
\end{equation}
where \((\cdot)_{\mathrm{trl}}\) denotes the traceless Hermitian part on the internal \(2\times2\) space.

After a constant valley-phase choice, the off-diagonal linear term can be written canonically as
\begin{equation}
\tau_x\otimes (p_1W^1+p_2W^2).
\label{eq:offdiag_linear_core}
\end{equation}

Thus the full canonical core form becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau_x\otimes(p_1W^1+p_2W^2)
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\label{eq:Hcore_canonical_core}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the canonical target form required by the current program.

\section{Locked Pauli form of the transverse matrices}

Now choose the internal basis so that the transverse matrices are in locked form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^1=\alpha \sigma_1+\beta \sigma_2,
\qquad
W^2=-\beta \sigma_1+\alpha \sigma_2.
}
\label{eq:locked_W_core}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
(W^1)^2=(W^2)^2=(\alpha^2+\beta^2)\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\{W^1,W^2\}=0,
\label{eq:W_relations_core}
\end{equation}
and the transverse speed is
\begin{equation}
v_\perp=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}.
\label{eq:vperp_core}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:locked_W_core} into \eqref{eq:Hcore_canonical_core},
\begin{align}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
&=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\tau_x\otimes
\Bigl[
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\sigma_1
+
(\beta p_1+\alpha p_2)\sigma_2
\Bigr]
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Hcore_locked_full}
\end{align}

\section{Dirac-carrier conditions}

The explicit finite Dirac-carrier conditions are therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
W^1,\ W^2\ \text{traceless Hermitian, nonzero, and linearly independent.}
}
\label{eq:Dirac_conditions_core}
\end{equation}

In the locked basis this is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Dirac_conditions_alpha_beta_core}
\end{equation}

\section{Clifford closure}

Define
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^1=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Gamma_core_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\label{eq:Gamma_core_clifford}
\end{equation}

Hence, after a transverse rotation, the principal symbol of the massless core block is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N),\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
v_\perp p_1'\Gamma^1
+
v_\perp p_2'\Gamma^2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \Gamma^3.
\label{eq:principal_Dirac_core}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit enriched shell carrier is a genuine anisotropic massless Dirac carrier whenever \eqref{eq:Dirac_conditions_alpha_beta_core} holds.

\section{Connection with the finite microscopic carrier audit}

The shell-adapted microscopic seed space is
\begin{equation}
V_{\min}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}.
\label{eq:Vmin_core}
\end{equation}

For any microscopic transport basis \(\{E_A\}\subset V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\), decompose
\begin{equation}
E_A=a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J+R_A,
\qquad
R_A\perp V_{\min}.
\label{eq:EA_seed_decomp_core}
\end{equation}

Then:

\begin{itemize}
\item \(a_A\neq 0\) feeds the longitudinal coefficient \(v_\parallel\),
\item \((b_A,c_A)\neq (0,0)\) feeds the transverse matrices \(W^1,W^2\).
\end{itemize}

Hence the microscopic completion criterion is exactly the finite audit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:finite_audit_completion_core}
\end{equation}

Thus the explicit \(4\)-dimensional shell basis and the finite basis-overlap audit fit together perfectly:
the former gives the carrier, the latter tells us whether the actual microscopic linearization populates it nontrivially.

\section{Final Summary}

The enriched shell Dirac carrier can be fixed explicitly as
\[
\mathcal H_D^{(N)}
=
\mathrm{span}
\{\Psi_{+,1},\Psi_{+,2},\Psi_{-,1},\Psi_{-,2}\},
\qquad
\Psi_{\pm,a}(x)=e^{\pm ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\]

In the ordered basis
\[
(\Psi_{+,1},\Psi_{+,2},\Psi_{-,1},\Psi_{-,2}),
\]
the projected enriched shell core is
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with \(2\times2\) internal blocks.

Its canonical expansion is
\[
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
\tau_x\otimes(p_1W^1+p_2W^2)
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\]

The exact finite Dirac-carrier conditions are
\[
\boxed{
m=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
W^1,\ W^2\ \text{traceless Hermitian, nonzero, and linearly independent.}
}
\]

Choosing the internal basis in locked Pauli form,
\[
W^1=\alpha \sigma_1+\beta \sigma_2,
\qquad
W^2=-\beta \sigma_1+\alpha \sigma_2,
\]
one obtains
\[
v_\perp=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2},
\]
and the principal core symbol becomes
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N),\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
v_\perp p_1'\Gamma^1
+
v_\perp p_2'\Gamma^2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \Gamma^3,
\]
where
\[
\Gamma^1=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\]

Therefore the enriched shell carrier is a genuine anisotropic massless Dirac carrier if and only if
\[
\boxed{
m=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

At the microscopic finite-audit level, the completion criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0),
}
\]
where
\[
E_A=a_A B_\parallel+b_A B_I+c_A B_J+R_A,
\qquad
R_A\perp \mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}.
\]

Thus the remaining frontier is no longer conceptual:
it is the explicit extraction of
\[
m,\qquad v_\parallel,\qquad W^1,\qquad W^2
\]
from the refined locked \(+\) Class II microscopic Bloch operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Explicit Extraction of \(m\), \(v_\parallel\), \(W^1\), and \(W^2\) from the Refined Locked \(+\) Class II Branch}

\section{Starting point}

We start from the refined locked microscopic branch with one heavy Class II mediator:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k),
\qquad
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X.
\label{eq:Heff_start_extract}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac{1}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger.
\label{eq:Heff_schur_extract}
\end{equation}

Fix the selected shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and set
\begin{equation}
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\label{eq:kstar_extract}
\end{equation}

Choose the enriched shell basis
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
a=1,2.
\label{eq:enriched_shell_basis_extract}
\end{equation}

Then the shell-projected operator is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Pi_{S_*},
\label{eq:Hshell_extract}
\end{equation}
and the enriched core block is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
P_D^{(N)}H_{\mathrm{shell}}^{(N)}(p)P_D^{(N)}.
\label{eq:Hcore_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{Valley-block matrix elements}

In the ordered basis
\[
(\Psi_{+,1},\Psi_{+,2},\Psi_{-,1},\Psi_{-,2}),
\]
the projected core block has the form
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
E_\pm(p),\,B(p)\in \mathrm{Mat}_{2\times2}(\mathbb C),
\label{eq:Hcore_blocks_extract}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{align}
(E_+(p))_{ab}
&=
\langle \Psi_{+,a}, H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Psi_{+,b}\rangle,
\label{eq:Eplus_def_extract}
\\
(E_-(p))_{ab}
&=
\langle \Psi_{-,a}, H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Psi_{-,b}\rangle,
\label{eq:Eminus_def_extract}
\\
B_{ab}(p)
&=
\langle \Psi_{+,a}, H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\Psi_{-,b}\rangle.
\label{eq:B_def_extract}
\end{align}

Thus the complete microscopic extraction problem reduces to computing these finite matrix elements.

\section{Constant and linear decomposition}

Expand around \(p=0\):
\begin{align}
E_\pm(p)
&=
E_\pm(0)
+
p_i\,V_{\pm,i}
+
O(|p|^2),
\label{eq:Epm_expand_extract}
\\
B(p)
&=
B(0)
+
p_i\,\mathcal W_i
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:B_expand_extract}
\end{align}

We write the common scalar part as
\begin{equation}
E_*(p)=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p).
\label{eq:Estar_extract}
\end{equation}

Then three quantities control the Dirac carrier:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the constant pair-off-diagonal block \(B(0)\);
\item the odd pair-diagonal linear splitting \(E_+(p)-E_-(p)\);
\item the linear pair-off-diagonal matrices \(\mathcal W_1,\mathcal W_2\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Constant mass extraction}

The constant Dirac mass is the little-group-scalar part of \(B(0)\).
At the doubled block level, the genuine constant Dirac mass space is
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes\mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes\mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
\label{eq:mass_space_extract}
\end{equation}

Therefore the scalar constant pair-mixing amplitude is
\begin{equation}
M_0:=\frac12\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}} B(0),
\label{eq:M0_trace_extract}
\end{equation}
and after a constant valley-phase choice the mass term is
\begin{equation}
m\,\tau_x\otimes\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
m=|M_0|.
\label{eq:m_from_M0_extract}
\end{equation}

In the constant-envelope shell basis,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_0
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
}
\label{eq:M0_Fourier_extract}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m=0
\iff
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)=0.
}
\label{eq:m0_Uhat_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{Longitudinal slope extraction}

Define the shell-adapted longitudinal direction
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\qquad
p_\parallel=\hat n\cdot p.
\]

The longitudinal pair splitting is
\begin{equation}
\Delta E(p):=\frac12\bigl(E_+(p)-E_-(p)\bigr).
\label{eq:DeltaE_extract}
\end{equation}

Its scalar shell-relevant coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac14
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\bigl(E_+(p)-E_-(p)\bigr)
\right]_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:vpar_matrix_extract}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
E_+(p)-E_-(p)
=
2v_\parallel p_\parallel \mathbf 1_2
+
O(|p|^2)
\label{eq:Epm_split_vpar_extract}
\end{equation}
is the exact shell-level longitudinal criterion.

For the refined working branch, the total longitudinal slope decomposes as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\label{eq:vpar_decomp_extract}
\end{equation}

Thus the longitudinal carrier condition is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
v_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:vpar_nonzero_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{Transverse matrix extraction}

Fix a shell-adapted orthonormal frame
\[
(e_1,e_2,\hat n).
\]
Define the two transverse momentum coordinates
\[
p_1=e_1\cdot p,
\qquad
p_2=e_2\cdot p.
\]

The transverse Dirac matrices are the traceless Hermitian parts of
\begin{equation}
\mathcal W_1=\left.\partial_{p_1}B(p)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\mathcal W_2=\left.\partial_{p_2}B(p)\right|_{p=0}.
\label{eq:Wraw_extract}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^1=
\left[\frac12\bigl(\mathcal W_1+\mathcal W_1^\dagger\bigr)\right]_{\mathrm{trl}},
\qquad
W^2=
\left[\frac12\bigl(\mathcal W_2+\mathcal W_2^\dagger\bigr)\right]_{\mathrm{trl}}.
}
\label{eq:W12_from_derivative_extract}
\end{equation}

In the constant-envelope reduction, these are controlled by first-shell Fourier coefficients:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^\alpha
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:Walpha_Fourier_extract}
\end{equation}

Moreover, the effective transverse coefficients split into explicit microscopic sources:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
W^\alpha
=
\Bigl[
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*)
\Bigr]s^\alpha.
}
\label{eq:Walpha_decomp_extract}
\end{equation}

Hence the transverse nondegeneracy condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Talpha_nonzero_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{Locked Pauli form and \((\alpha,\beta)\) extraction}

Because \(W^1,W^2\) are traceless Hermitian \(2\times2\) matrices, one may choose the internal basis so that
\begin{equation}
W^1=\alpha \sigma_1+\beta \sigma_2,
\qquad
W^2=-\beta \sigma_1+\alpha \sigma_2.
\label{eq:locked_form_extract}
\end{equation}

Then the coefficients are read off exactly by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}\bigl(\sigma_1W^1+\sigma_2W^2\bigr),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}\bigl(\sigma_2W^1-\sigma_1W^2\bigr).
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_trace_extract}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the shell-seed dictionary,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_I I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_J I_\theta.
\label{eq:seed_to_ab_extract}
\end{equation}

Hence, since \(I_\theta\neq 0\) and \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\), the finite basis audit
\[
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0,
\qquad
\exists B:\ (b_B,c_B)\neq (0,0)
\]
is equivalent to
\[
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
\]

\section{Canonical core Hamiltonian}

Combining the previous steps, the explicit enriched shell core becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau_x\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_z\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
\tau_x\otimes(p_1W^1+p_2W^2)
+
O(|p|^2).
}
\label{eq:Hcore_canonical_extract}
\end{equation}

In the locked basis \eqref{eq:locked_form_extract},
\begin{align}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
&=
E_*(p)\mathbf 1_4
+
m\,\tau_x\otimes\mathbf 1_2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel\,\tau_z\otimes\mathbf 1_2
\nonumber\\
&\quad
+
\tau_x\otimes
\Bigl[
(\alpha p_1-\beta p_2)\sigma_1
+
(\beta p_1+\alpha p_2)\sigma_2
\Bigr]
+
O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:Hcore_locked_extract}
\end{align}

Define
\begin{equation}
\Gamma^1=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_1,
\qquad
\Gamma^2=\tau_x\otimes \sigma_2,
\qquad
\Gamma^3=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:Gamma_extract}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\{\Gamma^i,\Gamma^j\}=2\delta^{ij}\mathbf 1_4.
\label{eq:Clifford_extract}
\end{equation}

Hence the massless principal symbol is
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{\mathrm{pr}}(p)
=
v_\perp p_1' \Gamma^1
+
v_\perp p_2' \Gamma^2
+
v_\parallel p_\parallel \Gamma^3,
\qquad
v_\perp=\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}.
\label{eq:principal_Dirac_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{Final finite extraction dictionary}

The complete refined locked \(+\) Class II extraction problem is therefore reduced to the finite computation of the following four objects:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel.
}
\label{eq:final_four_extract}
\end{equation}

Equivalently:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m\ \Longleftrightarrow\ \widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
W^\alpha\ \Longleftrightarrow\ \widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel\ \Longleftrightarrow\ \partial_{p_\parallel}(E_+-E_-)|_{0}.
}
\label{eq:equiv_extract_dict}
\end{equation}

Thus the explicit massless Dirac-carrier conditions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:final_Dirac_test_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

Fix the enriched shell basis
\[
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,a}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_a(x),
\qquad
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\]

The shell core block is
\[
H_{\mathrm{core}}^{(N)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
E_+(p) & B(p)\\
B(p)^\dagger & E_-(p)
\end{pmatrix}.
\]

The exact extraction rules are:

\[
\boxed{
m
=
\left|
\frac12\operatorname{tr}_{\mathrm{int}} B(0)
\right|,
\qquad
B(0)=\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
m=0
\iff
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)=0.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
\frac14
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathrm{int}}
\left[
\partial_{p_\parallel}
\bigl(E_+(p)-E_-(p)\bigr)
\right]_{p=0},
}
\]
with
\[
\boxed{
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
W^\alpha
=
\left[
\frac12
\left(
\partial_{p_\alpha}B(0)+\partial_{p_\alpha}B(0)^\dagger
\right)
\right]_{\mathrm{trl}}
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\]

Choosing the internal basis in locked Pauli form,
\[
W^1=\alpha \sigma_1+\beta \sigma_2,
\qquad
W^2=-\beta \sigma_1+\alpha \sigma_2,
\]
the explicit coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}\bigl(\sigma_1W^1+\sigma_2W^2\bigr),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}\bigl(\sigma_2W^1-\sigma_1W^2\bigr).
}
\]

Therefore the refined locked \(+\) Class II branch gives a massless shell Dirac carrier if and only if
\[
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)=0,
\qquad
v_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\neq 0.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
m=0,
\qquad
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Thus the remaining microscopic frontier is the finite evaluation of
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^1_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
\widehat T^2_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*),\qquad
v_\parallel
\]
for the actual refined locked TECT Bloch operator.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Term-by-term Role of the Refined Locked \(+\) Class II Branch}

\section{Goal}

The remaining shell-side microscopic problem is to separate the refined locked \(+\) Class II contribution into:

\begin{equation}
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*),
\qquad
\widehat T^1_{(II)}(G_*),
\qquad
\widehat T^2_{(II)}(G_*),
\qquad
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}.
\end{equation}

These govern, respectively:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the scalar intervalley Bragg block,
\item the first transverse Dirac matrix,
\item the second transverse Dirac matrix,
\item the longitudinal shell slope.
\end{enumerate}

The key point is that these four quantities do \emph{not} play symmetric roles.

\section{1. Schur-complement decomposition of the Class II correction}

Start from the refined locked branch with one heavy auxiliary Class II field:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k),
\qquad
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X.
\end{equation}

Using
\begin{equation}
H_{\Psi X}(k)=\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k),
\end{equation}
one gets
\begin{align}
\Delta_X(k)
&:=
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k)
\\
&=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger
\\
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal J\mathcal J^\dagger
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,(\mathcal J\mathcal K^\dagger+\mathcal K\mathcal J^\dagger)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\mathcal K\mathcal K^\dagger.
\label{eq:DeltaX_JJJKKK}
\end{align}

Therefore the Class II shell correction naturally decomposes into
\[
JJ,\qquad JK,\qquad KK
\]
sectors.

\section{2. Fourier-shell decomposition at \(Q=G_*\)}

At the folded Bragg point
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
the shell-relevant constant-envelope extraction is controlled by the \(Q=G_*\) primitive-cell Fourier coefficient.

Thus the total effective shell data are
\begin{equation}
M_0
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
W^\alpha
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\qquad
\alpha=1,2,
\end{equation}
together with
\begin{equation}
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\end{equation}

The exact split is
\begin{equation}
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat U_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*),
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{bare}}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
+
\widehat T^\alpha_{(\mathrm{sp})}(G_*),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
\end{equation}

So the Class II problem is to identify the \(Q=G_*\) identity and traceless Pauli parts of \(\Delta_X\).

\section{3. Formal shell projections of the Class II block}

Let \((\cdot)_{\mathbf 1}\) denote the internal identity part and \((\cdot)_{\alpha}\) the \(s^\alpha\) coefficient.
Then formally:
\begin{equation}
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\left[
\widehat{\Delta_X}(G_*)
\right]_{\mathbf 1},
\label{eq:Uii_formal}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
\left[
\widehat{\Delta_X}(G_*)
\right]_{\alpha},
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
\label{eq:Tii_formal}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:DeltaX_JJJKKK}, this gives
\begin{align}
\widehat U_{(II)}(G_*)
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left[\widehat{\mathcal J\mathcal J^\dagger}(G_*)\right]_{\mathbf 1}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\left[\widehat{\mathcal J\mathcal K^\dagger+\mathcal K\mathcal J^\dagger}(G_*)\right]_{\mathbf 1}
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left[\widehat{\mathcal K\mathcal K^\dagger}(G_*)\right]_{\mathbf 1},
\label{eq:Uii_split}
\end{align}
and
\begin{align}
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
&=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left[\widehat{\mathcal J\mathcal J^\dagger}(G_*)\right]_{\alpha}
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\left[\widehat{\mathcal J\mathcal K^\dagger+\mathcal K\mathcal J^\dagger}(G_*)\right]_{\alpha}
\nonumber\\
&\qquad
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}
\left[\widehat{\mathcal K\mathcal K^\dagger}(G_*)\right]_{\alpha}.
\label{eq:Tii_split}
\end{align}

So, in complete generality, both \(JK\) and \(KK\) can contribute to the traceless transverse sector, while the scalar identity part controls the Bragg mass.

\section{4. Explicit transverse Class II overlap}

Inside the folded-Bragg Class II audit isolated in the notes, the transverse coefficient compresses to the shell convolution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
}
\label{eq:Talpha_explicit}
\end{equation}

If the shell-relevant \(K\)-coefficient is zero-mode dominated, then
\begin{equation}
\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q')
\approx
\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(0)\,\delta_{Q',0},
\end{equation}
and \eqref{eq:Talpha_explicit} reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\approx
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A iG_{*i}A_{G_*}\,j^A\,\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(0).
}
\label{eq:Talpha_zero_mode}
\end{equation}

Hence the canonical first-shell form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
iA_{G_*}(C_\alpha\!\cdot\! G_*),
}
\label{eq:Talpha_canonical}
\end{equation}
for an effective microscopic vector \(C_\alpha\).

Therefore the transverse witness is structurally natural:
\begin{equation}
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
A_{G_*}\neq 0,\ \ C_\alpha\!\cdot\! G_*\neq 0
\quad
\text{modulo accidental cancellations.}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Explicit longitudinal Class II coefficient}

The longitudinal coefficient remains separate from the transverse shell Fourier overlaps.
At the reduced level,
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
\label{eq:seed_dictionary}
\end{equation}

In the explicit local Class II-compatible branch, one has
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so the active longitudinal route is the primitive Branch-B one:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_branchB}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the pure Class II working truncation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}(p)
=
\frac{\nu_\parallel\Gamma c_\parallel}{2}\,I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\nu_\perp\Gamma I_\theta
\Big[
c_I(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
c_J(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2)
\Big].
}
\label{eq:A1_pure_classII_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the explicit Class II contribution to the shell slope is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac{\nu_\parallel\Gamma c_\parallel}{2}\,I_{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:dvpar_classII}
\end{equation}
while the transverse reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha^{(II)}=\nu_\perp\Gamma c_I I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta^{(II)}=\nu_\perp\Gamma c_J I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:ab_classII}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Why Class II does not solve the scalar Bragg-mass problem}

Now the crucial asymmetry appears.

A naive scalar periodic-core contribution such as
\[
U_{\mathrm{quad}}(x)=u_2\phi_0(x)^2
\]
gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat U_{\mathrm{quad}}(G_*)=4u_2A^2,
\qquad
M_0^{\mathrm{quad}}=4u_2A^2\,\mathbf 1_2\neq 0
}
\label{eq:Uquad_nonzero}
\end{equation}
in the equal-amplitude 12-mode branch.

By contrast, every Class II contribution carries an explicit internal Pauli generator.
Hence its constant pair-mixing block lies in
\[
\tau_1\otimes s_a
\quad\text{or}\quad
\tau_2\otimes s_a,
\]
not in the scalar identity channel
\[
\tau_1\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]
Since identity and traceless Pauli channels are orthogonal, the Class II sector cannot directly cancel the scalar Bragg block.

Moreover, in the natural odd/reflection parity of the shell-Dirac construction, the constant gradient-sector pair mixing vanishes at principal order:
\[
\delta B_0^{\mathrm{Class\,II}}=0.
\]

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II renormalizes the derivative witness sector }(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
\text{ but does not remove the scalar identity-channel obstruction }M_0.
}
\label{eq:key_asymmetry}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Route selection}

Because of \eqref{eq:key_asymmetry}, the plain shell-pair route has only two logically distinct exits:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(i) identity-channel cancellation,}
\qquad
\text{(ii) graded }2+2\text{ bypass.}
}
\label{eq:two_routes}
\end{equation}

The exact scalar cancellation law is
\begin{equation}
2A^2\bigl(2c_0+q_*^2c_1+2q_*^2c_2\bigr)
-
\sum_{\eta,\zeta\in S_{\mathrm{bi}}}
\widehat V(\eta)(R_0)_{\eta\zeta}\overline{\widehat V(\zeta+G_*)}
=0.
\label{eq:identity_cancellation_law}
\end{equation}

If one does not want to rely on this cancellation, the correct mainline is the graded \(2+2\) infrared route, where the principal operator is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_1(p)=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & A_1(p)\\
A_1(p)^\dagger & 0
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
D_1(0)=0,
}
\label{eq:graded_bypass_mainline}
\end{equation}
so the scalar Bragg block is bypassed rather than cancelled.

\section{8. Final strategic conclusion}

At the strongest honest current stage:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the explicit Class II branch already supplies
\[
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)},\qquad
\alpha^{(II)},\qquad
\beta^{(II)};
\]

\item the transverse shell witness is structurally natural and reduced to finite shell convolutions;

\item the longitudinal primitive Branch-B carrier is explicitly available;

\item the true bottleneck of the plain shell route is not the witness sector but the scalar Bragg mass
\[
M_0=\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*);
\]

\item therefore the strongest current mainline is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{use Class II to extract the coefficient point }
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
\text{ but use graded }2+2\text{ for the robust massless Dirac route.}
}
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The refined locked \(+\) Class II correction is
\[
\Delta_X(k)
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger,
\]
hence it decomposes into
\[
JJ,\qquad JK,\qquad KK
\]
channels.

At the folded Bragg shell \(Q=G_*\), the shell data are
\[
M_0
=
\widehat U_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,\mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
W^\alpha
=
\widehat T^\alpha_{\mathrm{eff}}(G_*)\,s^\alpha,
\qquad
v_\parallel
=
v_\parallel^{\mathrm{bare}}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}
+
\delta v_\parallel^{(\mathrm{sp})}.
\]

The explicit Class II transverse overlap is
\[
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
}
\]
In the minimal first-shell channel this reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
iA_{G_*}(C_\alpha\!\cdot\! G_*),
}
\]
so the transverse witness is structurally natural.

The explicit longitudinal Class II contribution is
\[
\boxed{
\delta v_\parallel^{(II)}
=
\frac{\nu_\parallel\Gamma c_\parallel}{2}\,I_{\theta'^3},
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
\alpha^{(II)}=\nu_\perp\Gamma c_I I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta^{(II)}=\nu_\perp\Gamma c_J I_\theta.
}
\]

Thus Class II genuinely supplies the derivative witness sector
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

However, the scalar Bragg mass behaves differently.
A naive scalar periodic core gives
\[
\widehat U_{\mathrm{quad}}(G_*)=4u_2A^2,
\qquad
M_0^{\mathrm{quad}}=4u_2A^2\,\mathbf 1_2\neq 0.
\]
Moreover, the Class II constant block lies in the traceless internal Pauli channel and is orthogonal to the scalar identity channel.
Hence:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Class II renormalizes the derivative witness sector, but does not remove the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction }M_0.
}
\]

Therefore the plain shell-pair route has only two exits:
\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) identity-channel cancellation,}
\qquad
\text{(ii) graded }2+2\text{ bypass.}
}
\]

The strongest honest strategic conclusion is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{use the refined locked \(+\) Class II branch to extract }
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta),
\text{ but use the graded }2+2\text{ route as the robust massless Dirac mainline.}
}
\]

\section{Exact Three-Direction Projection of the Intervalley Class-II Tensor}

\section{Starting point}

The shell-pair intervalley channel is controlled by the single harmonic \(Q=G_*\).
At the current refined locked \(+\) Class II stage, the surviving microscopic tensor is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
}
\label{eq:Cvalley_start}
\end{equation}

This is the unique object to be projected onto the three shell-adapted Dirac witness channels.

\section{Shell-adapted frame and projector tensors}

Fix the adapted shell frame
\[
(\hat n,e_1,e_2),
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and the tangent-doublet Pauli basis
\[
(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3).
\]

Define the three projector tensors
\begin{equation}
P^{(\parallel)\,i,r}{}_{a}
:=
\mathcal N_\parallel\,\hat n^i(\Sigma_3)^r{}_{a},
\label{eq:Ppar_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
P^{(E)\,i,r}{}_{a}
:=
\mathcal N_E\,
\frac12
\left[
e_1^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_{a}
+
e_2^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_{a}
\right],
\label{eq:PE_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
P^{(O)\,i,r}{}_{a}
:=
\mathcal N_O\,
\frac12
\left[
-\,e_2^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_{a}
+
e_1^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_{a}
\right].
\label{eq:PO_def}
\end{equation}

Here \(\mathcal N_\parallel,\mathcal N_E,\mathcal N_O\) are fixed normalization constants.

\section{Exact coefficient extraction}

The three seed coefficients are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
P^{(\parallel)\,i,r}{}_{a}\,
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
}
\label{eq:cpar_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
=
P^{(E)\,i,r}{}_{a}\,
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
}
\label{eq:cE_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
=
P^{(O)\,i,r}{}_{a}\,
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
}
\label{eq:cO_exact}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Cvalley_start}, one gets the exact linear decomposition
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
\alpha_X c_\parallel^{(J)}
+
\beta_X c_\parallel^{(K)},
}
\label{eq:cpar_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
=
\alpha_X c_E^{(J)}
+
\beta_X c_E^{(K)},
}
\label{eq:cE_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
=
\alpha_X c_O^{(J)}
+
\beta_X c_O^{(K)},
}
\label{eq:cO_split}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{align}
c_\parallel^{(J)}
&:=
P^{(\parallel)\,i,r}{}_{a}\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
&
c_\parallel^{(K)}
&:=
P^{(\parallel)\,i,r}{}_{a}\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
\label{eq:cparJK_def}
\\
c_E^{(J)}
&:=
P^{(E)\,i,r}{}_{a}\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
&
c_E^{(K)}
&:=
P^{(E)\,i,r}{}_{a}\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
\label{eq:cEJK_def}
\\
c_O^{(J)}
&:=
P^{(O)\,i,r}{}_{a}\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0),
&
c_O^{(K)}
&:=
P^{(O)\,i,r}{}_{a}\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\label{eq:cOJK_def}
\end{align}

Thus the coefficient extraction problem is reduced to six finite tensor contractions.

\section{Current explicit leading branch input}

At the current explicit leading local level, the \(K\)-sector intervalley tensor has the shell-adapted form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,k^{a}(\theta_*)
\Big[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}(\Sigma_1)_r
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}(\Sigma_2)_r
\Big]
+
\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
}
\label{eq:K_leading_explicit}
\end{equation}
with no leading longitudinal component:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0.
}
\label{eq:K_no_long}
\end{equation}

Moreover, the pure \(J\)-sector is axial-only at the shell-adapted local level, so it does not supply transverse witnesses:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E^{(J)}=0,
\qquad
c_O^{(J)}=0.
}
\label{eq:J_no_trans}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact split \eqref{eq:cpar_split}--\eqref{eq:cO_split} reduces at current explicit leading order to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
\alpha_X\,c_\parallel^{(J)},
}
\label{eq:cpar_leading}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
=
\beta_X\,c_E^{(K)},
\qquad
c_O
=
\beta_X\,c_O^{(K)}.
}
\label{eq:cEO_leading}
\end{equation}

Thus the primitive longitudinal carrier and the transverse carrier are separated already at the level of explicit shell projectors.

\section{Reduced Dirac dictionary}

Once \((c_\parallel,c_E,c_O)\) are known, the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:reduced_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12
\bigl(
\alpha_X c_\parallel^{(J)}
+
\beta_X c_\parallel^{(K)}
\bigr)
I_{\theta'^3},
}
\label{eq:lambda_split}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\bigl(
\alpha_X c_E^{(J)}
+
\beta_X c_E^{(K)}
\bigr)I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta
=
\bigl(
\alpha_X c_O^{(J)}
+
\beta_X c_O^{(K)}
\bigr)I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:alphabeta_split}
\end{equation}

Under the current explicit leading branch input,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 \alpha_X c_\parallel^{(J)} I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha
=
\beta_X c_E^{(K)} I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta
=
\beta_X c_O^{(K)} I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:leading_reduced_split}
\end{equation}

\section{Immediate yes/no criterion}

Therefore the shell-level nondegeneracy test is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:seed_nondeg_test}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the present branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(J)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E^{(K)},c_O^{(K)})\neq (0,0),
}
\label{eq:branch_yesno_test}
\end{equation}
up to accidental cancellations and higher-order corrections.

\section{Honest caveat: why this is not yet the final unconditional transverse closure}

The projector algebra above is exact.
However, the current explicit leading transverse bookkeeping should still be described honestly.

A naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear vanishes because
\[
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}=0,
\qquad
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\]
Therefore the genuine microscopic transverse frontier is not a naive undifferentiated local \(JK\) term, but the derivative-resolved shell audit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:derivative_resolved_frontier}
\end{equation}

Hence \eqref{eq:cEO_leading} should be read as the strongest current explicit branch-level extraction structure, not yet as the unconditional final closure of the full microscopic TECT PDE.

\section{Connection to the Bloch calibration}

The transport coefficients \((c_\parallel,c_E,c_O)\) feed the reduced coefficients \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\), while the shell-core Bloch block yields the overlap-normalized coefficients \((C_\parallel,C_E,C_O)\).
The final microscopic viability test remains
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:Bloch_calibration_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the present tensor-contraction step is the correct transport-side half of the final Bloch calibration.

\section{Final Summary}

The intervalley shell-pair tensor is
\[
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\]

Its three exact shell-adapted projections are
\[
c_\parallel
=
\mathcal N_\parallel \hat n^i(\Sigma_3)^r{}_a\,\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a},
\]
\[
c_E
=
\mathcal N_E\frac12
\bigl[e_1^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_a+e_2^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_a\bigr]\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a},
\]
\[
c_O
=
\mathcal N_O\frac12
\bigl[-e_2^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_a+e_1^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_a\bigr]\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}.
\]

Therefore
\[
c_\parallel=\alpha_X c_\parallel^{(J)}+\beta_X c_\parallel^{(K)},
\qquad
c_E=\alpha_X c_E^{(J)}+\beta_X c_E^{(K)},
\qquad
c_O=\alpha_X c_O^{(J)}+\beta_X c_O^{(K)}.
\]

At the current explicit leading branch level,
\[
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
c_E^{(J)}=0,
\qquad
c_O^{(J)}=0.
\]
Hence the leading bookkeeping reduces to
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel=\alpha_X c_\parallel^{(J)},
\qquad
c_E=\beta_X c_E^{(K)},
\qquad
c_O=\beta_X c_O^{(K)}.
}
\]

The reduced Dirac coefficients are then
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\]

So the present explicit branch-level nondegeneracy test is
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(J)}\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E^{(K)},c_O^{(K)})\neq (0,0),
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

However, this should still be stated honestly:
the exact projector algebra is closed, but the genuine microscopic transverse frontier is not a naive local \(JK\) bilinear.
It is the derivative-resolved shell audit
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}.
}
\]

Thus the current result is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the exact tensor-extraction formulas are closed,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the leading branch-level coefficient split is explicit,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the final unconditional microscopic transverse closure still requires the derivative-resolved Bloch audit.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Branch-Level Explicit Closed Form for \texorpdfstring{$c_\parallel,c_E,c_O$}{c_parallel,cE,cO}}

\section{Starting point}

At the current refined locked \(+\) Class II stage, the pre-Schur intervalley tensor is
\begin{equation}
\mathsf C_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\alpha_X\,\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
+
\beta_X\,\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0).
\label{eq:C_preSchur}
\end{equation}

However, the actual shell witness coefficients are not extracted directly from
\eqref{eq:C_preSchur}.
They are extracted from the Schur-complement correction
\begin{equation}
\Delta_X
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)^\dagger.
\label{eq:Schur_basic_closed}
\end{equation}

Therefore the physical witness channels decompose into
\begin{equation}
JJ,\qquad JK,\qquad KK,
\label{eq:JJJKKK_split_closed}
\end{equation}
and their leading shell roles are different.

\section{Shell-adapted leading ansatz}

Fix the shell frame
\[
(\hat n,e_1,e_2),
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and the tangent Pauli basis
\[
(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2,\Sigma_3).
\]

The current explicit leading shell-adapted branch ansatz is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,j^a\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{a}
+
\mathsf J^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
}
\label{eq:J_leading_closed}
\end{equation}
where the null part is orthogonal to the three shell witness projectors.

Likewise,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,k^a
\Big[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}(\Sigma_1)_r{}^{a}
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}(\Sigma_2)_r{}^{a}
\Big]
+
\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a}.
}
\label{eq:K_leading_closed}
\end{equation}

Thus, at leading shell level, \(J\) is purely longitudinal and \(K\) is purely transverse.

\section{Projector definitions}

Define the exact shell-adapted witness projectors
\begin{equation}
P^{(\parallel)\,i,r}{}_{a}
=
\mathcal N_\parallel \hat n^i(\Sigma_3)^r{}_{a},
\label{eq:Ppar_closed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
P^{(E)\,i,r}{}_{a}
=
\mathcal N_E\frac12
\Big[
e_1^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_{a}
+
e_2^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_{a}
\Big],
\label{eq:PE_closed}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
P^{(O)\,i,r}{}_{a}
=
\mathcal N_O\frac12
\Big[
-\,e_2^i(\Sigma_1)^r{}_{a}
+
e_1^i(\Sigma_2)^r{}_{a}
\Big].
\label{eq:PO_closed}
\end{equation}

At the pre-Schur level these define
\[
c_\parallel^{\mathrm{pre}},
\qquad
c_E^{\mathrm{pre}},
\qquad
c_O^{\mathrm{pre}}.
\]
But the physical shell-core coefficients must be computed from \(\Delta_X\), not directly from \(\mathsf C\).

\section{Longitudinal coefficient from the \(JJ\) channel}

Because \(K\) is transverse-only at leading shell order, the longitudinal coefficient comes from the \(JJ\) channel.
Substituting \eqref{eq:J_leading_closed} into \eqref{eq:Schur_basic_closed}, the longitudinal shell scalar is proportional to
\[
\hat n^i(\Sigma_3)^r{}_{a}
\,
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}
\,
\hat n^j(\Sigma_3)^s{}_{b}
\,
\mathsf J_{j,s}^{b}
\sim j^a j^a=j^2.
\]
After normalization, we obtain
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,j^2.
}
\label{eq:cpar_closed_final}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the Branch-B longitudinal coefficient.
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,j^2.
}
\label{eq:lambdac_closed_final}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced longitudinal witness is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\,\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,j^2.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_closed_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Transverse coefficients from the \(JK\) channel}

Now consider the leading transverse part.
Because pure \(J\) is axial-only and pure \(K\) is transverse, the first nontrivial transverse witness comes from the mixed \(JK\) channel.

Substituting \eqref{eq:J_leading_closed} and \eqref{eq:K_leading_closed} into the mixed part of \eqref{eq:Schur_basic_closed}, one gets a shell contraction proportional to
\[
j^a k^a = j\!\cdot\! k.
\]
The even transverse piece carries \(\Lambda_E^{(0)}\), and the odd one carries \(\Lambda_O^{(0)}\).

Therefore the exact leading branch-level coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(j\!\cdot\!k)\,
\Lambda_E^{(0)},
}
\label{eq:cE_closed_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
=
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(j\!\cdot\!k)\,
\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:cO_closed_final}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced transverse witnesses are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
I_\theta\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(j\!\cdot\!k)\,
\Lambda_E^{(0)},
}
\label{eq:alpha_closed_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
I_\theta\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
(j\!\cdot\!k)\,
\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:beta_closed_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Complete coefficient point}

Collecting the results,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
c_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
c_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:full_cpoint_closed}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
\alpha
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:full_witness_point_closed}
\end{equation}

This is the explicit branch-level closed form of the current refined locked \(+\) Class II realization.

\section{Immediate nondegeneracy test}

The shell witness nondegeneracy conditions become
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
j^2\neq 0,
\qquad
(j\!\cdot\!k)\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)})\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:branch_nondeg_closed}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:witness_nondeg_closed}
\end{equation}

\section{Anisotropy ratio}

The leading anisotropy ratio is
\begin{equation}
\rho
=
\frac{|\lambda_\parallel|}{\sqrt{\alpha^2+\beta^2}}
=
\frac12
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta}
\frac{j^2}{|j\!\cdot\!k|}
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
\label{eq:rho_closed_final}
\end{equation}

Using the explicit overlap ratio
\[
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta}
=
\frac{3}{16}\theta_0^2\kappa^2,
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{3}{32}
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{j^2}{|j\!\cdot\!k|}
\frac{\theta_0^2\kappa^2}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
}
\label{eq:rho_final_explicit}
\end{equation}
In particular, \(\rho\) is independent of the heavy mediator mass \(M_X\).

\section{Honest status}

The formulas \eqref{eq:full_cpoint_closed}--\eqref{eq:rho_final_explicit} are the strongest current explicit leading closed form of the refined locked \(+\) Class II branch.

However, they should still be stated honestly:

\begin{enumerate}
\item they are branch-level explicit closure, not yet the unconditional final closure of the full microscopic TECT PDE;
\item the exact projector algebra is closed, but the full microscopic transverse frontier is still the derivative-resolved shell audit of the \(JK/KK\) sector;
\item the scalar Bragg-mass obstruction \(M_0\) remains logically separate from the witness coefficient point \((\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta)\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

At the current refined locked \(+\) Class II stage, the actual shell witness coefficients are extracted from the Schur-complement block
\[
\Delta_X
=
-\frac1{M_X^2}
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)
(\alpha_X\mathcal J+\beta_X\mathcal K)^\dagger,
\]
not directly from the pre-Schur tensor
\[
\mathsf C^{\mathrm{valley}}=\alpha_X\mathsf J+\beta_X\mathsf K.
\]

Using the shell-adapted leading ansatz
\[
\mathsf J_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,j^a\,(\Sigma_3)_r{}^{a}
+
\mathsf J^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
\]
\[
\mathsf K_{i,r}^{a}(G_*;0)
=
\hat n_i\,k^a
\Big[
\Lambda_E^{(0)}(\Sigma_1)_r{}^{a}
+
\Lambda_O^{(0)}(\Sigma_2)_r{}^{a}
\Big]
+
\mathsf K^{\mathrm{null}}_{i,r}{}^{a},
\]
the exact branch-level leading coefficient point becomes
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
c_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
c_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\]

Hence the reduced Dirac witness coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
\alpha
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\]

Therefore the explicit branch-level nondegeneracy condition is
\[
\boxed{
j^2\neq 0,
\qquad
(j\!\cdot\!k)\neq 0,
\qquad
(\Lambda_E^{(0)},\Lambda_O^{(0)})\neq (0,0),
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

The corresponding anisotropy ratio is
\[
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac12
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta}
\frac{j^2}{|j\!\cdot\!k|}
\frac{1}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}},
}
\]
and using
\[
\frac{I_{\theta'^3}}{I_\theta}=\frac{3}{16}\theta_0^2\kappa^2,
\]
this becomes
\[
\boxed{
\rho
=
\frac{3}{32}
\frac{\alpha_X}{\beta_X}
\frac{j^2}{|j\!\cdot\!k|}
\frac{\theta_0^2\kappa^2}{\sqrt{\Lambda_E^{(0)2}+\Lambda_O^{(0)2}}}.
}
\]

Honest status:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the explicit branch-level coefficient point is now closed,}
}

but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the unconditional full microscopic transverse closure still requires the derivative-resolved shell audit,}
}

and

\section{Final Bloch Calibration: Exact Separation of the Transport Coefficient Point and the Bloch Overlap Layer}

\section{Goal}

At the present stage, the transport-side coefficient point of the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is already explicit.
However, the actual microscopic shell coefficients are not given directly by this transport-side point.
They still require the final Bloch-frame overlap calibration.

Thus the final microscopic task is to separate exactly:

\[
\text{transport-side coefficients }(g_c,g_E,g_O)
\]
from
\[
\text{Bloch overlap constants }(C_c,C_E,C_O),
\]
and then reconstruct the physical reduced coefficients
\[
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\section{Transport/Bloch exact normalization layer}

The exact overlap-normalization dictionary is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O.
}
\label{eq:exact_transport_bloch_dictionary}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\lambda_\parallel}{C_c},
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha}{C_E},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\beta}{C_O}.
}
\label{eq:g_from_C_dictionary}
\end{equation}

This layer is exact.
What remains open is only the explicit evaluation of the overlap constants
\[
C_c,\qquad C_E,\qquad C_O.
\]

\section{Current branch-level transport coefficient point}

Inside the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the leading explicit coefficient point is already fixed in branch-level closed form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:branch_g_point}
\end{equation}

Therefore the physical reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
C_c\,
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\label{eq:lambda_final_Cg}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
C_E\,
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
}
\label{eq:alpha_final_Cg}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
C_O\,
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:beta_final_Cg}
\end{equation}

Thus the previous branch-level formulas are not replaced; they are completed by the final Bloch overlap layer.

\section{Projected shell matrix audit}

Let
\[
\Pi_D
\]
be the projector onto the shell-relevant doubled low-mode block
\[
\mathcal H_D\cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}}.
\]

Let the linear-in-\(p\) projected Bloch operator be
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_D^{(1)}(p)
=
\Pi_D\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}(p)\Pi_D\Big|_{\mathrm{linear\ in}\ p}.
\label{eq:LD1_calib}
\end{equation}

Choose low-mode bases \(\{u_a^+\}\), \(\{u_b^-\}\) at the opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\), and define the projected shell matrices
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle u_a^+,\,V^\mu\,u_b^- \rangle,
\qquad
a,b=1,2.
\label{eq:Mmu_calib}
\end{equation}

Then the first-order shell symbol is
\begin{equation}
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.
\label{eq:A1pmu_calib}
\end{equation}

\section{Shell-adapted Pauli decomposition}

Fix the shell direction
\[
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
and an orthonormal frame
\[
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\}.
\]
Define
\[
M^\parallel:=\hat n_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
M^1:=e_{1\mu}M^\mu,
\qquad
M^2:=e_{2\mu}M^\mu.
\]

Under the locked Pauli selection rule, the shell matrices take the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^\parallel=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\qquad
M^1=\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2,
\qquad
M^2=\alpha\sigma_2-\beta\sigma_1.
}
\label{eq:locked_Pauli_shell}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced coefficients are extracted exactly by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel),
}
\label{eq:lambda_trace_calib}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1+\sigma_2M^2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1-\sigma_1M^2).
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_trace_calib}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the explicit nondegeneracy test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel)\neq 0,
\qquad
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1),\,
\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1)
\right)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:matrix_nondeg_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Definition of the calibration overlaps}

The overlap constants are defined by comparing the projected shell matrices with the transport-side coefficient point.

Write the three unit channels:
\[
(c\text{-unit}),\qquad
(E\text{-unit}),\qquad
(O\text{-unit}),
\]
meaning:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(g_c=1,\ g_E=g_O=0\);
\item \(g_E=1,\ g_c=g_O=0\);
\item \(g_O=1,\ g_c=g_E=0\).
\end{enumerate}

Then the Bloch overlaps are exactly the shell traces extracted from these three unit-channel calibration runs:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c
=
\left.\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel)\right|_{g_c=1,\ g_E=g_O=0},
}
\label{eq:Cc_def_unit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
=
\left.\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1)\right|_{g_E=1,\ g_c=g_O=0},
}
\label{eq:CE_def_unit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
=
\left.\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1)\right|_{g_O=1,\ g_c=g_E=0}.
}
\label{eq:CO_def_unit}
\end{equation}

Once these are known, the full coefficients follow from \eqref{eq:exact_transport_bloch_dictionary}.

\section{Final microscopic decision theorem for the current branch}

The current working ansatz survives the final microscopic audit if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:final_calibration_condition}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:final_calibration_condition} holds, then the current branch is dynamically sufficient to realize the required shell Dirac carrier.

If instead one finds
\begin{equation}
C_c=0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
(C_E,C_O)=(0,0),
\label{eq:calibration_failure}
\end{equation}
then this proves that the present microscopic action is structurally obstructed from being the final complete microscopic TECT PDE.

\section{Anisotropy ratio after calibration}

Before calibration, the branch-level anisotropy ratio is
\[
\rho_{\mathrm{branch}}=\frac{|g_c|}{\sqrt{g_E^2+g_O^2}}.
\]
After Bloch calibration, the physical anisotropy ratio becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\rho_{\mathrm{phys}}
=
\frac{|C_c|}{\sqrt{C_E^2g_E^2+C_O^2g_O^2}}\,
|g_c|.
}
\label{eq:rho_phys_calibrated}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, substituting \eqref{eq:branch_g_point},
\begin{equation}
\rho_{\mathrm{phys}}
=
\frac{
|C_c|\,\dfrac12 I_{\theta'^3}\dfrac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2
}{
\sqrt{
\left(
C_E I_\theta\dfrac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)}
\right)^2
+
\left(
C_O I_\theta\dfrac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}
\right)^2
}
}.
\label{eq:rho_phys_expanded}
\end{equation}

Thus the transport-side ratio and the physical Bloch-calibrated ratio differ unless the shell basis is canonically normalized so that
\[
C_c=C_E=C_O=1.
\]

\section{Honest status}

At this point the logic is sharply separated:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduced Dirac/Weyl architecture is already algebraically closed;
\item the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch gives an explicit transport-side coefficient point \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\);
\item the final microscopic arbiter is the Bloch-frame calibration \((C_c,C_E,C_O)\);
\item failure of the calibration is not a minor defect but a structural obstruction of the current working microscopic ansatz.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch provides an explicit transport-side coefficient point
\[
\boxed{
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}

However, the actual physical reduced coefficients are not these raw transport numbers.
They are obtained only after the final Bloch-frame overlap calibration:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O.
}
\]

The Bloch overlaps are extracted from the projected \(2\times2\) shell matrices
\[
(M^\mu)_{ab}=\langle u_a^+,V^\mu u_b^- \rangle,
\qquad
A_1(p)=p_\mu M^\mu.

With

M^\parallel=\hat n_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
M^1=e_{1\mu}M^\mu,

the exact Pauli-trace extraction is

\alpha=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1+\sigma_2M^2),
\qquad

}

Equivalently, the overlap constants are fixed by the three unit calibration runs:

\boxed{
C_c
=
\left.\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel)\right|_{g_c=1},
\qquad
C_E
=
\left.\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1)\right|_{g_E=1},
\qquad
C_O
=
\left.\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1)\right|_{g_O=1}.
}
\]

Therefore the final microscopic viability condition for the current working ansatz is
\[
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

If this condition holds, then the current branch is dynamically sufficient and the Dirac carrier is microscopically realized.
If instead one finds
\[
C_c=0
\qquad\text{or}\qquad
(C_E,C_O)=(0,0),
\]
this rigorously proves that the present
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi,P]
+

is structurally incomplete as the final full microscopic TECT PDE.

Thus the strongest honest current status is:

\boxed{
\text{the reduced Dirac architecture is closed,}

but
