\section{Exact Unit-Channel Bloch Calibration and the General Calibration Matrix}

\section{Goal}

The final microscopic frontier is the explicit evaluation of the Bloch overlap layer.
The usual diagonal normalization law
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O
\]
is correct only after the shell basis, Pauli basis, and unit-channel conventions are fixed so that the calibration map is diagonal.

To make the calibration protocol completely rigorous, one should first define the general linear calibration map, and only then impose the locked Pauli selection rule as the condition that diagonalizes it.

\section{Transport-side coefficient vector}

Define the transport-side coefficient vector
\begin{equation}
g:=
\begin{pmatrix}
g_c\\ g_E\\ g_O
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:g_vector_def}
\end{equation}

For the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the explicit branch-level leading point is
\begin{equation}
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\label{eq:g_branch_point_cal}
\end{equation}

\section{Bloch-side extracted coefficient vector}

Let
\[
\Pi_D
\]
be the projector onto the shell-relevant doubled low-mode block, and let
\[
\{\Psi_a^+\}_{a=1}^2,\qquad
\{\Psi_b^-\}_{b=1}^2
\]
be the orthonormal opposite-valley low-mode bases.

Project the full microscopic first-order Bloch linearization to the doubled shell block:
\begin{equation}
\mathcal L_D^{(1),\mu}
=
\Pi_D\mathcal L_{\mathrm{mic}}^{\mu}\Pi_D\Big|_{\mathrm{linear\ in}\ p}.
\label{eq:LD_projected_cal}
\end{equation}

Define the shell matrices
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_a^+,\mathcal L_D^{(1),\mu}\Psi_b^- \rangle.
\label{eq:Mmu_def_cal}
\end{equation}

With the shell-adapted frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\), define
\begin{equation}
M^\parallel=\hat n_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
M^1=e_{1\mu}M^\mu,
\qquad
M^2=e_{2\mu}M^\mu.
\label{eq:Mpar12_def_cal}
\end{equation}

The Bloch-side extracted coefficient vector is
\begin{equation}
y:=
\begin{pmatrix}
\lambda_\parallel\\ \alpha\\ \beta
\end{pmatrix},
\label{eq:y_vector_def}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel),
\label{eq:lambda_trace_general_cal}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\alpha=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1+\sigma_2M^2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1-\sigma_1M^2).
\label{eq:alpha_beta_trace_general_cal}
\end{equation}

\section{General calibration matrix}

Because the projected trace extraction is linear in the microscopic first-order operator, there exists a real \(3\times3\) calibration matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y=\mathbb C\,g,
\qquad
\mathbb C\in M_{3\times3}(\mathbb R).
}
\label{eq:general_calibration_matrix}
\end{equation}

Write
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C=
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{\parallel c} & C_{\parallel E} & C_{\parallel O}\\
C_{Ec} & C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{Oc} & C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Cmatrix_components}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{align}
\lambda_\parallel
&=
C_{\parallel c}g_c+C_{\parallel E}g_E+C_{\parallel O}g_O,
\label{eq:lambda_general_mix}
\\
\alpha
&=
C_{Ec}g_c+C_{EE}g_E+C_{EO}g_O,
\label{eq:alpha_general_mix}
\\
\beta
&=
C_{Oc}g_c+C_{OE}g_E+C_{OO}g_O.
\label{eq:beta_general_mix}
\end{align}

This is the most rigorous general form of the Bloch calibration layer.

\section{Unit-channel calibration runs}

To compute \(\mathbb C\), one performs the three unit-channel calibration runs:

\paragraph{(c-unit)}
Set
\[
g^{(c)}=(1,0,0)^T.
\]
Compute the projected shell matrices
\[
M^{\parallel}_{(c)},\qquad M^1_{(c)},\qquad M^2_{(c)},
\]
and define
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C_{\bullet c}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1_{(c)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(c)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1_{(c)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(c)})
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Ccol_c}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(E-unit)}
Set
\[
g^{(E)}=(0,1,0)^T.
\]
Compute
\[
M^{\parallel}_{(E)},\qquad M^1_{(E)},\qquad M^2_{(E)},
\]
and define
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C_{\bullet E}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(E)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1_{(E)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(E)})
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Ccol_E}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(O-unit)}
Set
\[
g^{(O)}=(0,0,1)^T.
\]
Compute
\[
M^{\parallel}_{(O)},\qquad M^1_{(O)},\qquad M^2_{(O)},
\]
and define
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C_{\bullet O}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(O)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1_{(O)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(O)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)})
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:Ccol_O}
\end{equation}

The three columns \(\mathbb C_{\bullet c},\mathbb C_{\bullet E},\mathbb C_{\bullet O}\) determine the full calibration matrix \(\mathbb C\).

\section{Diagonal locked calibration}

Under the exact locked Pauli selection rule, there is no cross-channel mixing:
\begin{equation}
C_{\parallel E}=C_{\parallel O}=C_{Ec}=C_{EO}=C_{Oc}=C_{OE}=0.
\label{eq:diagonal_locking}
\end{equation}

Then \(\mathbb C\) becomes diagonal:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C=\mathrm{diag}(C_c,C_E,C_O),
}
\label{eq:Cmatrix_diag}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c=
\frac12\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)}),
}
\label{eq:Cc_diag_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E=
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)}),
}
\label{eq:CE_diag_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O=
\frac14\operatorname{Tr}(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)}).
}
\label{eq:CO_diag_def}
\end{equation}

In this case the calibration law reduces exactly to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_cg_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_Eg_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_Og_O.
}
\label{eq:diag_dictionary_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Decision criteria}

\subsection{Diagonal case}

If the locked Pauli selection rule is exact and \(\mathbb C\) is diagonal, the branch survives the Bloch calibration iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:diag_decision}
\end{equation}

\subsection{General case}

If small off-diagonal mixing is present, the correct criterion is not \eqref{eq:diag_decision} but:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det \mathbb C\neq 0
}
\label{eq:invertibility_decision}
\end{equation}
together with the requirement that the image of the transverse transport plane
\[
\mathrm{span}\{(0,1,0)^T,(0,0,1)^T\}
\]
under \(\mathbb C\) is genuinely two-dimensional in the shell-extracted \((\alpha,\beta)\) sector.

Equivalently, writing
\[
\mathbb C_\perp=
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix},
\]
one needs
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\parallel c}\neq 0,
\qquad
\det \mathbb C_\perp \neq 0.
}
\label{eq:block_decision}
\end{equation}

Thus the diagonal criterion is just the symmetry-reduced special case of the general matrix criterion.

\section{Current branch after calibration}

Substituting the current branch-level transport point \eqref{eq:g_branch_point_cal} into the diagonal calibration law, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
C_c\,\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\label{eq:lambda_calibrated_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
C_E\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
}
\label{eq:alpha_calibrated_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
C_O\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:beta_calibrated_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the final microscopic viability of the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is decided entirely by the finite projected shell audit of \(\mathbb C\).

\section{Honest status}

At the current strongest honest stage:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduced Dirac architecture is algebraically closed;
\item the branch-level transport coefficient point \((g_c,g_E,g_O)\) is explicit;
\item the final remaining microscopic frontier is the explicit evaluation of the Bloch calibration matrix \(\mathbb C\);
\item if \(\mathbb C\) fails the required rank/nondegeneracy test, then the present working microscopic ansatz is structurally incomplete.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Summary}

The final Bloch calibration layer should be written in its most rigorous form as a linear map
\[
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
\lambda_\parallel\\ \alpha\\ \beta
\end{pmatrix}
=
\mathbb C
\begin{pmatrix}
g_c\\ g_E\\ g_O
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\mathbb C\in M_{3\times3}(\mathbb R).
}
\]

The matrix \(\mathbb C\) is determined by the three unit-channel calibration runs:
\[
(c\text{-unit}),\qquad
(E\text{-unit}),\qquad
(O\text{-unit}),
\]
by projecting the first-order Bloch linearization to the doubled shell block and evaluating the Pauli traces of
\[
M^\parallel,\qquad M^1,\qquad M^2.
\]

If the locked Pauli selection rule is exact, then \(\mathbb C\) is diagonal:
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb C=\mathrm{diag}(C_c,C_E,C_O),
}
\]
and the calibration law reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_cg_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_Eg_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_Og_O.
}
\]

In this diagonal case, the final microscopic viability condition is
\[
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

In the more general case with residual cross-channel mixing, the correct criterion is:
\[
\boxed{
C_{\parallel c}\neq 0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}
\neq 0.
}
\]

For the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the transport-side coefficient point is already explicit:
\[
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Therefore, after diagonal calibration,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
C_c\,\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
C_E\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
C_O\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\]

Thus the strongest honest current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the reduced Dirac architecture is closed,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the branch-level transport coefficient point is explicit,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the final microscopic arbiter is the explicit Bloch calibration matrix }\mathbb C.
}
\]

If that calibration fails the stated nondegeneracy/rank test, then the present working microscopic ansatz is structurally incomplete.

\section{Executable Bloch Calibration Protocol for the Refined Locked Shell Carrier}

\section{Goal}

The reduced Dirac architecture is already closed.
The branch-level transport coefficient point
\[
(g_c,g_E,g_O)
\]
is already explicit.
Hence the only remaining microscopic frontier is the explicit Bloch calibration step.

The goal is to construct an executable finite protocol:
\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\;\longrightarrow\;
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\;\longrightarrow\;
P_D
\;\longrightarrow\;
M^\mu
\;\longrightarrow\;
\mathbb C
\;\longrightarrow\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

\section{Step 0: fixed input data}

Fix once and for all:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the selected opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\),
\item the folded shell center
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\]
\item the shell-adapted orthonormal frame
\[
(\hat n,e_1,e_2),
\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},
\]
\item the doubled low shell block
\[
\mathcal H_D \cong \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{valley}}\otimes \mathbb C^2_{\mathrm{int}},
\]
with an orthonormal basis
\[
\{\Psi_a^+\}_{a=1}^2,\qquad
\{\Psi_b^-\}_{b=1}^2.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{Step 1: construct the Bloch effective operator}

Start from the refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
H_{\Psi X}(k)H_{XX}(k)^{-1}H_{X\Psi}(k),
\qquad
H_{XX}(k)=M_X^2\mathbf 1_X.
\label{eq:protocol_Heff}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
=
H_{\Psi\Psi}(k)
-
\frac1{M_X^2}
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)
\bigl(\alpha_X\mathcal J(k)+\beta_X\mathcal K(k)\bigr)^\dagger.
\label{eq:protocol_Heff_schur}
\end{equation}

This is the only microscopic input required for the calibration run.

\section{Step 2: shell projection}

Define the shell-projected operator around the chosen shell pair:
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
=
\Pi_{S_*}\,H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k_*+p)\,\Pi_{S_*}.
\label{eq:protocol_Hshell}
\end{equation}

Here \(\Pi_{S_*}\) projects to the shell truncation used for the chosen opposite-valley pair.

\section{Step 3: low-slot spectral projector}

At \(p=0\), diagonalize the shell block
\[
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0).
\]
Choose the \(4\)-dimensional low carrier
\[
\mathcal H_D\subset \mathcal H_{\mathrm{shell}}
\]
and define its spectral projector
\begin{equation}
P_D
=
\frac{1}{2\pi i}\oint_{\Gamma_D}(z-H_{\mathrm{shell}}(0))^{-1}\,dz,
\label{eq:protocol_PD}
\end{equation}
where \(\Gamma_D\) encloses exactly the desired doubled low slot.

Then define the core shell block
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}(p)
=
P_D H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p) P_D.
\label{eq:protocol_Hcore}
\end{equation}

\section{Step 4: first-order Bloch matrices}

Expand \(H_{\mathrm{core}}(p)\) to first order in \(p\):
\begin{equation}
H_{\mathrm{core}}(p)
=
H_{\mathrm{core}}(0)+p_\mu M^\mu+O(|p|^2).
\label{eq:protocol_linear_expand}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
M^\mu
=
\left.
P_D\,\partial_{k_\mu}H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)\,P_D
\right|_{k=k_*}.
\label{eq:protocol_Mmu}
\end{equation}

In the chosen opposite-valley basis,
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_a^+,\,M^\mu\,\Psi_b^- \rangle.
\label{eq:protocol_Mmu_ab}
\end{equation}

Now define the shell-adapted components
\begin{equation}
M^\parallel:=\hat n_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
M^1:=e_{1\mu}M^\mu,
\qquad
M^2:=e_{2\mu}M^\mu.
\label{eq:protocol_Mcomponents}
\end{equation}

\section{Step 5: direct Pauli-trace extraction}

If the locked Pauli selection rule holds exactly, then
\begin{equation}
M^\parallel=\lambda_\parallel\sigma_3,
\qquad
M^1=\alpha\sigma_1+\beta\sigma_2,
\qquad
M^2=\alpha\sigma_2-\beta\sigma_1.
\label{eq:protocol_locked_form}
\end{equation}

Hence the reduced coefficients are extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel),
}
\label{eq:protocol_lambda_trace}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1+\sigma_2M^2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1-\sigma_1M^2).
}
\label{eq:protocol_alpha_beta_trace}
\end{equation}

This is the direct shell-side readout.

\section{Step 6: general calibration matrix}

To make the protocol fully rigorous, define
\[
g=
\begin{pmatrix}
g_c\\ g_E\\ g_O
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
y=
\begin{pmatrix}
\lambda_\parallel\\ \alpha\\ \beta
\end{pmatrix}.
\]
Then there exists a real \(3\times3\) matrix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
y=\mathbb C\,g.
}
\label{eq:protocol_Cmatrix}
\end{equation}

If the locked Pauli selection rule is exact and there is no cross-channel mixing, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C=\mathrm{diag}(C_c,C_E,C_O),
}
\label{eq:protocol_diagC}
\end{equation}
so that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
}
\label{eq:protocol_diag_dictionary}
\end{equation}

\section{Step 7: three unit-channel calibration runs}

To compute \(\mathbb C\), perform the following three runs.

\subsection*{(c-unit)}
Set
\[
g^{(c)}=(1,0,0)^T.
\]
Compute the corresponding first-order Bloch matrices
\[
M^\parallel_{(c)},\qquad M^1_{(c)},\qquad M^2_{(c)}.
\]
Then the first column of \(\mathbb C\) is
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C_{\bullet c}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(c)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(c)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(c)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(c)})
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:protocol_col_c}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(E-unit)}
Set
\[
g^{(E)}=(0,1,0)^T.
\]
Compute
\[
M^\parallel_{(E)},\qquad M^1_{(E)},\qquad M^2_{(E)}.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C_{\bullet E}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(E)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(E)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(E)})
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:protocol_col_E}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(O-unit)}
Set
\[
g^{(O)}=(0,0,1)^T.
\]
Compute
\[
M^\parallel_{(O)},\qquad M^1_{(O)},\qquad M^2_{(O)}.
\]
Then
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C_{\bullet O}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(O)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(O)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(O)})\\[2mm]
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)})
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:protocol_col_O}
\end{equation}

Thus the full calibration matrix is
\[
\mathbb C=
\bigl(
\mathbb C_{\bullet c}\;\mathbb C_{\bullet E}\;\mathbb C_{\bullet O}
\bigr).
\]

\section{Step 8: decision criteria}

\subsection*{Diagonal locked case}

If the shell basis is already locked and no cross-channel mixing appears, then
\[
\mathbb C=\mathrm{diag}(C_c,C_E,C_O).
\]
The branch survives iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:protocol_diag_decision}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{General case}

If small cross-channel mixing is present, then the correct criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\parallel c}\neq 0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}
\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:protocol_general_decision}
\end{equation}
Equivalently, the longitudinal image must be nonzero and the transverse image must have rank two.

\section{Step 9: insert the current branch-level transport point}

For the present refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the transport-side coefficient point is
\begin{equation}
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\label{eq:protocol_gpoint_insert}
\end{equation}

Therefore, after diagonal calibration,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
C_c\,\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\label{eq:protocol_lambda_final}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
C_E\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
C_O\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:protocol_alpha_beta_final}
\end{equation}

\section{Step 10: final outputs}

The protocol returns exactly four microscopic verdicts:

\begin{enumerate}
\item whether the longitudinal shell overlap survives;
\item whether the transverse shell overlap survives;
\item whether the calibration is diagonal or mildly mixed;
\item whether the current working branch is microscopically viable.
\end{enumerate}

The branch is accepted as the final microscopic carrier only if the calibration test passes.
If it fails, the conclusion is structural incompleteness of the present microscopic ansatz, not merely a poor parameter choice.

\section{Final Summary}

The final microscopic problem is no longer conceptual.
It is the executable finite Bloch calibration protocol

\[
H_{\mathrm{eff}}(k)
\;\longrightarrow\;
H_{\mathrm{shell}}(p)
\;\longrightarrow\;
P_D
\;\longrightarrow\;
M^\mu
\;\longrightarrow\;
\mathbb C
\;\longrightarrow\;
(\lambda_\parallel,\alpha,\beta).
\]

The projected shell matrices are
\[
M^\parallel=\hat n_\mu M^\mu,
\qquad
M^1=e_{1\mu}M^\mu,
\qquad
M^2=e_{2\mu}M^\mu.
\]

Their exact Pauli-trace readout is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1+\sigma_2M^2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1-\sigma_1M^2).
}
\]

The most rigorous calibration law is the linear map
\[
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
\lambda_\parallel\\ \alpha\\ \beta
\end{pmatrix}
=
\mathbb C
\begin{pmatrix}
g_c\\ g_E\\ g_O
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

Under exact locked Pauli selection, this reduces to the diagonal normalization layer
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
}
\]

The matrix \(\mathbb C\) is computed by three unit-channel runs:
\[
(c\text{-unit}),\qquad
(E\text{-unit}),\qquad
(O\text{-unit}),
\]
with columns extracted from the corresponding shell Pauli traces.

For the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch,
\[
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Hence, after diagonal calibration,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
C_c\,\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\alpha
=
C_E\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
C_O\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}

Therefore the final microscopic viability criterion is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{diagonal locked case: }
C_c\neq0,\qquad (C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0),
}
\]
or, more generally,
\[
\boxed{
\text{mixed case: }
C_{\parallel c}\neq0,\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE}&C_{EO}\\
C_{OE}&C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}\neq0.
}
\]

Thus the strongest honest current status is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{the reduced Dirac architecture is closed,}
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{the branch-level transport coefficient point is explicit,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the final microscopic arbiter is the explicit unit-channel Bloch calibration.}
}
\]

\section{Explicit Unit-Channel Implementation for the Final Bloch Calibration}

\section{Goal}

The final Bloch calibration requires not only the abstract statement
\[
g^{(c)}=(1,0,0),\qquad
g^{(E)}=(0,1,0),\qquad
g^{(O)}=(0,0,1),
\]
but an explicit microscopic realization of these three unit channels as concrete first-order transport inputs.

The correct implementation is to start from the already constructed primitive shell seeds and normalize them so that their reduced witness output is exactly unit in the desired channel.

\section{Primitive seed operators}

The explicit primitive longitudinal seed is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,
n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
\label{eq:seed_long_impl}
\end{equation}

Its reduced witness is
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel[V_{(\parallel)}]
=
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha[V_{(\parallel)}]=0,
\qquad
\beta[V_{(\parallel)}]=0.
\label{eq:seed_long_output_impl}
\end{equation}

The explicit transverse even seed is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:seed_E_impl}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel[V_{(\perp,E)}]=0,
\qquad
\alpha[V_{(\perp,E)}]=I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta[V_{(\perp,E)}]=0.
\label{eq:seed_E_output_impl}
\end{equation}

The explicit transverse odd seed is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:seed_O_impl}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel[V_{(\perp,O)}]=0,
\qquad
\alpha[V_{(\perp,O)}]=0,
\qquad
\beta[V_{(\perp,O)}]=I_\theta.
\label{eq:seed_O_output_impl}
\end{equation}

\section{Normalized unit-channel inputs}

We now normalize these seeds so that the transport-side output is exactly one in the chosen channel.

\subsection*{(c-unit)}
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(c)}(\xi)
:=
\frac{2}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:c_unit_input}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel[V_{(c)}]=1,
\qquad
\alpha[V_{(c)}]=0,
\qquad
\beta[V_{(c)}]=0.
}
\label{eq:c_unit_output}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(E-unit)}
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)
:=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}\,V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:E_unit_input}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel[V_{(E)}]=0,
\qquad
\alpha[V_{(E)}]=1,
\qquad
\beta[V_{(E)}]=0.
}
\label{eq:E_unit_output}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(O-unit)}
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)
:=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}\,V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:O_unit_input}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel[V_{(O)}]=0,
\qquad
\alpha[V_{(O)}]=0,
\qquad
\beta[V_{(O)}]=1.
}
\label{eq:O_unit_output}
\end{equation}

Thus these three operators realize the canonical transport-side unit vectors
\[
g^{(c)}=(1,0,0)^T,\qquad
g^{(E)}=(0,1,0)^T,\qquad
g^{(O)}=(0,0,1)^T.
\]

\section{Projected Bloch implementation}

Let
\[
\{\Psi_a^+\}_{a=1}^2,\qquad
\{\Psi_b^-\}_{b=1}^2
\]
be the orthonormal opposite-valley Bloch basis spanning the shell-relevant doubled low block \(\mathcal H_D\).

For any one of the three unit inputs \(V^\mu_{(u)}\), with \(u\in\{c,E,O\}\), define the projected first-order Bloch matrices
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu_{(u)})_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_a^+,\,V^\mu_{(u)}\,\Psi_b^- \rangle.
\label{eq:Mmu_unit_impl}
\end{equation}

Using the shell-adapted frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\), define
\begin{equation}
M^\parallel_{(u)}=\hat n_\mu M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^1_{(u)}=e_{1\mu}M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^2_{(u)}=e_{2\mu}M^\mu_{(u)}.
\label{eq:Mcomp_unit_impl}
\end{equation}

\section{Column-by-column calibration matrix extraction}

The full calibration matrix
\[
\mathbb C=
\bigl(
\mathbb C_{\bullet c}\;
\mathbb C_{\bullet E}\;
\mathbb C_{\bullet O}
\bigr)
\]
is obtained by the three columns:

\subsection*{(c-column)}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C_{\bullet c}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(c)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(c)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(c)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(c)})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Ccol_c_impl}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(E-column)}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C_{\bullet E}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(E)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(E)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(E)})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Ccol_E_impl}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(O-column)}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C_{\bullet O}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(O)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(O)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(O)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Ccol_O_impl}
\end{equation}

This is the exact executable finite implementation of the Bloch calibration layer.

\section{Diagonal locked case}

If the locked Pauli selection rule holds exactly, then the off-channel entries vanish and
\[
\mathbb C=\mathrm{diag}(C_c,C_E,C_O),
\]
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)}),
}
\label{eq:Cc_impl}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)}),
}
\label{eq:CE_impl}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)}).
}
\label{eq:CO_impl}
\end{equation}

Therefore the physical coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O.
\label{eq:diag_final_impl}
\end{equation}

\section{Acceptance criteria}

\subsection*{Diagonal locked case}
The branch passes the final Bloch calibration iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:diag_accept_impl}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{General mixed case}
If the calibration is not perfectly diagonal, one must use the full matrix criterion:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\parallel c}\neq 0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}
\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:mixed_accept_impl}
\end{equation}

\section{Relation to the current branch-level coefficient point}

For the present refined locked \(+\) Class II branch,
\[
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]
Hence, after diagonal calibration,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
C_c\,
\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\label{eq:lambda_after_impl}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
C_E\,
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
C_O\,
I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:ab_after_impl}
\end{equation}

\section{Honest status}

At this point, the remaining frontier is no longer the definition of the seed channels or the calibration algorithm.
Both are explicit.

What remains is only the actual evaluation of the finite overlap matrices
\[
M^\mu_{(c)},\qquad M^\mu_{(E)},\qquad M^\mu_{(O)}
\]
in the true refined locked microscopic Bloch basis.

If this final projected overlap audit fails, the conclusion is not a minor normalization problem.
It means that the current working microscopic ansatz is structurally incomplete as the final full TECT PDE.

\section{Final Summary}

The correct microscopic implementation of the three unit-channel calibration runs is obtained by normalizing the already constructed primitive shell seeds.

The primitive seeds are:
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
\[
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

After exact unit normalization, the calibration inputs are
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(c)}(\xi)
=
\frac{2}{I_{\theta'^3}}V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\]

These realize the canonical unit transport outputs
\[
g^{(c)}=(1,0,0)^T,\qquad
g^{(E)}=(0,1,0)^T,\qquad
g^{(O)}=(0,0,1)^T.
\]

For each \(u\in\{c,E,O\}\), define the projected Bloch matrices
\[
(M^\mu_{(u)})_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_a^+,V^\mu_{(u)}\Psi_b^- \rangle,
\]
and their shell-adapted components
\[
M^\parallel_{(u)}=\hat n_\mu M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^1_{(u)}=e_{1\mu}M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^2_{(u)}=e_{2\mu}M^\mu_{(u)}.
\]

Then the calibration matrix columns are
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb C_{\bullet u}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(u)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(u)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(u)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(u)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(u)})
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u\in\{c,E,O\}.
}
\]

Under exact locked Pauli selection, this reduces to the diagonal normalization law
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_cg_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_Eg_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_Og_O.
}
\]

The diagonal acceptance criterion is
\[
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

If residual channel mixing is present, one must instead use the full matrix criterion
\[
\boxed{
C_{\parallel c}\neq 0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE}&C_{EO}\\
C_{OE}&C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}
\neq 0.
}
\]

Thus the seed operators and the calibration protocol are now explicit.
The only remaining frontier is the actual finite overlap evaluation in the true refined locked microscopic Bloch basis.

\section{Exact Folded-Bragg Overlap Formulas for the Unit-Channel Calibration}

\section{Fixed conventions and mandatory gate}

Before any calibration, one must first fix:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the low-valley Pauli basis \(\{\sigma_1,\sigma_2,\sigma_3\}\),
\item the shell-adapted frame \((\hat n,e_1,e_2)\),
\item the overlap normalization convention defining \(C_c,C_E,C_O\),
\item the sign convention for the lowest signed channel.
\end{enumerate}

Moreover, the remote-gap condition must hold so that the low slot is spectrally isolated and the projector \(P_D\) is well-defined:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
\]

\section{Folded Bragg basis}

Fix the selected opposite shell pair \(\pm G_*\) and adopt the folded Bragg convention
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
k=k_*+p,
\qquad
|p|\ll |G_*|.
}
\label{eq:folded_bragg_basis}
\end{equation}

Choose an orthonormal opposite-valley low-mode basis
\[
\{u_a^+\}_{a=1}^2,\qquad
\{u_b^-\}_{b=1}^2,
\]
and define the Bloch states
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a^+(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,b}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_b^-(x).
}
\label{eq:Psi_pm_basis}
\end{equation}

Then the intervalley first-order Bloch matrices are
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\langle \Psi_{+,a},V^\mu\Psi_{-,b}\rangle.
\label{eq:Mmu_def_general}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Psi_pm_basis} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,V^\mu(x)\,u_b^-(x).
}
\label{eq:Mmu_folded_exact}
\end{equation}

Thus every intervalley overlap is exactly the \(Q=G_*\) Fourier component of the operator weighted by the envelope overlap.

\section{Normalized unit-channel inputs}

The primitive seeds are
\[
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)=\theta'(\xi)J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\]

Their correctly normalized unit-channel versions are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(c)}(\xi)
=
\frac{2}{I_{\theta'^3}}V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Vc_unit_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}V^\mu_{(\perp,E)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
}
\label{eq:VE_unit_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}V^\mu_{(\perp,O)}(\xi)
=
\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:VO_unit_exact}
\end{equation}

These correspond exactly to the transport-side unit vectors
\[
g^{(c)}=(1,0,0)^T,\qquad
g^{(E)}=(0,1,0)^T,\qquad
g^{(O)}=(0,0,1)^T.
\]

\section{Cell-integral overlap matrices}

For each unit input \(u\in\{c,E,O\}\), define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu_{(u)})_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,V^\mu_{(u)}(x)\,u_b^-(x).
}
\label{eq:Mmu_u_exact}
\end{equation}

Now define the shell-adapted components
\begin{equation}
M^\parallel_{(u)}=\hat n_\mu M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^1_{(u)}=e_{1\mu}M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^2_{(u)}=e_{2\mu}M^\mu_{(u)}.
\label{eq:Mcomp_u_exact}
\end{equation}

These are the exact finite objects from which the calibration overlaps are extracted.

\section{Exact integral formulas for the calibration columns}

The full \(3\times3\) calibration matrix
\[
\mathbb C=
\bigl(
\mathbb C_{\bullet c}\;\mathbb C_{\bullet E}\;\mathbb C_{\bullet O}
\bigr)
\]
is computed column-by-column by Pauli traces.

\subsection*{(c-column)}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C_{\bullet c}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(c)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(c)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(c)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(c)})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Ccol_c_exact}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(E-column)}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C_{\bullet E}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(E)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(E)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(E)})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Ccol_E_exact}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(O-column)}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb C_{\bullet O}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(O)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(O)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(O)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)})
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Ccol_O_exact}
\end{equation}

This is the fully executable finite calibration layer.

\section{Diagonal locked case}

If the locked Pauli selection rule holds exactly, then off-channel mixing vanishes and
\[
\mathbb C=\mathrm{diag}(C_c,C_E,C_O).
\]

In that case,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c
=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)})
=
\frac{1}{2I_{\theta'^3}}
\Tr\!\left[
\sigma_3
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger(x)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3\,U_-(x)
\right],
}
\label{eq:Cc_integral_exact}
\end{equation}
where
\[
U_\pm(x):=(u_1^\pm(x),u_2^\pm(x)).
\]

Likewise,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)})
=
\frac{1}{4I_\theta}
\Tr\!\left[
\sigma_1
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger\theta'(\xi)E^1{}_a\sigma_a U_-
+
\sigma_2
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger\theta'(\xi)E^2{}_a\sigma_a U_-
\right],
}
\label{eq:CE_integral_exact}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)})
=
\frac{1}{4I_\theta}
\Tr\!\left[
\sigma_2
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger\theta'(\xi)J^1{}_a\sigma_a U_-
-
\sigma_1
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger\theta'(\xi)J^2{}_a\sigma_a U_-
\right].
}
\label{eq:CO_integral_exact}
\end{equation}

These are the exact folded-Bragg overlap formulas for the diagonal calibration constants.

\section{Reduction to one-dimensional radial overlaps}

If the opposite-valley Bloch modes separate as
\[
u_a^\pm(x)=f_\pm(\xi)\,\chi_a(x_\perp,\xi),
\]
then all three calibration constants reduce to weighted radial overlaps of the form
\begin{equation}
C_c
=
\frac{1}{I_{\theta'^3}}
\int d\xi\;f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi),
\label{eq:Cc_radial_reduce}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_E
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\;f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_E(\xi),
\qquad
C_O
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\;f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_O(\xi),
\label{eq:CEO_radial_reduce}
\end{equation}
where the profile functions \(\mathfrak s_c,\mathfrak s_E,\mathfrak s_O\) are the corresponding internal/tangential Bloch overlaps.

Thus \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) measure the mismatch between the canonical seed normalization and the actual Bloch low-mode frame.

\section{Final acceptance criterion}

In the diagonal locked case, the final calibration test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:diag_accept_exact}
\end{equation}

In the general mixed case, one must use the full matrix criterion:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_{\parallel c}\neq 0,
\qquad
\det
\begin{pmatrix}
C_{EE} & C_{EO}\\
C_{OE} & C_{OO}
\end{pmatrix}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:mixed_accept_exact}
\end{equation}

\section{Connection to the current branch-level coefficient point}

For the present refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the transport-side point is already explicit:
\[
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]

Hence, after diagonal calibration,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
C_c\,\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
}
\label{eq:lambda_after_overlap}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
C_E\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
\beta
=
C_O\,I_\theta\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
}
\label{eq:ab_after_overlap}
\end{equation}

\section{Honest status}

At this point the seed operators, the unit normalization, the folded-Bragg matrix elements,
and the calibration traces are all explicit.

What remains is only the actual finite evaluation of the overlap integrals
\[
M^\mu_{(c)},\qquad M^\mu_{(E)},\qquad M^\mu_{(O)}
\]
in the true refined locked microscopic Bloch basis.

If this final overlap audit fails, the conclusion is structural incompleteness of the current working microscopic ansatz, not merely an unfortunate normalization choice.

\section{Final Summary}

Using the folded Bragg convention
\[
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2},
\qquad
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a^+(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,b}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_b^-(x),
\]
the intervalley projected Bloch matrix element of any first-order transport input \(V^\mu\) is exactly
\[
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,V^\mu(x)\,u_b^-(x).
}
\]

The correctly normalized unit-channel inputs are
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(c)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\]

For each \(u\in\{c,E,O\}\), define
\[
M^\parallel_{(u)}=\hat n_\mu M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^1_{(u)}=e_{1\mu}M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^2_{(u)}=e_{2\mu}M^\mu_{(u)}.
\]

Then the calibration matrix columns are exactly
\[
\boxed{
\mathbb C_{\bullet u}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(u)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(u)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(u)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(u)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(u)})
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
u\in\{c,E,O\}.
}
\]

If the locked Pauli selection rule is exact, this reduces to the diagonal overlap-normalization law
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
}
\]

The exact folded-Bragg overlap formulas are then
\[
\boxed{
C_c
=
\frac{1}{2I_{\theta'^3}}
\Tr\!\left[
\sigma_3
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger(x)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3\,U_-(x)
\right],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac{1}{4I_\theta}
\Tr\!\left[
\sigma_1
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger\theta'(\xi)E^1{}_a\sigma_a U_-
+
\sigma_2
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger\theta'(\xi)E^2{}_a\sigma_a U_-
\right],
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_O
=
\frac{1}{4I_\theta}
\Tr\!\left[
\sigma_2
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger\theta'(\xi)J^1{}_a\sigma_a U_-
-
\sigma_1
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger\theta'(\xi)J^2{}_a\sigma_a U_-
\right].
}
\]

Thus \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) are not abstract constants; they are exact normalized \(Q=G_*\) Bloch-overlap integrals in the true low-mode frame.

The diagonal acceptance criterion is
\[
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]
More generally, in the mixed case one must use the full calibration matrix rank condition.

Therefore the strongest honest current status is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the seed channels and the calibration protocol are explicit,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{the final microscopic frontier is still the actual finite evaluation of these folded-Bragg overlap integrals.}
}
\]

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Factorization of the Folded-Bragg Calibration Integrals}

\section{Exact starting point}

Fix the folded Bragg basis
\begin{equation}
\Psi_{+,a}(x)=e^{ik_*\cdot x}u_a^+(x),
\qquad
\Psi_{-,b}(x)=e^{-ik_*\cdot x}u_b^-(x),
\qquad
k_*=\frac{G_*}{2}.
\label{eq:factor_basis}
\end{equation}

For any unit-channel input \(V^\mu_{(u)}\), \(u\in\{c,E,O\}\), the projected intervalley matrix is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu_{(u)})_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,V^\mu_{(u)}(x)\,u_b^-(x).
}
\label{eq:M_exact_factor}
\end{equation}

The shell-adapted matrices are
\begin{equation}
M^\parallel_{(u)}=\hat n_\mu M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^1_{(u)}=e_{1\mu}M^\mu_{(u)},
\qquad
M^2_{(u)}=e_{2\mu}M^\mu_{(u)}.
\label{eq:M_components_factor}
\end{equation}

The overlap-calibration columns are then
\begin{equation}
\mathbb C_{\bullet u}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\dfrac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(u)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(u)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(u)})\\[2mm]
\dfrac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(u)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(u)})
\end{pmatrix}.
\label{eq:C_columns_factor}
\end{equation}

In the exact locked diagonal case,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)}),\qquad
C_E=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)}),\qquad
C_O=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)}).
}
\label{eq:C_diag_factor}
\end{equation}

\section{Normalized unit-channel seeds}

The correctly normalized calibration inputs are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(c)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Vc_factor}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
}
\label{eq:VEO_factor}
\end{equation}

\section{Separable shell-adapted low-mode ansatz}

To reduce the 3D cell overlap to a more transparent form, assume the shell-adapted low modes admit the decomposition
\begin{equation}
u_a^\pm(x)=f_\pm(\xi)\,\chi_a^\pm(x_\perp,\xi),
\label{eq:sep_ansatz_factor}
\end{equation}
where
\[
x=(x_\perp,\xi),
\qquad
\xi:=\hat n\cdot x,
\qquad
x_\perp\perp \hat n.
\]

This is not an additional conceptual theorem; it is the natural factorized implementation of the defect-adapted shell basis.

Substituting \eqref{eq:sep_ansatz_factor} into \eqref{eq:M_exact_factor}, we obtain
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu_{(u)})_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\;
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
\mathcal I^\mu_{ab;(u)}(\xi),
\label{eq:M_xi_reduction}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I^\mu_{ab;(u)}(\xi)
:=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}_\perp(\xi)} d^2x_\perp\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{\chi_a^+(x_\perp,\xi)}\,
V^\mu_{(u)}(x_\perp,\xi)\,
\chi_b^-(x_\perp,\xi).
}
\label{eq:Iab_mu_xi}
\end{equation}

Thus the full overlap is already reduced to a one-dimensional weighted integral over \(\xi\), with a transverse primitive-cell overlap kernel \(\mathcal I^\mu_{ab;(u)}(\xi)\).

\section{Primitive-cell Fourier / internal split}

For the unit seeds \eqref{eq:Vc_factor}--\eqref{eq:VEO_factor}, the \(\xi\)-dependence factorizes explicitly:
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(c)}(x)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,
\mathcal S^\mu_{(c)}(x_\perp,\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal S^\mu_{(c)}:=n^\mu\sigma_3,
\label{eq:Sc_factor}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(E)}(x)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,
\mathcal S^\mu_{(E)}(x_\perp,\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal S^\mu_{(E)}:=E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\label{eq:SE_factor}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
V^\mu_{(O)}(x)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,
\mathcal S^\mu_{(O)}(x_\perp,\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal S^\mu_{(O)}:=J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:SO_factor}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu_{(c)})_{ab}
=
\frac{1}{I_{\theta'^3}}
\int d\xi\;f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,
\mathfrak F^\mu_{ab;(c)}(\xi),
\label{eq:M_c_factorized}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu_{(E)})_{ab}
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\;f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\mathfrak F^\mu_{ab;(E)}(\xi),
\label{eq:M_E_factorized}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
(M^\mu_{(O)})_{ab}
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\;f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,
\mathfrak F^\mu_{ab;(O)}(\xi),
\label{eq:M_O_factorized}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak F^\mu_{ab;(u)}(\xi)
:=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}_\perp(\xi)} d^2x_\perp\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{\chi_a^+(x_\perp,\xi)}\,
\mathcal S^\mu_{(u)}(x_\perp,\xi)\,
\chi_b^-(x_\perp,\xi).
}
\label{eq:Fkernel_def}
\end{equation}

This is the precise factorization:
\[
\text{radial weight}\times \text{primitive-cell Fourier overlap}\times \text{internal matrix overlap}.
\]

\section{Compressed scalar overlap functions}

Define the shell-traced scalar kernels
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak s_c(\xi)
:=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_3\,\hat n_\mu\,\mathfrak F^\mu_{(c)}(\xi)\bigr),
\label{eq:sc_xi_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak s_E(\xi)
:=
\frac14\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_1 e_{1\mu}\mathfrak F^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)+\sigma_2 e_{2\mu}\mathfrak F^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)\bigr),
\label{eq:sE_xi_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak s_O(\xi)
:=
\frac14\Tr\!\bigl(\sigma_2 e_{1\mu}\mathfrak F^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)-\sigma_1 e_{2\mu}\mathfrak F^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)\bigr).
\label{eq:sO_xi_def}
\end{equation}

Then the diagonal calibration constants reduce to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c
=
\frac{1}{I_{\theta'^3}}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi),
}
\label{eq:Cc_final_factor}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_E(\xi),
}
\label{eq:CE_final_factor}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_O(\xi).
}
\label{eq:CO_final_factor}
\end{equation}

These are the exact one-dimensional factorized forms under the separable shell-adapted basis ansatz.

\section{Further reduction in the constant-envelope limit}

If the transverse envelopes are \(\xi\)-independent and one uses the constant-envelope shell basis
\[
u_a(x)=\frac{1}{\sqrt{V_{\mathrm{cell}}}}\xi_a,
\]
then the projected shell overlaps reduce to primitive-cell Fourier coefficients.
In particular, first-derivative coefficient fields supported on the first BCC shell satisfy
\begin{equation}
\widehat{\mathcal T_j}(G_*)
=
i\Bigl(\sum_m C_{jm}G_{*,m}\Bigr)A_{G_*},
\label{eq:first_shell_fourier_support}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
W^\alpha=\widehat{\mathcal T^\alpha}(G_*)\,s^\alpha.
\label{eq:constant_env_W}
\end{equation}

So in the simplest constant-envelope reduction,
\[
\mathfrak s_c,\ \mathfrak s_E,\ \mathfrak s_O
\]
collapse to fixed primitive-cell Fourier amplitudes times constant internal traces.

\section{Vanishing mechanisms}

The factorized formulas \eqref{eq:Cc_final_factor}--\eqref{eq:CO_final_factor} show that a calibration constant can vanish for three logically distinct reasons.

\subsection*{(i) Radial cancellation}
Even if the microscopic seed exists, the weighted defect overlap may vanish:
\begin{equation}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^m\,\mathfrak s(\xi)=0.
\label{eq:radial_cancel}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{(ii) Primitive-cell Fourier cancellation}
The \(Q=G_*\) primitive-cell Fourier overlap may vanish:
\begin{equation}
\mathfrak F^\mu_{ab;(u)}(\xi)\equiv 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\text{the }G_*\text{-harmonic does not couple to the chosen Bloch pair.}
\label{eq:fourier_cancel}
\end{equation}
In the first-shell derivative case this can happen when the coefficient tensor annihilates \(G_*\):
\[
\sum_m C_{jm}G_{*,m}=0.
\]

\subsection*{(iii) Internal Pauli orthogonality}
The internal matrix overlap may vanish after the shell Pauli trace:
\begin{equation}
\Tr(\sigma_3\hat n_\mu \mathfrak F^\mu_{(c)})=0,
\qquad
\Tr(\sigma_1 e_{1\mu}\mathfrak F^\mu_{(E)}+\sigma_2 e_{2\mu}\mathfrak F^\mu_{(E)})=0,
\qquad
\Tr(\sigma_2 e_{1\mu}\mathfrak F^\mu_{(O)}-\sigma_1 e_{2\mu}\mathfrak F^\mu_{(O)})=0.
\label{eq:pauli_orthogonality}
\end{equation}

Therefore the final microscopic calibration problem is completely reduced to checking whether each desired seed survives these three filters.

\section{Connection to the branch-level coefficient point}

For the present refined locked \(+\) Class II branch, the transport-side point is already explicit:
\[
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2,
\qquad
g_E=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_E^{(0)},
\qquad
g_O=\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}(j\!\cdot\!k)\Lambda_O^{(0)}.
\]
Hence the physical reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O,
}
\label{eq:coeff_after_factor}
\end{equation}
with \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) given by \eqref{eq:Cc_final_factor}--\eqref{eq:CO_final_factor}.

\section{Honest status}

The exact folded-Bragg overlap problem is now reduced as far as one can reduce it analytically without inserting an explicit Bloch wave basis.

What remains open is no longer conceptual:
it is the direct evaluation of the scalar kernel functions
\[
\mathfrak s_c(\xi),\qquad
\mathfrak s_E(\xi),\qquad
\mathfrak s_O(\xi)
\]
for the actual refined locked microscopic Bloch frame.

\section{Final Summary}

The exact folded-Bragg calibration starts from
\[
(M^\mu_{(u)})_{ab}
=
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
\overline{u_a^+(x)}\,V^\mu_{(u)}(x)\,u_b^-(x),
\qquad
u\in\{c,E,O\}.
\]

With the normalized unit-channel inputs
\[
V^\mu_{(c)}=\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(E)}=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(O)}=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
the diagonal calibration constants are extracted by Pauli traces of the shell-adapted components.

Under the separable shell-adapted Bloch basis
\[
u_a^\pm(x)=f_\pm(\xi)\,\chi_a^\pm(x_\perp,\xi),
\]
the calibration integrals factorize into
\[
\text{radial overlap} \times \text{primitive-cell Fourier overlap} \times \text{internal Pauli overlap}.
\]

More precisely,
\[
\boxed{
C_c
=
\frac{1}{I_{\theta'^3}}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi),
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_E(\xi),
\qquad
C_O
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_O(\xi).
}
\]

Thus a calibration constant can vanish for exactly three distinct reasons:

\[
\boxed{
\text{(i) radial cancellation,}
\qquad
\text{(ii) primitive-cell Fourier cancellation,}
\qquad
\text{(iii) internal Pauli orthogonality.}
}
\]

In the first-shell derivative case, the Fourier obstruction is explicit:
\[
\widehat{\mathcal T_j}(G_*)
=
i\Bigl(\sum_m C_{jm}G_{*,m}\Bigr)A_{G_*},
\]
so vanishing occurs if the coefficient tensor annihilates \(G_*\).

Therefore the final microscopic calibration problem has been reduced as far as possible without inserting the actual refined locked Bloch wavefunctions:
it is the explicit evaluation of the scalar overlap kernels
\[
\mathfrak s_c(\xi),\qquad
\mathfrak s_E(\xi),\qquad
\mathfrak s_O(\xi).
\]

The physical reduced coefficients remain
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O,
}
\]
with the branch-level transport point already explicit.

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Practical Nonvanishing Criteria for the Final Bloch Calibration}

\section{Short explanation}

The calibration constants \(C_c,C_E,C_O\) were reduced to folded-Bragg overlap integrals.
The next task is not to rewrite those integrals, but to turn them into actual executable nonvanishing criteria.

The key point is that each calibration constant can fail only through three filters:

\begin{enumerate}
\item radial cancellation,
\item primitive-cell Fourier cancellation at \(Q=G_*\),
\item internal Pauli orthogonality.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the final carrier audit becomes a sign/support/overlap problem.

\section{Starting point}

The exact reduced extraction formulas are
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
\qquad
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2),
\label{eq:crit_start_trace}
\end{equation}
together with the exact overlap-normalization layer
\begin{equation}
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
\label{eq:crit_start_norm}
\end{equation}

Inside the explicit seed space, the reduced symbol is nondegenerate if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:crit_seed_nondeg}
\end{equation}

Thus the final Bloch calibration problem is exactly whether the explicit seed channels survive in the true Bloch low-mode frame.

\section{Factorized calibration form}

Under the shell-adapted separable Bloch basis,
\[
u_a^\pm(x)=f_\pm(\xi)\chi_a^\pm(x_\perp,\xi),
\]
the diagonal calibration constants reduce to
\begin{equation}
C_c
=
\frac{1}{I_{\theta'^3}}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi),
\label{eq:Cc_fact_crit}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
C_E
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_E(\xi),
\qquad
C_O
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_O(\xi).
\label{eq:CEO_fact_crit}
\end{equation}

Here:
\begin{itemize}
\item \(f_+f_-\) is the radial/envelope overlap,
\item \(\mathfrak s_c,\mathfrak s_E,\mathfrak s_O\) are the primitive-cell Fourier plus internal Pauli overlap kernels,
\item the normalization denominators \(I_{\theta'^3},I_\theta\) are nonzero by construction.
\end{itemize}

\section{Longitudinal criterion for \texorpdfstring{$C_c\neq 0$}{Cc nonzero}}

\subsection{Necessary condition}

A necessary condition is that the weighted kernel is not identically zero:
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
\label{eq:Cc_necessary}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, at least one longitudinal microscopic overlap must survive.
At the tensor-basis level this is the executable criterion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}=E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:long_basis_criterion}
\end{equation}

At the graded overlap level this is the same condition written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:Jpar3_criterion}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Simple sufficient condition}

A clean sufficient condition is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi)
\text{ has a definite sign on a set of positive measure.}
}
\label{eq:Cc_sufficient_sign}
\end{equation}

Indeed, under \eqref{eq:Cc_sufficient_sign}, the integral \eqref{eq:Cc_fact_crit} cannot cancel to zero.

Thus the longitudinal overlap survives whenever there is

\begin{enumerate}
\item nontrivial radial overlap,
\item nonvanishing \(Q=G_*\) harmonic coupling,
\item nonzero \(\sigma_3\)-projected internal trace,
\end{enumerate}
with no sign-changing cancellation strong enough to kill the integral.

\section{Transverse criterion for \texorpdfstring{$(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0)$}{(CE,CO) nonzero}}

\subsection{Necessary condition}

A necessary condition is that at least one transverse weighted kernel is not identically zero:
\begin{equation}
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_E(\xi)\not\equiv 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_O(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
\label{eq:CEO_necessary}
\end{equation}

At the corrected microscopic level, this requires a nontrivial derivative-resolved shell source:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}
\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:transverse_deriv_necessary}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Minimal sufficient mechanisms}

The minimal nonvanishing mechanisms for the transverse sector are exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(a) derivative on the shell phase,}
}
\label{eq:trans_a}
\end{equation}
\[
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J})(G_*;0)\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})(G_*;0)\neq 0;
\]

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(b) nontrivial internal-index contraction,}
}
\label{eq:trans_b}
\end{equation}
meaning that the mediator/internal contraction distinguishes the \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2\) channels rather than collapsing to a trivial scalar;

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(c) nontrivial complex intervalley phase data,}
}
\label{eq:trans_c}
\end{equation}
so that the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic does not reduce to the naive vanishing anticommutator structure;

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(d) direct }KK\text{ transverse contribution.}
}
\label{eq:trans_d}
\end{equation}

If at least one of these mechanisms is present and the final Pauli projection is nonzero, then \((C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0)\) can survive.

\subsection{Minimal first-shell sufficient test}

In the explicit folded-Bragg Class II reduction, the full transverse audit compresses to two scalar Fourier overlaps:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:first_shell_two_overlap_test}
\end{equation}

If \eqref{eq:first_shell_two_overlap_test} holds, then the explicit Class II branch realizes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:ab_nonzero_realized}
\end{equation}

Thus, at the practical branch level, \eqref{eq:first_shell_two_overlap_test} is the strongest usable explicit sufficient test for the transverse carrier.

\section{Three-filter decomposition of failure}

The factorized formulas show that failure of a calibration constant can occur only through one of three mechanisms:

\paragraph{(i) radial cancellation}
\[
\int d\xi\, f_+f_-\,\theta'^m\,\mathfrak s(\xi)=0
\]
by sign-changing or oscillatory cancellation in the defect/radial overlap;

\paragraph{(ii) primitive-cell Fourier cancellation}
the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic does not couple to the chosen Bloch pair;

\paragraph{(iii) internal Pauli orthogonality}
the desired \(\sigma_3\), \(\sigma_1\), or \(\sigma_2\) component vanishes after projection.

So the calibration audit is exactly a three-filter survival test.

\section{Practical final acceptance criteria}

\subsection{Diagonal locked case}

If the shell basis is locked and the overlap matrix is diagonal, the current branch passes iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:diag_final_accept}
\end{equation}

\subsection{Practical sufficient version}

A convenient sufficient form is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi)
\text{ has definite nonzero sign on positive measure,}
}
\label{eq:Cc_suff_practical}
\end{equation}
and either
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*)\neq 0
}
\label{eq:CE_suff_practical}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:CO_suff_practical}
\end{equation}

Under these conditions, the explicit branch survives the final Bloch calibration.

\section{Honest status}

At the strongest honest current stage:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the reduced witness architecture is closed;
\item the branch-level transport coefficient point is explicit;
\item the calibration problem is reduced to finite overlap survival tests;
\item the longitudinal side is governed by the basis-overlap / graded-overlap criterion;
\item the transverse side is governed by the derivative-resolved \(JK/KK\) shell audit, with the first-shell two-overlap test as the practical explicit sufficient criterion.
\end{enumerate}

What remains open is not conceptual structure, but the explicit evaluation of the actual overlap kernels in the true refined locked Bloch frame.

\section{Final Summary}

The exact final Bloch calibration problem has now been reduced to explicit nonvanishing criteria.

The reduced witness extraction is
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel),
\qquad
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2),
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2),
\]
with the exact normalization layer
\[
\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
\]

In the explicit seed space, the symbol is nondegenerate if and only if
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Under the factorized shell-adapted Bloch basis,
\[
C_c
=
\frac{1}{I_{\theta'^3}}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi),
\]
\[
C_E
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_E(\xi),
\qquad
C_O
=
\frac{1}{I_\theta}
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,\mathfrak s_O(\xi).
\]

Therefore each calibration constant can fail only through one of three filters:
\[
\boxed{
\text{radial cancellation,}
\qquad
\text{primitive-cell Fourier cancellation,}
\qquad
\text{internal Pauli orthogonality.}
}
\]

For the longitudinal channel, an executable criterion is
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j\neq 0,
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi)\neq 0.
}
\]

For the transverse channel, the honest microscopic frontier is not the naive local \(JK\) term, but the derivative-resolved shell audit
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}.
}
\]

The minimal transverse nonvanishing mechanisms are:
\[
\boxed{
\text{(a) derivative on the shell phase,}
\quad
\text{(b) nontrivial internal contraction,}
\quad
\text{(c) nontrivial complex intervalley phase,}
\quad
\text{(d) direct }KK\text{ transverse piece.}
}
\]

In the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, this compresses to the practical sufficient test
\[
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*)\neq 0,
}
\]
which implies
\[
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Hence the sharp practical acceptance criterion for the current branch is:

\[
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0
}
\]
via a nonvanishing longitudinal overlap, and
\[
\boxed{
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0)
}
\]
via the derivative-resolved transverse shell audit, or in the minimal explicit reduction, via the two first-shell Fourier overlap tests.

Thus the remaining frontier is no longer conceptual.
It is the explicit evaluation of the overlap kernels and their sign/support structure in the true refined locked Bloch frame.

\section{Final Decision Tree for the Refined Locked + Class II Working Branch}

\section{Goal}

We now convert the current refined locked \(+\) Class II program into a final pass/fail decision tree.

The purpose is to separate:

\begin{enumerate}
\item support gates that must hold before the shell Dirac carrier is meaningful,
\item actual carrier-survival gates,
\item mass-protection gates,
\item the downstream one-defect/one-mode realization criterion.
\end{enumerate}

The logic is sequential:
\[
\text{Gate 1} \Longrightarrow \text{Gate 2} \Longrightarrow \text{Gate 3} \Longrightarrow \text{Gate 4},
\]
and only after all four pass does one proceed to the protected-mode criterion.

\section{Gate 1: Remote-gap support theorem}

\subsection*{Criterion}

The first mandatory gate is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G1_remote_gap}
\end{equation}

The current explicit benchmark side is
\begin{equation}
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}
=
\min\Biggl\{
4K-|r_*|,
\;
\sqrt{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2(q_*-\rho)^2},
\;
q_*^2\left|
(\lambda+\mu)+\frac{g^2}{M_\sigma^2+c_\sigma^2q_*^2}
\right|,
\;
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
\Biggr\},
\label{eq:G1_benchmark}
\end{equation}
while the residual side is bounded by
\begin{equation}
\eta_{R,\rho}
\le
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{tail},\rho}
+
\eta_{\mathrm{diag},\rho},
\label{eq:G1_residual}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\eta_{R,\rho}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le
2\sum_{(ab)\in\mathfrak P_6}
\left[
\mathcal D_{ab,\rho}
+
\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JJ}
+
\frac{|\alpha_X\beta_X|}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{JK}
+
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\mathcal M_{ab,\rho}^{KK}
\right].
\label{eq:G1_residual_tr}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Meaning}

If Gate 1 passes, the enriched low slot is spectrally isolated from the remote sector.
This is a support theorem, not the main frontier.

If Gate 1 fails, then spectral isolation is not established, and all later shell-carrier statements are unsupported.

\subsection*{Current honest status}

The benchmark-side frontier has been reduced to one finite eigenvalue problem:
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}
-
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr},\rho}^{(N)}.
\]
So Gate 1 is operationally finite.

\section{Gate 2: Longitudinal survival}

\subsection*{Criterion}

The shell-extracted longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel)=C_c\,g_c.
}
\label{eq:G2_lambda}
\end{equation}

Therefore the carrier requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
g_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_basic}
\end{equation}

Inside the explicit Class II transport truncation,
\[
g_c\propto c_\parallel,
\]
and in the current refined working branch
\[
g_c=\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}j^2.
\]

At the basis-overlap level, a practical executable criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_basis_overlap}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, at the graded/radial level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_radial_overlap}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Sufficient form}

A clean sufficient condition is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi)
\text{ has definite nonzero sign on a set of positive measure.}
}
\label{eq:G2_sign_sufficient}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Meaning}

If Gate 2 fails, then \(\lambda_\parallel=0\), so the branch does not realize the required longitudinal Dirac carrier.
This is not a minor normalization issue; it kills the shell Dirac architecture.

\section{Gate 3: Transverse survival}

\subsection*{Criterion}

The shell-extracted transverse coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M_1+\sigma_2M_2)=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M_1-\sigma_1M_2)=C_O\,g_O.
}
\label{eq:G3_ab}
\end{equation}

Hence the carrier requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0)
\quad\text{and}\quad
(g_E,g_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_basic}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Honest microscopic frontier}

A naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear vanishes because
\[
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}=\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\]
Therefore the real microscopic frontier is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G3_true_frontier}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Minimal explicit sufficient mechanisms}

The minimal nonvanishing mechanisms are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item derivative on the shell phase,
\item nontrivial internal-index contraction,
\item nontrivial complex intervalley phase data,
\item direct \(KK\) transverse contribution.
\end{enumerate}

In the folded-Bragg first-shell reduction, this compresses to the explicit sufficient test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G3_first_shell_test}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Meaning}

If Gate 3 fails, then the branch does not realize a genuine two-direction transverse Dirac witness.
This does not necessarily refute the reduced architecture itself, but it shows that the current microscopic branch is insufficient.

\section{Gate 4: Mass protection}

\subsection*{Criterion}

For the doubled Dirac block,
\[
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),
\]
the exact constant Dirac-mass space is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_mass_space}
\end{equation}

Let
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in \mathrm{Herm}(4):U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}
\]
be the residual-symmetry allowed constant algebra.
Mass protection requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_exact}
\end{equation}

\subsection*{Sufficient mechanism}

It is sufficient to prove exact residual valley symmetry
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U(1)_V
\quad\text{or already}\quad
\mathbb Z_2^V.
}
\label{eq:G4_valley_sym}
\end{equation}

With
\[
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\]
the two mass generators rotate nontrivially under \(U(1)_V\), and are odd already under \(\mathbb Z_2^V\).
Therefore either symmetry excludes the mass space.

\subsection*{Meaning}

If Gate 4 fails, then even if Gates 1--3 pass, the doubled Dirac block is not protected against a constant symmetry-allowed mass.
So the branch is not an acceptable robust massless Dirac realization.

\section{Post-acceptance Gate 5: one-defect / one-protected-mode realization}

Only after Gates 1--4 pass does it make sense to test the downstream protected-mode criterion.

In the currently cleanest operational form, the sufficient criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,\qquad
\alpha>0,\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\label{eq:G5_post_acceptance}
\end{equation}

This is not part of branch acceptance itself.
It is the next physical realization step once the branch has already been accepted as a valid microscopic carrier.

\section{Final decision tree}

The final decision tree is:

\paragraph{Gate 1.}
Check \eqref{eq:G1_remote_gap}.
If false:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Reject as unsupported: spectral isolation not established.}
}
\]

If true, continue.

\paragraph{Gate 2.}
Check \eqref{eq:G2_basic}, preferably via \eqref{eq:G2_basis_overlap} or \eqref{eq:G2_radial_overlap}.
If false:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Reject: no longitudinal Dirac witness.}
}
\]

If true, continue.

\paragraph{Gate 3.}
Check \eqref{eq:G3_basic}, with the honest frontier \eqref{eq:G3_true_frontier} and practical explicit test \eqref{eq:G3_first_shell_test}.
If false:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Reject current branch as transversely insufficient.}
}
\]

If true, continue.

\paragraph{Gate 4.}
Check \eqref{eq:G4_exact}, preferably by proving \eqref{eq:G4_valley_sym}.
If false:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Reject as unprotected: constant Dirac mass may survive.}
}
\]

If true:
\[
\boxed{
\text{Accept the current refined locked + Class II branch as a viable microscopic massless Dirac carrier.}
}
\]

Then, and only then, proceed to Gate 5 \eqref{eq:G5_post_acceptance}.

\section{Final Summary}

The refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch is accepted or rejected by the following final decision tree.

\paragraph{Gate 1: remote-gap support.}
Require
\[
\boxed{
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
}
\]
If this fails, spectral isolation is not established, so all later shell-carrier statements are unsupported.

\paragraph{Gate 2: longitudinal survival.}
Require
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel)=C_c g_c\neq 0.
}
\]
Practical executable criteria are:
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j\neq 0,
}
\]
or equivalently
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi)\neq 0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Gate 3: transverse survival.}
Require
\[
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,\quad \beta=C_O g_O.
}
\]
The honest microscopic frontier is
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}\neq 0.
}
\]
In the explicit folded-Bragg reduction, a practical sufficient test is

\paragraph{Gate 4: mass protection.}

Acceptance requires

}

A sufficient mechanism is exact residual valley symmetry
\[

U(1)_V
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathbb Z_2^V.

\paragraph{Acceptance verdict.}
If Gates 1--4 all pass, then

If any gate fails, the branch is rejected for the corresponding reason:
unsupported, longitudinally insufficient, transversely insufficient, or unprotected.

\section{Final Master Checklist for the Refined Locked + Class II Working Branch}

\section{Purpose}

The purpose of this checklist is not to introduce new structure, but to classify every required gate in the current working branch into exactly one of the following three statuses:

\[
\boxed{

\text{finite computation left},\qquad
\text{structurally open}.
}
\]

Here:

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{closed} means the theorem-level structure is complete and no additional conceptual input is needed;
\item \textbf{finite computation left} means the criterion is already exact, but the concrete branch values still have to be evaluated;
\item \textbf{structurally open} means an honest nontrivial conceptual caveat remains, so one must not overstate closure.
\end{itemize}

\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{G4: finite computation left}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{G5: finite computation left after branch acceptance}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Priority order for the next calculation}

The correct next order is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item Gate 2: longitudinal survival \(C_c\neq 0\);
\item Gate 3: transverse survival \((C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0)\);
\item Gate 4: mass protection;
\item Gate 1: remote-gap verification in the same parameter regime;
\item Gate 5: one-defect / one-mode realization.
\end{enumerate}

The reason is simple:

\begin{itemize}
\item Gates 2 and 3 decide whether there is any shell Dirac carrier at all;
\item Gate 4 decides whether that carrier is robustly massless;
\item Gate 1 is a support theorem that must ultimately hold in the same regime, but it is no longer the main conceptual frontier;
\item Gate 5 only makes sense after acceptance of the carrier branch.
\end{itemize}

\section{Final Summary}

The refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch is now best organized by the following master checklist.

\paragraph{Gate 1: remote-gap support}
\[
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{fin}}>\eta_{R,\rho}.
\]
Status:
\[
\boxed{\text{finite computation left}.}
\]
Reason:
the theorem-level structure is already closed, but the concrete branch sign has not yet been verified.

\paragraph{Gate 2: longitudinal survival}
\[
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M_\parallel)=C_c g_c\neq 0.
\]
Executable criteria:
\[
\exists A:\ E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j\neq 0,
\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]
Status:
\[
\boxed{\text{finite computation left}.}
\]

\paragraph{Gate 3: transverse survival}
\[
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0),
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,\quad \beta=C_O g_O.
\]
Honest microscopic frontier:
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}\neq 0.
\]
Practical branch-level sufficient test:
\[
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq 0.
\]
Status:
\[
\boxed{
\text{finite computation left on the working branch, with a structural caveat for unconditional closure.}
}
\]

\paragraph{Gate 4: mass protection}
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
\qquad
\mathcal M_D=\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}\{\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2\}.
\]
Sufficient mechanism:
\[
U(1)_V
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathbb Z_2^V.
\]
Status:
\[
\boxed{\text{finite computation left}.}
\]

\paragraph{Gate 5: one-defect / one-mode}
This is a post-acceptance downstream criterion, not a branch-acceptance gate.
In the most practical case it reduces to
\[
\boxed{
-1<R_c<1,\qquad
\alpha>0,\qquad
\mu_\infty>0,\qquad
\Delta_{\mathrm{bench},\rho}^{\mathrm{full}}>\eta_{\mathrm{rem},\rho}.
}
\]
Status:
\[
\boxed{\text{finite computation left after branch acceptance}.}
\]

Therefore the strongest honest current global verdict is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{G1: finite computation left,}
}
\]

\text{G2: finite computation left,}

\text{G4: finite computation left,}

Hence the next actual priority order is:

\text{Gate 2} \;\longrightarrow\; \text{Gate 3} \;\longrightarrow\; \text{Gate 4} \;\longrightarrow\; \text{Gate 1} \;\longrightarrow\; \text{Gate 5}.

This is because Gates 2 and 3 decide whether the shell Dirac carrier exists at all, Gate 4 decides whether it is protected, Gate 1 is the support theorem to be verified in the same regime, and Gate 5 is meaningful only after acceptance.
