\section{Gate 2 Checklist: Actual Longitudinal Survival Audit}

\section{Purpose}

Gate 2 asks whether the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch truly carries a nonzero longitudinal primitive shell channel.

The exact question is:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0\ ?
}
\]

At the current stage this is no longer a conceptual PDE question.
It is a finite microscopic audit that can be organized into four nested levels:

\begin{enumerate}
\item basis-level overlap audit,
\item shell-seed coefficient audit,
\item graded/radial overlap audit,
\item final Bloch calibration audit.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Exact longitudinal target}

The canonical primitive longitudinal shell target is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_\parallel:\quad
N^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=N^2_{ij}=0.
}
\label{eq:G2_target}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the shell covector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}
=
\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta_{a3}.
}
\label{eq:G2_target_covector}
\end{equation}

The primitive transport operator representative is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel)}(\xi)
=
\theta'(\xi)(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}\,n^\mu
=
\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:G2_primitive_seed}
\end{equation}

Its reduced witness is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,c_\parallel\,I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_lambda_from_cpar}
\end{equation}

Therefore the longitudinal question is exactly whether the full microscopic theory generates a nonzero coefficient in front of this primitive odd singlet channel.

\section{Level A: basis-level overlap audit}

Let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}
\otimes
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}
\otimes
U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the actual microscopic transport space extracted from the full refined locked linearization.

Choose any basis
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d
\]
of \(V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\).
Define the longitudinal overlaps
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{\parallel A}
:=
\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle
=
E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j.
}
\label{eq:G2_ellA}
\end{equation}

Then the exact basis-level longitudinal criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_basis_criterion}
\end{equation}

This is already a complete finite linear-algebra test.

\paragraph{Checklist A.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Fix the shell pair \(G_*\) and the adapted frame \((e_1,e_2,\hat n)\).
\item Extract the actual microscopic transport basis \(\{E_A\}\).
\item Compute
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j
\]
for every basis element.
\item If all \(\ell_{\parallel A}=0\), Gate 2 fails immediately.
\item If at least one \(\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0\), proceed.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level B: shell-seed coefficient audit}

Decompose the actual induced shell tensor onto the explicit seed space:
\begin{equation}
P_{\mathrm{seed}}N_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}B_\parallel
+
c_I^{(\mathrm{mic})}B_I
+
c_J^{(\mathrm{mic})}B_J.
\label{eq:G2_seed_projection}
\end{equation}

The basis-overlap audit is equivalent to the nonvanishing of the longitudinal seed coefficient:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_basis_to_seed}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0
}
\label{eq:G2_seed_to_lambda}
\end{equation}
provided the overlap normalization is nonzero.

\paragraph{Checklist B.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Project the actual shell transport tensor onto \(V_{\mathrm{seed}}=\mathrm{span}\{B_\parallel,B_I,B_J\}\).
\item Read off \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\).
\item If \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}=0\), Gate 2 fails.
\item If \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0\), proceed.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level C: graded/radial overlap audit}

At the projected defect-profile level, the same condition is encoded in the \(\sigma_3\)-component of the traceless quadratic response:
\[
s_3(\xi).
\]
The exact graded overlap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\; f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi).
}
\label{eq:G2_Jpar}
\end{equation}

The graded criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_graded_criterion}
\end{equation}

A simple sufficient condition is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi)
\text{ has definite nonzero sign on a set of positive measure.}
}
\label{eq:G2_sign_suff}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Checklist C.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Construct the low-mode radial profiles \(f_\pm(\xi)\).
\item Extract the \(\sigma_3\)-projected kernel \(s_3(\xi)\) or \(\mathfrak s_c(\xi)\).
\item Evaluate
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi).
\]
\item If this vanishes by sign cancellation, Gate 2 fails.
\item If it is nonzero, proceed.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level D: final Bloch calibration}

Even after the longitudinal seed survives, the actual physical coefficient still carries the Bloch overlap factor:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c.
}
\label{eq:G2_bloch_norm}
\end{equation}

In the current working branch, the transport-side coefficient \(g_c\) is already explicit.
So the remaining final Gate-2 condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_Cc_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Using the normalized longitudinal unit input,
\[
V^\mu_{(c)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\]
the calibration overlap is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_c
=
\frac{1}{2I_{\theta'^3}}
\Tr\!\left[
\sigma_3
\int_{\mathrm{cell}} d^3x\;
e^{-iG_*\cdot x}\,
U_+^\dagger(x)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3\,U_-(x)
\right].
}
\label{eq:G2_Cc_formula}
\end{equation}

Thus Gate 2 finally passes iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
C_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_final_pass}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Checklist D.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Build the normalized \(c\)-unit input \(V^\mu_{(c)}\).
\item Compute the folded-Bragg overlap matrix \(M^\parallel_{(c)}\).
\item Evaluate
\[
C_c=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)}).
\]
\item If \(C_c=0\), Gate 2 fails at the calibration layer.
\item If \(C_c\neq 0\), Gate 2 passes completely.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Gate-2 decision tree}

The complete Gate-2 decision tree is:

\paragraph{Step 1.}
Check whether
\[
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0.
\]
If not, reject: no longitudinal microscopic seed exists.

\paragraph{Step 2.}
Check whether
\[
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
\]
If not, reject: the full shell projection kills the primitive longitudinal channel.

\paragraph{Step 3.}
Check whether
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]
If not, reject: the defect/graded overlap cancels the longitudinal seed.

\paragraph{Step 4.}
Check whether
\[
C_c\neq 0.
\]
If not, reject: the Bloch-frame overlap kills the surviving longitudinal seed.

\paragraph{Final verdict.}
Only if all four steps pass do we conclude
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_final_verdict}
\end{equation}

\section{Status}

At the present stage, every ingredient of this decision tree is already structurally fixed.

Therefore Gate 2 is not conceptually open.
It is an exact finite executable audit.

What remains is only the actual evaluation of
\[
\ell_{\parallel A},\qquad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})},\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)},\qquad
C_c
\]
for the true refined locked microscopic transport basis.

\section{Final Summary}

Gate 2 asks whether the primitive longitudinal shell channel truly survives in the full refined locked microscopic transport space.

The canonical longitudinal target is
\[
B_\parallel:\quad
N^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=N^2_{ij}=0,
\]
equivalently
\[
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}=\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta_{a3}.
\]

The exact basis-level overlap audit is
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{\parallel A}
=
E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0.
}
\]

This is equivalent to the shell-seed survival condition
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
}
\]

At the graded/radial level, the same survival question becomes
\[
\boxed{
J_\parallel^{(3)}
=
\int d\xi\, f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\,s_3(\xi)\neq 0.
}
\]

A simple sufficient condition is that
\[
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi)
\]
has definite nonzero sign on a set of positive measure.

Finally, the actual physical longitudinal coefficient carries the Bloch overlap factor:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c,
}
\]
so the final calibration condition is
\[
\boxed{
C_c\neq 0.
}
\]

Therefore the complete Gate-2 pass condition is
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\Longleftrightarrow
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0,
\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0,
\qquad
C_c\neq 0.
}
\]

Only when all of these hold can one conclude
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\]

Thus Gate 2 is not conceptually open.
It is an exact finite executable audit of:
\[
\ell_{\parallel A},\qquad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})},\qquad
J_\parallel^{(3)},\qquad
C_c.
\]

\section{Gate 3 Checklist: Actual Transverse Survival Audit}

\section{Purpose}

Gate 3 asks whether the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch truly carries nonzero transverse shell witnesses.

The exact question is:
\[
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0)\ ?
}
\]

At the present stage this should be organized into four nested layers:

\begin{enumerate}
\item shell-adapted witness projection level,
\item derivative-resolved microscopic shell audit,
\item folded-Bragg first-shell compressed test,
\item final Bloch calibration audit.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Exact transverse target}

The exact shell-adapted transverse witness projections are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E
\propto
\frac12
\left[
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(\Sigma_1\,\mathcal S_{1}\right)
+
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(\Sigma_2\,\mathcal S_{2}\right)
\right],
}
\label{eq:G3_cE_target}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_O
\propto
\frac12
\left[
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(\Sigma_2\,\mathcal S_{1}\right)
-
\operatorname{Tr}\!\left(\Sigma_1\,\mathcal S_{2}\right)
\right].
}
\label{eq:G3_cO_target}
\end{equation}

The reduced witness coefficients are then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
\qquad
I_\theta\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G3_reduced_dict}
\end{equation}

Thus the transverse question is exactly whether the full microscopic theory generates a nonzero coefficient in at least one of these two shell-adapted transverse channels.

\section{Level A: honest microscopic frontier}

The first fact that must be fixed is negative:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the naive local real Hermitian }JK\text{ bilinear vanishes.}
}
\label{eq:G3_naive_zero}
\end{equation}

Indeed, in the minimal shell-adapted form,
\[
J\sim j\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
K\sim k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2,
\]
so the simplest Hermitian bilinear reduces to
\[
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)
+
(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
=
k_E\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}+k_O\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\]

Therefore the genuine microscopic transverse frontier is not the undifferentiated local \(JK\) term, but the derivative-resolved shell audit
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:G3_true_frontier}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Checklist A.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Do \emph{not} use the naive statement \(JK\Rightarrow\) transverse automatically.
\item Construct the shell-derivative blocks
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0}.
\]
\item Pauli-decompose their shell matrices.
\item If both derivative blocks have zero \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2\) projections, Gate 3 fails immediately.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level B: exact witness decomposition}

After Pauli decomposition,
\begin{equation}
c_E=c_E^{(JK)}+c_E^{(KK)},
\qquad
c_O=c_O^{(JK)}+c_O^{(KK)},
\label{eq:G3_total_cEcO}
\end{equation}
since pure \(JJ\) is axial only and does not contribute to the transverse witness pair.

Hence the exact shell-level transverse criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_shell_criterion}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_reduced_criterion}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Checklist B.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Compute the shell-derivative Pauli coefficients in the \(JK\) and \(KK\) sectors.
\item Form
\[
c_E=c_E^{(JK)}+c_E^{(KK)},\qquad
c_O=c_O^{(JK)}+c_O^{(KK)}.
\]
\item If both vanish, Gate 3 fails.
\item If at least one is nonzero, proceed.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level C: minimal nonvanishing mechanisms}

The transverse sector can survive only if at least one of the following is nontrivial:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(a) derivative on the shell phase,}
}
\end{equation}
\[
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal J})(G_*;0)\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
(\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat{\mathcal K})(G_*;0)\neq 0;
\]

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(b) nontrivial internal-index contraction,}
}
\end{equation}
meaning that the mediator/internal contraction distinguishes the \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2\) channels;

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(c) nontrivial complex intervalley phase data,}
}
\end{equation}
so that the \(Q=G_*\) harmonic does not collapse to a pure anticommutator;

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{(d) direct }KK\text{ transverse piece.}
}
\end{equation}

These are not optional interpretations; they are the minimal ways to bypass the naive local anticommutation obstruction.

\paragraph{Checklist C.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Check whether the shell derivative acts nontrivially on the \(G_*\)-harmonic.
\item Check whether the internal contraction over mediator labels is genuinely anisotropic in the \(\Sigma_1,\Sigma_2\) plane.
\item Check whether intervalley phase data are complex/nontrivial.
\item Check whether the \(KK\) block already contains a direct transverse Pauli component.
\item If none of these mechanisms is present, Gate 3 fails.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level D: folded-Bragg compressed test}

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, the derivative bookkeeping compresses to the exact Fourier convolution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
}
\label{eq:G3_Talpha_exact}
\end{equation}

In the minimal first-shell-dominant channel, this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)\propto iA_{G_*}(C_\alpha\cdot G_*),
\qquad \alpha=1,2.
\label{eq:G3_first_shell_reduce}
\end{equation}

Therefore the practical explicit sufficient test becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*)\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G3_two_overlap_test}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:G3_two_overlap_test}, the explicit Class II branch realizes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_ab_realized}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Checklist D.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Compute the first-shell Fourier amplitude \(A_{G_*}\).
\item Compute the projected vectors \(C_1,C_2\).
\item Evaluate
\[
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*),\qquad A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*).
\]
\item If both vanish, Gate 3 fails on the working branch.
\item If at least one is nonzero, Gate 3 survives on the working branch.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level E: final Bloch calibration}

Even after the transport-side transverse seed survives, the actual physical coefficients still carry the Bloch overlap factors:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=C_E\,g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O\,g_O.
}
\label{eq:G3_bloch_norm}
\end{equation}

Therefore the final calibration condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_CECO_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Using the normalized \(E\)- and \(O\)-unit inputs,
\[
V^\mu_{(E)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\qquad
V^\mu_{(O)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)}{I_\theta}J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
the exact calibration overlaps are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_E
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)}),
}
\label{eq:G3_CE_formula}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_O
=
\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)}).
}
\label{eq:G3_CO_formula}
\end{equation}

Thus Gate 3 completely passes iff
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0)
\quad\text{and}\quad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_final_pass}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Checklist E.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Build the normalized \(E\)- and \(O\)-unit inputs.
\item Compute the folded-Bragg overlap matrices \(M^1_{(E)},M^2_{(E)}\) and \(M^1_{(O)},M^2_{(O)}\).
\item Evaluate
\[
C_E=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_1M^1_{(E)}+\sigma_2M^2_{(E)}),
\qquad
C_O=\frac14\Tr(\sigma_2M^1_{(O)}-\sigma_1M^2_{(O)}).
\]
\item If both vanish, Gate 3 fails at the calibration layer.
\item If at least one is nonzero, Gate 3 passes completely.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Gate-3 decision tree}

The complete Gate-3 decision tree is:

\paragraph{Step 1.}
Reject the naive undifferentiated local \(JK\) criterion.

\paragraph{Step 2.}
Compute the derivative-resolved shell blocks
\[
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0}.
\]
If both have zero transverse Pauli projections, reject.

\paragraph{Step 3.}
Compute the shell witness pair
\[
(c_E,c_O).
\]
If both vanish, reject.

\paragraph{Step 4.}
On the explicit folded-Bragg branch, evaluate
\[
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*),\qquad A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*).
\]
If both vanish, reject on the working branch.

\paragraph{Step 5.}
Compute the Bloch calibration overlaps
\[
(C_E,C_O).
\]
If both vanish, reject at the calibration layer.

\paragraph{Final verdict.}
Only if all previous steps pass do we conclude
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_final_verdict}
\end{equation}

\section{Status}

At the present stage, Gate 3 has two distinct logical statuses:

\begin{enumerate}
\item as a working-branch acceptance problem, it is already reduced to finite explicit computations;
\item as a fully unconditional microscopic theorem, it still carries the honest derivative-resolved \(JK/KK\) caveat.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore Gate 3 is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{finite computation left on the working branch, with a structural caveat for unconditional closure.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

Gate 3 asks whether the transverse witness pair truly survives:
\[
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

The exact shell-level transverse coefficients are
\[
c_E=c_E^{(JK)}+c_E^{(KK)},
\qquad
c_O=c_O^{(JK)}+c_O^{(KK)},
\]
and the reduced dictionary is
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\]

However, the naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear vanishes:
\[
\boxed{
\text{naive local }JK=0
\quad\text{by}\quad
\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}=\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
}
\]

Therefore the honest microscopic frontier is
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0}.
}
\]

The minimal nonvanishing mechanisms are:
\[
\boxed{
\text{(a) derivative on the shell phase,}
\quad
\text{(b) nontrivial internal contraction,}
\quad
\text{(c) nontrivial complex intervalley phase,}
\quad
\text{(d) direct }KK\text{ transverse piece.}
}
\]

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, this compresses to the finite practical test
\[
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*)\neq 0.
}
\]

After transport-side survival, the final Bloch calibration layer is
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O,
}
\]
so the last acceptance condition is
\[
\boxed{
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0).
}
\]

Therefore the complete Gate-3 pass condition is
\[
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq (0,0),
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq (0,0),
}
\]
with the first-shell explicit sufficient version
\[
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\cdot G_*)\neq 0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\cdot G_*)\neq 0.
}
\]

Thus Gate 3 is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{finite computation left on the explicit working branch,}
}
\]
but also
\[
\boxed{
\text{still carrying the honest derivative-resolved \(JK/KK\) caveat as an unconditional microscopic statement.}
}
\]

\section{Gate 4 Checklist: Actual Mass-Protection Audit}

\section{Purpose}

Gate 4 asks whether the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch is protected against all symmetry-allowed constant Dirac masses.

The exact question is:
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}\ ?
}
\]

At the present stage this is no longer a conceptual emergence problem.
It is a finite residual-symmetry audit on the isolated doubled shell block.

\section{Exact mass-space classification}

Once the isolated doubled shell carrier exists, the local Dirac block has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i).
}
\label{eq:G4_HD}
\end{equation}

The full little-group-scalar constant Hermitian operator space is
\begin{equation}
K
=
a_0\,\mathbf 1_4
+
a_3\,\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_1\,\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2
+
m_2\,\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\label{eq:G4_Kspace}
\end{equation}

Among these, the genuine constant Dirac-mass space is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_massspace}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact mass-protection problem is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
}
\label{eq:G4_exactcriterion}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}.
\label{eq:G4_Ares}
\end{equation}

\section{Level A: reject insufficient shortcuts}

Two common shortcuts are \emph{not} sufficient:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{little-group scalarity only } \Longrightarrow \text{ not enough,}
}
\label{eq:G4_not_scalar_only}
\end{equation}
because both mass generators remain allowed;

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{opposite-valley matching only } \Longrightarrow \text{ not enough.}
}
\label{eq:G4_not_valleymatch_only}
\end{equation}

Opposite-valley matching may fix doubling,
\[
h_-(p)=-h_+(-p),
\]
but it does not remove
\[
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2.
\]

\paragraph{Checklist A.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Do \emph{not} count little-group scalarity as a proof of mass protection.
\item Do \emph{not} count opposite-valley matching as a proof of mass protection.
\item Start only from the exact criterion \eqref{eq:G4_exactcriterion}.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level B: sufficient residual symmetry mechanisms}

A sufficient mechanism is exact residual valley \(U(1)_V\).
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta:=e^{\,i\theta Q_V/2}.
}
\label{eq:G4_QV}
\end{equation}

Since
\begin{equation}
[Q_V,H_D(p)]=0,
\label{eq:G4_QV_comm_HD}
\end{equation}
the doubled kinetic block is compatible with residual valley symmetry.

Now
\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
\cos\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\sin\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\label{eq:G4_tauxrot}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
U_\theta(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)U_\theta^{-1}
=
-\sin\theta\,(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)
+
\cos\theta\,(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:G4_tauyrot}
\end{equation}

Hence no nonzero element of \(\mathcal M_D\) is invariant under all \(\theta\), so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_U1_forbid}
\end{equation}

The weaker remnant
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_V:=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
S_V^2=\mathbf 1_4
}
\label{eq:G4_Z2_generator}
\end{equation}
already suffices, because
\begin{equation}
S_V(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2),
\qquad
S_V(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2)S_V^{-1}
=
-(\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2).
\label{eq:G4_Z2_forbid}
\end{equation}
Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:G4_Z2_forbid_exact}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Checklist B.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Determine whether the isolated doubled shell block preserves exact \(Q_V\).
\item If exact \(U(1)_V\) survives, Gate 4 passes immediately.
\item If only the discrete remnant \(S_V\) survives, Gate 4 still passes.
\item If neither survives, continue to Level C.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level C: explicit residual-algebra audit}

If exact \(U(1)_V\) or \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) is not manifest, one must compute the full residual constant operator algebra
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}
\]
directly on the isolated doubled block.

The exact audit is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item list all residual symmetries of the corrected \(4\times4\) shell block;
\item compute the constant Hermitian operators commuting with all of them;
\item intersect the resulting algebra with \(\mathcal M_D\).
\end{enumerate}

If
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
\]
Gate 4 passes.
If not, Gate 4 fails.

\paragraph{Checklist C.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Extract the exact residual group \(G_{\mathrm{res}}\) of the corrected isolated shell block.
\item Compute
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K,\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}.
\]
\item Compute the intersection
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D.
\]
\item If the intersection is nonzero, Gate 4 fails.
\item If it is zero, Gate 4 passes.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level D: remote-sector compatibility audit}

Mass protection must survive the remote-sector elimination as well.
So it is not enough that the principal kinetic block preserve the residual symmetry;
the full corrected microscopic constant piece must preserve it too.

Operationally, one must verify that the constant corrected block and the remote self-energy preserve the same residual generator.
In the simplest theorem-level form, this is the requirement that the full corrected constant sector remain \(Q_V\)-invariant.

Thus Gate 4 is not only a bare-shell test.
It is a test of the corrected isolated block after Schur-complement elimination.

\paragraph{Checklist D.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Compute the constant corrected shell block \(\delta H_{\mathrm{const}}\).
\item Compute the zero-momentum self-energy \(\Sigma(0,0)\) from remote-sector elimination.
\item Check whether the same residual symmetry generator is preserved by both.
\item If the corrected constant sector breaks the protecting symmetry, Gate 4 fails.
\item If the protecting symmetry survives the correction, Gate 4 passes.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Level E: role of Class II}

The canonical minimal Class II correction is gradient-linear.
Therefore it renormalizes derivative shell coefficients rather than directly inserting an independent constant Dirac mass.

Hence:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Class II is compatible with mass protection, but is not by itself a proof of it.}
}
\label{eq:G4_ClassII_compatible}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Checklist E.}
\begin{enumerate}
\item Do use Class II compatibility as a consistency check.
\item Do \emph{not} count Class II compatibility as a substitute for the residual-symmetry audit.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final Gate-4 decision tree}

The complete Gate-4 decision tree is:

\paragraph{Step 1.}
Construct the isolated doubled shell block and identify the exact mass space \(\mathcal M_D\).

\paragraph{Step 2.}
Test whether exact residual \(U(1)_V\) survives.
If yes, accept Gate 4 immediately.

\paragraph{Step 3.}
If not, test whether exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) survives.
If yes, accept Gate 4 immediately.

\paragraph{Step 4.}
If neither symmetry is manifest, compute the residual constant algebra \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\).
If
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D\neq \{0\},
\]
reject: a symmetry-allowed constant Dirac mass remains.

\paragraph{Step 5.}
Check that the same protecting symmetry survives the corrected constant block after remote-sector elimination.
If it fails at this level, reject.

\paragraph{Final verdict.}
Only if all previous steps pass do we conclude
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
}
\label{eq:G4_final_verdict}
\end{equation}
hence the branch is genuinely mass-protected.

\section{Honest status}

At the present stage, Gate 4 is theorem-level closed.
The only remaining task is the explicit microscopic symmetry audit of the actual corrected refined locked shell block.

Therefore Gate 4 is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{finite computation left.}
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

Gate 4 asks whether the refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is protected against all constant Dirac masses.

For the isolated doubled shell block
\[
H_D(p)=\sum_{i=1}^3 v_i p_i\,(\tau_z\otimes \sigma_i),
\]
the exact constant Dirac-mass space is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_D
=
\mathrm{span}_{\mathbb R}
\left\{
\tau_x\otimes \mathbf 1_2,\,
\tau_y\otimes \mathbf 1_2
\right\}.
}
\]

Hence the exact Gate-4 criterion is
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\},
}
\]
where
\[
A_{\mathrm{res}}
=
\{K\in\mathrm{Herm}(4):U(g)KU(g)^{-1}=K\ \forall g\in G_{\mathrm{res}}\}.
\]

Two shortcuts are insufficient:
\[
\boxed{
\text{little-group scalarity only} \not\Rightarrow \text{mass protection},
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{opposite-valley matching only} \not\Rightarrow \text{mass protection}.
}
\]

A sufficient mechanism is exact residual valley symmetry:
\[
\boxed{
Q_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2,
\qquad
U_\theta=e^{i\theta Q_V/2}.
}
\]
Under exact \(U(1)_V\), the two mass generators rotate as a charged doublet, so
\[
\boxed{
A_{U(1)_V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\]
The weaker remnant
\[
\boxed{
S_V=\tau_z\otimes \mathbf 1_2
}
\]
already suffices, because both mass generators are odd under it:
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathbb Z_2^V}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\]

Therefore the complete Gate-4 checklist is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item identify the isolated doubled shell block and the exact mass space \(\mathcal M_D\);
\item test whether exact residual \(U(1)_V\) survives;
\item if not, test whether exact residual \(\mathbb Z_2^V\) survives;
\item if neither is manifest, compute the full residual constant algebra \(A_{\mathrm{res}}\);
\item check whether the protecting symmetry survives the corrected constant block after remote-sector elimination.
\end{enumerate}

Only if
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap \mathcal M_D=\{0\}
}
\]
holds for the corrected isolated shell block does Gate 4 pass.

Class II remains only
\[
\boxed{
\text{compatible with mass protection, but not by itself a proof of it.}
}
\]

Thus Gate 4 is not conceptually open.
It is a finite residual-symmetry audit on the actual corrected refined locked shell block.

\section{Integrated Execution Table for Gates 2--4}

\[
\text{input} \;\longrightarrow\; \text{compute} \;\longrightarrow\; \text{pass/fail} \;\longrightarrow\; \text{failure meaning}.

The three gates are:

\[
\text{Gate 2: longitudinal survival},\qquad

\text{Gate 4: mass protection}.

\section{Fixed extraction layer}

The shell-extracted reduced coefficients are read from the projected low-valley matrices by
\begin{equation}

\begin{equation}

\qquad

\begin{equation}

\lambda_\parallel=C_c g_c,
\qquad
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore Gates 2 and 3 each have two nested layers:

\begin{enumerate}
\item transport-side survival (\(g\)-side),
\item Bloch-frame calibration survival (\(C\)-side).

Thus the remaining frontier is no longer conceptual.

\section{Gate 2 Actual Input Table: Executable Longitudinal Survival Audit}

\section{Goal}

The actual remaining microscopic longitudinal question is not conceptual.
It is the explicit finite audit of whether the primitive longitudinal shell seed survives through all four layers:
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}
\;\longrightarrow\;
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}
\;\longrightarrow\;

\;\longrightarrow\;

The final Gate-2 objective is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

\section{Primitive longitudinal target}

The canonical primitive longitudinal seed target is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B_\parallel:\quad
N^3_{ij}=\hat n_i\hat n_j,
\qquad
N^1_{ij}=N^2_{ij}=0.

\label{eq:G2_target_again}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the shell covector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T^{(\parallel)}_{ija}=\hat n_i\hat n_j\,\delta_{a3}.
}
\label{eq:G2_covector_again}
\end{equation}

Inside the explicit seed space,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

\label{eq:G2_seed_dictionary_again}
\end{equation}
with \(I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0\).
After Bloch calibration,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=C_c\,g_c.
}
\label{eq:G2_bloch_dictionary_again}
\end{equation}

Thus Gate 2 requires both a nonzero transport-side longitudinal seed and a nonzero Bloch-frame calibration overlap.

\section{Level A: basis-level audit}

Let
\[
V_{\mathrm{TECT}}\subset
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{out}}
\otimes
\mathbb R^3_{\mathrm{grad}}
\otimes
U_{\mathrm{int}}
\]
be the actual microscopic transport space, and let
\[
\{E_A\}_{A=1}^d
\]
be any basis.

Define the longitudinal overlap coefficients
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{\parallel A}:=
\langle T^{(\parallel)},E_A\rangle
=
E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j.

\label{eq:G2_ell_inputtable}

Then the exact basis-level criterion is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2_basis_pass}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Input.}
\[
G_*,\qquad
\hat n=\frac{G_*}{|G_*|},\qquad
\{e_1,e_2,\hat n\},\qquad
\{E_A\}.
\]

\paragraph{Compute.}
\[
\ell_{\parallel A}=E_{A,ij}^{,3}\hat n_i\hat n_j
\quad\text{for all }A.
\]

\paragraph{Pass.}
At least one \(\ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0\).

\paragraph{Fail means.}
The microscopic transport space contains no admissible longitudinal seed direction.

\section{Level B: shell-seed projection audit}

Project the actual induced shell tensor onto the explicit seed space:
\begin{equation}

=

+

+

\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.

\label{eq:G2_basis_seed_equiv_again}

\paragraph{Input.}

\paragraph{Compute.}
The seed coefficient \(c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\).

\paragraph{Pass.}
\[
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Fail means.}
The full shell projection annihilates the primitive longitudinal channel.

\section{Level C: graded/radial overlap audit}

At the projected defect-profile level, the same survival condition becomes the \(\sigma_3\)-graded overlap
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

=

\paragraph{Input.}
\[

\paragraph{Compute.}
The scalar integral \(J_\parallel^{(3)}\).

\paragraph{Pass.}
\[
J_\parallel^{(3)}\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Fail means.}
The defect/envelope overlap cancels the surviving longitudinal seed.

A simple sufficient condition is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,\mathfrak s_c(\xi)
\text{ has definite nonzero sign on a set of positive measure.}
}
\label{eq:G2_sign_suff_again}
\end{equation}

\section{Level D: final Bloch calibration audit}

Even after the longitudinal seed survives on the transport side, the physical coefficient still depends on the Bloch-frame overlap

=
\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)}).

\end{equation}

\paragraph{Input.}

V^\mu_{(c)}(\xi)=\frac{\theta'(\xi)^3}{I_{\theta'^3}}\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
\qquad
\Psi_a^\pm,
\qquad
M^\parallel_{(c)}.

\paragraph{Compute.}
\[
C_c=\frac12\Tr(\sigma_3M^\parallel_{(c)}).
\]

\paragraph{Pass.}
\[
C_c\neq 0.
\]

\paragraph{Fail means.}
The longitudinal seed survives transport-side projection but dies in the actual Bloch frame.

\end{equation}

Thus \(C_c\) belongs to:

\boxed{\text{formula explicit but value not inserted}.}

\section{Gate 2-A: Actual Candidate Blocks for the Primitive Longitudinal Seed}

\section{Short explanation}

The honest remaining carrier question is only the survival of the primitive longitudinal seed.
This is already reduced to a finite microscopic audit:
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0.
}
\]

At the blockwise Hessian level, the strongest current statement is sharper:
\[
\boxed{
OO \text{ is the natural primitive longitudinal block for } \ell_0^{(3)}.
}
\]
Therefore the correct nonredundant next step is to start the longitudinal audit from the \(OO\) block, and only if this fails, extend to the full \(9\)-block sum.

\section{1. Starting point: full block Hessian}

Let the full background fluctuation field be decomposed as
\[
\varphi=(a,\nu,\zeta),
\]
where
\[
a\sim T,\qquad \nu\sim O,\qquad \zeta\sim D.
\]
Then the full background Hessian has the exact block form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\
\mathcal H_{DT} & \mathcal H_{DO} & \mathcal H_{DD}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:G2A_full_block_hessian}
\end{equation}

Each block expands as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V_{AB}^{\mu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
\mathcal W_{AB}^{\mu\nu}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}\partial_{y^\nu}
+\cdots.
\label{eq:G2A_block_expand}
\end{equation}

Only the first-order transport term \(\mathcal V_{AB}^{\mu}\) contributes to the primitive longitudinal audit.

\section{2. Blockwise longitudinal coefficients}

For each block \(AB\in\{T,O,D\}^2\), reduce the invariant shell transport part to
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)
=
h_{0;AB}(\theta)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_{\parallel;AB}(\theta)\,n^\mu\sigma_3
+
h_{E;AB}(\theta)\,E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a
+
h_{O;AB}(\theta)\,J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a.
\label{eq:G2A_Minv_block}
\end{equation}

Then the longitudinal block coefficient is extracted by the exact Pauli trace
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{\parallel;AB}(\theta)
=
\frac12\Tr\!\bigl[\sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}(\theta)\bigr].
}
\label{eq:G2A_hpar_trace}
\end{equation}

The exact longitudinal monomial coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{h_{\parallel;AB}(\theta)}{\theta},
\qquad
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta'\to 0}
\frac{h_{\parallel;AB}(\theta)}{\theta'^3}
\quad
(\text{if }\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}=0).
}
\label{eq:G2A_ellAB_def}
\end{equation}

Summing over all blocks gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}=\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)},
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:G2A_ellsum}
\end{equation}

The exact microscopic longitudinal survival criterion is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\ell_0^{(3)}\neq 0
\;\Longrightarrow\;
c_\parallel^{(\mathrm{mic})}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2A_exact_block_criterion}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Branch A / Branch B interpretation}

Identify
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=\ell_0^{(1)},
\qquad
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}=\ell_0^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:G2A_branch_identification}
\end{equation}

Hence the longitudinal audit splits into two mutually exclusive practical routes:

\paragraph{Branch A:}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2A_branchA}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Branch B:}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\neq 0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2A_branchB}
\end{equation}

Thus the actual Gate-2 bottleneck is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Does the microscopic branch realize Branch A or Branch B?}
}
\label{eq:G2A_bottleneck}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Why \(OO\) is the first block to audit}

At the current sharpest blockwise stage, the natural carrier assignment is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
OO \text{ is the natural primitive longitudinal block for } \ell_0^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:G2A_OO_long}
\end{equation}

The orientational diagonal block has the exact form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y),
}
\label{eq:G2A_HOO}
\end{equation}
where the last term is the background-induced first-order transport operator.

This makes \(OO\) the natural first candidate for carrying the primitive odd singlet \(\theta'(\xi)^3\sigma_3\), i.e. the \(\ell_0^{(3)}\) / \(\lambda_c\) channel.

Therefore the correct nonredundant audit order is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{first compute } \ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},\ \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:G2A_OO_first}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Minimal candidate list for Gate 2-A}

The actual candidate list is:

\paragraph{Primary candidate:}
\[
\boxed{
OO \quad\text{for }\ell_0^{(3)}\text{ / Branch B / }\lambda_c.
}
\]

\paragraph{Secondary candidate:}
all remaining blocks only if the primary candidate fails:
\[
\boxed{
TT,\ TO,\ TD,\ OT,\ OD,\ DT,\ DO,\ DD.
}
\]

Operationally, one computes the blockwise traces
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}]
}{\theta},
\qquad
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta'\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}]
}{\theta'^3}.
}
\label{eq:G2A_block_formula_oper}
\end{equation}

Then the Gate-2 blockwise decision rule is:

\begin{enumerate}
\item compute \((\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)})\);
\item if either is nonzero, Gate 2-A passes immediately;
\item if both vanish, compute the remaining eight blocks and test
\[
\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}\neq0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\sum_{A,B}\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}\neq0.
\]
\end{enumerate}

\section{6. Relation to the basis-overlap audit}

The blockwise audit and the basis-overlap audit are equivalent formulations.

The basis-overlap statement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq 0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\exists A:\ a_A\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2A_basis_equiv}
\end{equation}

The blockwise statement is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq 0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\ell_0^{(3)}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2A_block_equiv}
\end{equation}

So Gate 2-A can be executed in either language:

\begin{itemize}
\item basis language: find one microscopic basis vector with \(a_A\neq0\);
\item block language: find one nonzero longitudinal block coefficient.
\end{itemize}

\section{7. Final practical Gate-2-A execution sheet}

\[

\\

\section{Honest status}

The only remaining longitudinal carrier question is exactly this finite blockwise / basis-overlap audit.
No new conceptual structure is needed.

At the current strongest explicit stage, the \(OO\) block is the natural first carrier to test.
If it already yields nonzero \(\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\), then the primitive longitudinal channel is microscopically realized and Gate 2 is essentially open only at the overlap/calibration layer.

\section{Final Summary}

The honest remaining carrier question is only the survival of the primitive longitudinal seed.
This is reduced to a finite longitudinal audit:
\[
\boxed{
\exists A:\ \ell_{\parallel A}\neq0
}

or equivalently
\[
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}\neq0
\quad\text{or}\quad
\ell_0^{(3)}\neq0.

The blockwise Hessian audit uses
\[
\Gamma^{(2)}[\bar\Phi_{\min}]
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\mathcal H_{TT} & \mathcal H_{TO} & \mathcal H_{TD}\\
\mathcal H_{OT} & \mathcal H_{OO} & \mathcal H_{OD}\\

\end{pmatrix},

with first-order transport blocks extracted from
\[
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}
-

+\cdots.

For each block,
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{0;AB}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}

}{\theta},
\qquad
\ell_{0;AB}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta'\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr[\sigma_3 n_\mu \mathcal M^\mu_{AB,\mathrm{inv}}]
}{\theta'^3}.
}
\]

The sharpest current blockwise statement is
\[
\boxed{
OO \text{ is the natural primitive longitudinal block for } \ell_0^{(3)}.
}
\]

Hence the correct nonredundant Gate-2-A procedure is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{first compute } \ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},\ \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.

If either is nonzero, the longitudinal primitive channel is microscopically realized.

If both vanish, extend to all \(9\) blocks and test

\quad\text{or}\quad

This is equivalent to the basis-overlap audit

\]

Thus Gate 2-A is no longer conceptually open.
The immediate next executable task is the explicit \(OO\)-block longitudinal audit.

\section{Term-by-Term Longitudinal Audit of the \texorpdfstring{$OO$}{OO} Block}

\section{Goal}

We now perform the actual Gate-2-A audit on the \(OO\) block.
The purpose is to determine, term by term, which pieces of
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y)
\]
can contribute to the longitudinal primitive coefficients
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
\]
The answer will show that in the current explicit library the only genuine leading longitudinal carrier is the primitive Branch-B term inside \(\mathcal T_{OO}\).

\section{1. Blockwise extraction principle}

For each block \(AB\), the background Hessian is expanded as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+
O(\partial_y^2).
\label{eq:OO_block_expand}
\end{equation}

Only the first-order transport operator \(\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}\) can contribute to the local shell-carrier audit.
Therefore the longitudinal \(OO\)-coefficient is extracted from the invariant tangent reduction
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)
=
h_{0;OO}(\xi)\,n^\mu\mathbf 1_2
+
h_{\parallel;OO}(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
h_{E;OO}(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
h_{O;OO}(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a.
\label{eq:OO_Minv}
\end{equation}

The exact longitudinal trace is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
h_{\parallel;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:OO_hpar_trace}
\end{equation}

Then the two blockwise longitudinal coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}\frac{h_{\parallel;OO}(\xi)}{\theta'(\xi)},
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}\frac{h_{\parallel;OO}(\xi)-\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\theta'(\xi)}{\theta'(\xi)^3}.
}
\label{eq:OO_ell_def}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if
\begin{equation}
h_{\parallel;OO}(\xi)
=
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
\cdots,
\label{eq:OO_hpar_series}
\end{equation}
then \(\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}\) is the Branch-A coefficient and \(\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}\) is the primitive Branch-B coefficient.

\section{2. The actual \(OO\) block}

The background-dependent orientational block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y).
}
\label{eq:HOO_actual}
\end{equation}

We now audit each term separately.

\section{3. Kinetic term \texorpdfstring{$-Z_{O,k}\partial^2$}{-Z_O,k partial^2}}

The isotropic kinetic term contributes only a second-order derivative operator.
Hence it does not directly produce any first-order worldvolume transport tensor of the form
\[
n^\mu\Sigma_3\,\partial_{y^\mu}.
\]

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
\text{ contributes to }
\mathcal H_{OO}^{(0)}
\text{ and higher-derivative pieces, but not directly to }
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}
\text{ or }
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:OO_kinetic_no_direct}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Potential term \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)$}{M_OO^pot}}

The background-dependent potential term is zeroth order in worldvolume derivatives.
So it may shift the local mass matrix, but it cannot generate a transport operator carrying one derivative index and one longitudinal shell-tangent \(\Sigma_3\) structure.

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
\text{ cannot directly contribute to }
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}
\text{ or }
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}.
}
\label{eq:OO_potential_no_direct}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Gradient-anisotropy term \texorpdfstring{$Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}$}{Y_k K_OO^nablaani}}

This is the only nontrivial diagonal term that could, in principle, generate a first-order longitudinal structure.
So we must be honest here.

At the operator level, a Branch-A longitudinal contribution would require
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\,\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:OO_branchA_needed}
\end{equation}

But the current no-go theorem for the solved lowest-order complete realization states
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:OO_branchB_forced}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the current complete LO action class contains no additional linear longitudinal tangent carrier of the form \(\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3\). Thus Branch A is absent and Branch B is forced. Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
\text{ does not produce a nonzero }
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}
\text{ in the current solved LO class.}
}
\label{eq:OO_no_branchA}
\end{equation}

This is the precise sense in which the diagonal anisotropy term does not rescue Branch A inside the present library.

\section{6. Transport term \texorpdfstring{$\mathcal T_{OO}$}{T_OO}}

This is the only term that is structurally designed to contribute to the first-order transport operator.
Hence all genuine leading longitudinal information must sit inside \(\mathcal T_{OO}\).

The exact tangent first-order ansatz is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)
=
a_0(\xi)\,n^\mu\Pi_Q
+
a_3(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
+
b_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
b_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
V^\mu_{\mathrm{null}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:OO_general_V}
\end{equation}

The branch-sensitive longitudinal coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:OO_a3_branch}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:OO_branchB_forced}, this reduces in the current solved lowest-order realization to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi),
\qquad
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\label{eq:OO_a3_branchB}
\end{equation}

Therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:OO_final_ell}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the first closed blockwise longitudinal coefficient point inside the current explicit operator library.

\section{7. Final term-by-term verdict for \texorpdfstring{$OO$}{OO}}

Collecting the previous sections:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
\;\;\Rightarrow\;\;
\text{no direct contribution to }
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\label{eq:OO_verdict_kin}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}
\;\;\Rightarrow\;\;
\text{no direct contribution to }
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)},
}
\label{eq:OO_verdict_pot}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
\;\;\Rightarrow\;\;
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)}=0
\text{ in the current LO no-go class,}
}
\label{eq:OO_verdict_Y}
\end{equation}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{OO}
\;\;\Rightarrow\;\;
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}
\text{ is the leading genuine longitudinal primitive carrier.}
}
\label{eq:OO_verdict_T}
\end{equation}

Hence the complete current blockwise result is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:OO_global_result}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Consequence for Gate 2-A}

Thus Gate 2-A for the current working library is reduced to one finite question:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?
}
\label{eq:OO_gate_question}
\end{equation}

If yes, then Branch B is microscopically realized already at the \(OO\)-block level, and the longitudinal carrier survives at transport level:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:OO_lambda_result}
\end{equation}

Only if \(\lambda_{c;OO}=0\) should one continue to the remaining eight blocks and ask whether a hidden Branch-A carrier or subleading longitudinal channel appears elsewhere.

\section{Final Summary}

The actual orientational diagonal block is
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}
=
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
+
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
+
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}(\xi,\partial)
+
\mathcal T_{OO}(\xi,\partial_y).
\]

The blockwise longitudinal coefficients are defined by
\[
h_{\parallel;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\mathcal M^\mu_{OO,\mathrm{inv}}(\xi)\bigr),
\]
and
\[
\ell_{0;OO}^{(1)},\qquad \ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
\]
are the coefficients of \(\theta'(\xi)\) and \(\theta'(\xi)^3\) in its shell expansion.

Term by term:

\[
\boxed{
-Z_{O,k}\partial^2
\text{ gives no direct first-order longitudinal transport contribution,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
\mathcal M_{OO}^{\mathrm{pot}}(\xi)
\text{ gives no direct first-order longitudinal transport contribution,}
}
\]

\[
\boxed{
Y_k\mathcal K_{OO}^{\nabla\mathrm{ani}}
\text{ does not produce a nonzero Branch-A coefficient in the current solved LO class,}
}
\]
because
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0.
}
\]

Thus the only genuine leading longitudinal carrier inside the \(OO\) block is the first-order transport term
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_{OO}.
}
\]

Its tangent coefficient has the branch-sensitive form
\[
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
\]

In the current solved lowest-order realization,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\qquad \lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3+\cdots.
}
\]

Therefore the first closed blockwise longitudinal point is
\[
\boxed{
\ell_0^{(1)}=0,
\qquad
\ell_0^{(3)}=\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\]

Hence Gate 2-A in the current working library is reduced to the single finite question
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?
}
\]

If yes, then Branch B is already microscopically realized at the \(OO\)-block level and
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
I_{\theta'^3}\,\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{Actual Extraction Formula for \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_{c;OO}$}{lambda\_c,OO}}

\section{Short explanation}

The Gate-2-A problem is now reduced to extracting the primitive longitudinal coefficient from the first-order tangent transport block.

The load-bearing projected coefficient is
\[
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu(\xi)\bigr),
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q.
\]

In the current solved lowest-order class, the linear Branch-A term vanishes,
\[
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\]
so the only principal longitudinal source is the primitive commutator-square channel, i.e. the \(\theta'(\xi)^3\Sigma_3\) term.

\section{1. Exact projected first-order transport block}

Start from the exact term-by-term split of the first-order worldvolume Hessian:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)
=
\mathbb H_{1,\Psi}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,P}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,\sigma}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,X}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,J}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,K}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,EO}^\mu.
}
\label{eq:G2A_H1_split_final}
\end{equation}

Projecting to the tangent \(Q_B\)-bundle gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:G2A_V_projected_final}
\end{equation}

The longitudinal coefficient is extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:G2A_a3_trace_final}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Branch-sensitive decomposition of \texorpdfstring{$a_3(\xi)$}{a3(xi)}}

The exact branch-sensitive parameterization is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:G2A_a3_branch_final}
\end{equation}

The complete microscopic decision tree is therefore:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{first test }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\neq 0;
\qquad
\text{if it vanishes, test }\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:G2A_decision_tree_final}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Primitive commutator-square seed}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi:=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\label{eq:G2A_Txi_Sxi_final}
\end{equation}

For the explicit defect representative,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:G2A_Sxi_explicit_final}
\end{equation}

Hence the primitive longitudinal transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:G2A_Vprim_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:G2A_a3prim_final}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Why Branch A vanishes in the current solved local class}

Inside the current local isotropic scalar library, the first nonzero tangent \(\Sigma_3\)-object is quadratic in the defect gradient:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q(\partial_\xi P)^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:G2A_quadratic_first_final}
\end{equation}

Thus every local higher-order correction built from the same algebra generates only the odd tower
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)^3\Sigma_3,\quad
\theta'(\xi)^5\Sigma_3,\quad
\theta'(\xi)^7\Sigma_3,\ \dots
}
\label{eq:G2A_odd_tower_final}
\end{equation}
in the first-order transport kernel.

Therefore no linear Branch-A term appears:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0
}
\label{eq:G2A_Lambda0_zero_final}
\end{equation}
within the current solved local class.

So the principal longitudinal coefficient reduces to Branch B:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
\quad\text{at principal order.}
}
\label{eq:G2A_a3_branchB_final}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Actual extraction formula for \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_{c;OO}$}{lambda\_c,OO}}

Now restrict to the \(OO\)-candidate transport contribution.
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:G2A_VOO_def}
\end{equation}

Then its longitudinal Pauli trace is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:G2A_a3OO_def}
\end{equation}

If the current blockwise interpretation is correct and \(OO\) is indeed the natural primitive longitudinal carrier, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
O(\theta'(\xi)^5).
}
\label{eq:G2A_a3OO_expand}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact extraction formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}
\label{eq:G2A_lambda_cOO_extract}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}
\label{eq:G2A_ellOO3_extract}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Projection to the low Bloch modes}

Let
\[
u_a^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_a(\xi)
\]
be the opposite-valley low modes.
The projected shell matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\;
f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,
e_a^\dagger(\xi)\,
V^\mu(\xi)\,
e_b(\xi).
}
\label{eq:G2A_Mmu_projection}
\end{equation}

Using \eqref{eq:G2A_Vprim_final}, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:G2A_I3_def}
\end{equation}

Then the longitudinal reduced coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3.
}
\label{eq:G2A_lambda_parallel_I3}
\end{equation}

So if \(OO\) indeed carries the primitive branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3.
}
\label{eq:G2A_lambda_parallel_OO}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest block-label caveat}

There is a notation drift across the current notes:

\begin{itemize}
\item the blockwise audit summary states that \(OO\) is the natural primitive longitudinal block;
\item some explicit primitive formulas were written in a document whose local section/file labeling still carries a \(TT\)-style notation.
\end{itemize}

Therefore the fully honest statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the algebraic principal longitudinal source is unambiguously the primitive }
\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3\text{ channel,}
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the current blockwise working interpretation assigns this channel to the }OO\text{ candidate.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{8. Final Gate-2-A reduction}

Hence the actual Gate-2-A problem is reduced to the single finite extraction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?
}
\label{eq:G2A_final_single_question}
\end{equation}

If yes, then the primitive Branch-B longitudinal channel is microscopically realized already at the transport level, and Gate 2-A is closed up to the already-separated graded/Bloch overlap checks.

\section{Final Summary}

The actual longitudinal transport coefficient is extracted from
\[
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu(\xi)\bigr),
\qquad
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q.
}
\]

Its branch-sensitive expansion is
\[
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\]

Inside the current solved local isotropic scalar class,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
so the principal longitudinal source is forced to Branch B:
\[
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
\quad\text{at principal order.}
}
\]

The primitive commutator-square seed is
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3,
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\]

Under the current blockwise working interpretation, the natural primitive longitudinal candidate is the \(OO\) block.
Therefore the actual extraction formula is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
},
}
\]
equivalently
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}
\]

Projection to the low Bloch modes gives
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\]

Hence, if the \(OO\) candidate is confirmed,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3.
}
\]

So the Gate-2-A problem is now reduced to the single finite extraction:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?
}
\]

\section{Subterm Decomposition of \texorpdfstring{$\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu\Pi_Q$}{PiQ H1OO PiQ} and Actual Extraction of \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_{c;OO}$}{lambda c,OO}}

\section{Goal}

The Gate-2-A problem is to determine which microscopic subterm of the first-order tangent transport block actually contributes to the longitudinal primitive coefficient in the \(OO\) candidate block.

The full first-order worldvolume Hessian splits as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)
=
\mathbb H_{1,\Psi}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,P}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,\sigma}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,X}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,J}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,K}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,EO}^\mu.
}
\label{eq:H1_split_subterm}
\end{equation}

Projecting to the tangent \(Q_B\)-bundle gives
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q.
\label{eq:Vmu_projected_subterm}
\end{equation}

The longitudinal Pauli trace is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:a3_trace_subterm}
\end{equation}

The branch-sensitive parameterization is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:a3_branch_param_subterm}
\end{equation}

\section{Primitive longitudinal source}

Define the commutator seed
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi:=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\label{eq:Txi_Sxi_subterm}
\end{equation}

For the explicit defect representative,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Txi_square_sigma3_subterm}
\end{equation}

Therefore the primitive longitudinal transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Vprim_long_subterm}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:a3prim_subterm}
\end{equation}

\section{Why Branch A is absent in the solved LO class}

The solved lowest-order class satisfies the no-go result
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:nogo_branchA_subterm}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the current local isotropic scalar library contains no linear longitudinal tangent carrier of the form
\[
\theta'(\xi)\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
\]

Thus the principal longitudinal coefficient reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
\quad\text{at principal order.}
}
\label{eq:a3_branchB_only_subterm}
\end{equation}

\section{K-sector contribution}

The direct tangent-block contribution from the \(K\)-sector has the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_K^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\kappa_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\kappa_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:VK_subterm}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
b_E^{(K)}=\kappa_E(\xi)\theta'(\xi),
\qquad
b_O^{(K)}=\kappa_O(\xi)\theta'(\xi).
}
\label{eq:K_contrib_subterm}
\end{equation}

So the \(K\)-sector is purely transverse at principal order and cannot contribute to \(\lambda_c\).

\section{EO-slot contribution}

The explicit extra \(E/O\)-slot contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:VEO_subterm}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(EO)}=0,
\qquad
b_E^{(EO)}=\widetilde\Lambda_E\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\qquad
b_O^{(EO)}=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:EO_contrib_subterm}
\end{equation}

So the \(EO\)-slot is also purely transverse and cannot contribute to \(\lambda_c\).

\section{Canonical source table}

At principal order, the canonical source table is therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{source} & \text{canonical form} & a_3\text{-contribution} \\\hline
\text{primitive longitudinal} &
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 n^\mu\Sigma_3 &
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 \\
K\text{-sector} &
\theta'(\xi)\bigl[\kappa_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+\kappa_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a\bigr] &
0 \\
EO\text{-slot} &
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)\bigl[\widetilde\Lambda_E E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a+\widetilde\Lambda_O J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a\bigr] &
0 \\
\text{irreducible/forbidden} & V^\mu_{\mathrm{irr}} & 0
\end{array}
}
\label{eq:canonical_source_table_subterm}
\end{equation}

Thus the longitudinal principal source is unique.

\section{OO-candidate extraction}

Under the current blockwise working interpretation, the natural primitive longitudinal candidate is the \(OO\) block. Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\,\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:VOO_def_subterm}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu_{OO}(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:a3OO_def_subterm}
\end{equation}

If the current blockwise assignment is correct, then at principal order
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
O(\theta'(\xi)^5).
}
\label{eq:a3OO_expand_subterm}
\end{equation}

Therefore the actual extraction formula is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}
\label{eq:lambda_cOO_extract_subterm}
\end{equation}

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}
\label{eq:ellOO3_extract_subterm}
\end{equation}

\section{Projection to the low Bloch modes}

Projecting to the opposite-valley low modes gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(M^\mu)_{ab}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,e_a^\dagger(\xi)V^\mu(\xi)e_b(\xi).
}
\label{eq:Bloch_projection_subterm}
\end{equation}

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:I3_subterm}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_I3_subterm}
\end{equation}

Under the \(OO\)-candidate interpretation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_OO_subterm}
\end{equation}

\section{Honest notation caveat}

There is a notation drift across the current notes:
some primitive formulas were written in a local notation that resembles a \(TT\)-style label,
while the blockwise audit summary assigns the primitive longitudinal carrier to \(OO\).

Therefore the fully honest statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the algebraic principal longitudinal source is unambiguously the primitive }
\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3\text{ channel,}
}
\label{eq:notation_caveat1}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the current blockwise working interpretation assigns this channel to the }OO\text{ candidate.}
}
\label{eq:notation_caveat2}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Gate-2-A reduction}

Hence the actual Gate-2-A problem is reduced to the single finite extraction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?
}
\label{eq:final_single_gate2A}
\end{equation}

If yes, then the primitive Branch-B longitudinal channel is microscopically realized already at the transport level, and Gate 2-A is closed up to the already-separated graded/Bloch overlap checks.

\section{Final Summary}

The actual first-order tangent transport block is
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q,
\]
and the longitudinal coefficient is extracted by
\[
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\]

Its exact branch-sensitive form is
\[
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\]

In the solved local lowest-order class,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
so the principal longitudinal source is forced to Branch B:
\[
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
\quad\text{at principal order.}
}
\]

The primitive commutator-square seed is
\[
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3,
}
\]
hence
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\]

At principal order:
\[
\boxed{
a_3^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
a_3^{(EO)}=0,
}
\]
so the \(K\)-sector and \(EO\)-slot are purely transverse and do not contribute to the longitudinal primitive coefficient.

Under the current blockwise working interpretation, the natural primitive longitudinal candidate is the \(OO\) block.
Therefore the actual extraction formula is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
\lim_{\theta\to 0}
\frac{
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\]

Projection to the low Bloch modes gives
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\]
So under the \(OO\)-candidate interpretation,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3.
}
\]

Hence the actual Gate-2-A problem has now been reduced to the single finite extraction:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?
}
\]

The only honest caveat is a remaining notation drift across the notes: the algebraic primitive source is unambiguous, but some local formulas were written in a different block-label convention.

\section{Source Table for the \texorpdfstring{$\Sigma_3 n^\mu$}{Sigma3 nmu} Trace in \texorpdfstring{$\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu\Pi_Q$}{PiQ H1 PiQ}}

\section{Starting point}

The exact first-order tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q,
}
\end{equation}
with the additive source split
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathbb H_1^\mu
=
\mathbb H_{1,\Psi}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,P}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,\sigma}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,X}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,J}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,K}^\mu
+
\mathbb H_{1,EO}^\mu.
}
\end{equation}

The longitudinal coefficient is extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\end{equation}

Its branch-sensitive form is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\end{equation}

\section{Solved lowest-order class}

In the solved lowest-order complete realization, the no-go theorem gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the principal longitudinal source is forced onto Branch B:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
\quad\text{at principal order.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Primitive source}

The primitive commutator-square seed satisfies
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}
=
\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3,
}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3,
\qquad
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the primitive commutator-square channel is an explicit principal longitudinal source.

\section{K-sector}

The direct tangent-block contribution from the \(K\)-sector is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_K^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)
\Bigl[
\kappa_E(\xi)\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\kappa_O(\xi)\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(K)}=0.
}
\end{equation}

So the \(K\)-sector is purely transverse at principal order.

\section{EO-slot}

The explicit \(EO\)-slot contribution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V_{EO}^\mu
=
\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Bigl[
\widetilde\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\widetilde\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr].
}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(EO)}=0.
}
\end{equation}

So the \(EO\)-slot is also purely transverse.

\section{Scalar/isotropic sectors}

If every sector is built from local tangent-isotropic scalar contractions, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\Psi)}=a_3^{(P)}=a_3^{(\sigma)}=a_3^{(X)}=a_3^{(EO)}=0.
}
\end{equation}

Thus these sectors do not generate the principal longitudinal channel at lowest local order.

\section{J-sector status}

For the uploaded notes currently inspected, an explicit separate formula
\[
a_3^{(J)}=0
\]
was not found as a standalone displayed result.

However, the canonical source table already classifies the principal source content as:
\[
\text{primitive commutator-square}\to n^\mu\sigma_3\to\lambda_c,
\]
\[
\text{transverse even/odd}\to E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,\ J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a,
\]
with no additional principal longitudinal source listed.

Therefore the strongest honest current statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(J)}\ \text{is not separately extracted in the uploaded notes,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
the principal longitudinal source table assigns the leading }n^\mu\Sigma_3\text{ coefficient uniquely to the primitive channel.}
\end{equation}

\section{Final source table}

At principal order, the \(\Sigma_3 n^\mu\)-trace survival table is:

\[
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.35}
\begin{array}{c|c|c}
\text{Source} & \Sigma_3 n^\mu\text{-trace at principal order} & \text{Status} \\
\hline
\mathbb H_{1,\Psi}^\mu & 0 & \text{excluded in current local isotropic class} \\
\mathbb H_{1,P}^\mu & 0 & \text{excluded in current local isotropic class} \\
\mathbb H_{1,\sigma}^\mu & 0 & \text{excluded in current local isotropic class} \\
\mathbb H_{1,X}^\mu & 0 & \text{excluded in current local isotropic class} \\
\mathbb H_{1,J}^\mu & \text{not separately extracted} & \text{no explicit principal-source role established} \\
\mathbb H_{1,K}^\mu & 0 & \text{purely transverse} \\
\mathbb H_{1,EO}^\mu & 0 & \text{purely transverse} \\
\text{primitive commutator-square seed} & \dfrac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3 & \text{unique explicit principal longitudinal source}
\end{array}
\]

\section{OO-candidate interpretation}

Under the current blockwise working interpretation, this principal primitive longitudinal source is assigned to the \(OO\) candidate block.
Hence the actual extraction reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
\lim_{\theta\to0}
\frac{
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)

If \(\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0\), then

\qquad
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\end{equation}

So the Gate-2-A problem is reduced to the single finite question
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?
}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The first-order tangent transport block is
\[
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q,
\]
and the longitudinal coefficient is extracted by

\boxed{

}
\]
so the principal longitudinal source is forced to Branch B:

\boxed{

The explicit principal longitudinal source is the primitive commutator-square channel:

and also
\[
\boxed{

}
\]

For the \(J\)-sector, the uploaded notes do not yet provide a separate displayed extraction formula for \(a_3^{(J)}\).
So the strongest honest current statement is not that \(a_3^{(J)}=0\) is proven separately, but that the canonical principal-source table assigns the leading longitudinal coefficient uniquely to the primitive channel.

Under the current blockwise working interpretation, this principal primitive source is assigned to the \(OO\) candidate block.
Therefore the actual Gate-2-A extraction reduces to
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}
=
\lim_{\theta\to0}

\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
}{
\theta'(\xi)^3
}.
}

If \(\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0\), then

\qquad

}
\]

Hence the full Gate-2-A problem is reduced to the single finite question
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0\ ?
