\section{Practical Sufficient Conditions for \texorpdfstring{$\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0$}{lambda c,OO nonzero}}

\section{Starting point}

The exact first-order tangent transport block is
\begin{equation}
V^\mu(\xi)=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_1^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q,
\end{equation}
and the longitudinal coefficient is extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,V^\mu(\xi)\bigr).
}
\label{eq:a3_start_suff}
\end{equation}

Its branch-sensitive parameterization is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
}
\label{eq:a3_branch_suff}
\end{equation}

In the solved lowest-order complete realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:no_go_branchA_suff}
\end{equation}
so the principal longitudinal source is forced to Branch B:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3(\xi)=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
\quad\text{at principal order.}
}
\label{eq:branchB_only_suff}
\end{equation}

\section{Primitive principal source}

The primitive commutator-square channel is defined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal T_\xi=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
}
\label{eq:Txi_primitive_suff}
\end{equation}

For the explicit defect representative,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi=\frac12\theta'(\xi)^2\Sigma_3,
}
\label{eq:Sxi_explicit_suff}
\end{equation}
hence the primitive transport source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{\parallel,\mathrm{prim}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:Vprim_suff}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:a3prim_suff}
\end{equation}

\section{Subterm elimination at principal order}

At principal order, the following source sectors do \emph{not} contribute to the \(\Sigma_3 n^\mu\)-trace:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
a_3^{(EO)}=0,
}
\label{eq:K_EO_zero_suff}
\end{equation}
and, inside the current local tangent-isotropic scalar class,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\Psi)}=a_3^{(P)}=a_3^{(\sigma)}=a_3^{(X)}=0.
}
\label{eq:scalar_zero_suff}
\end{equation}

Thus the strongest honest principal-order source table is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{primitive commutator-square source}
\Longrightarrow
n^\mu\Sigma_3
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_c.
}
\label{eq:unique_principal_source_suff}
\end{equation}

This means that, within the current solved LO library, the principal longitudinal coefficient is unique.

\section{OO-candidate extraction}

Under the current blockwise working interpretation, the primitive longitudinal source is assigned to the \(OO\) candidate block:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO}(\xi):=\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:VOO_suff}

a_{3;OO}(\xi)
=

Equivalently,

=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}.
}
\label{eq:ellOO3_suff}
\end{equation}

\section{Transport-level sufficient condition}

A clean sufficient condition for
\[
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq 0
\]
is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\exists U\subset \mathbb R_\xi
\text{ of positive measure such that }
\theta'(\xi)\neq 0
\text{ on }U,
}
\label{eq:suff1}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac12\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
\text{ has the same nonzero sign as }\theta'(\xi)^3
\text{ on }U.
}
\label{eq:suff2}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0.
}
\label{eq:transport_suff_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Because the principal-order source is unique in the current solved library, \eqref{eq:suff2} is not merely sufficient in practice:
it is the effective principal-order nonvanishing test.

\section{Equivalent symmetry/parity/support formulation}

The same content can be written as four practical conditions:

\paragraph{(i) Nontrivial defect support}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)\not\equiv 0.
}
\label{eq:cond_support}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(ii) Allowed parity}
The source must be odd overall at first order, so that \(\theta'(\xi)^3\Sigma_3\) is not parity-forbidden:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the projected source is reflection-odd and compatible with }n^\mu\Sigma_3.
}
\label{eq:cond_parity}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(iii) Nontrivial internal trace}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Tr_{Q_B}\!\bigl(\Sigma_3\,n_\mu\,\Pi_Q\mathbb H_{1,OO}^\mu(\xi)\Pi_Q\bigr)
\not\equiv 0.
}
\label{eq:cond_trace}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{(iv) No principal-order cancellation}
Since the principal longitudinal source is unique in the current library, there is no competing principal-order term to cancel it.
Hence once \eqref{eq:cond_trace} holds with nonzero \(\theta'^3\)-coefficient, \(\lambda_{c;OO}\) survives.

\section{Full Gate-2 sufficient condition}

Transport-level survival is not yet the final physical longitudinal coefficient.
Projecting to the low Bloch modes gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_I3_suff}
\end{equation}

Therefore a sufficient condition for the full Gate 2 longitudinal survival is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0,
\qquad
C_c\neq0.
}
\label{eq:full_gate2_suff}
\end{equation}

If these hold, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_final_suff}
\end{equation}

\section{Honest caveat}

There remains a notation drift across the uploaded notes:
some primitive formulas were written in a local block-labeling convention that resembles a \(TT\)-style notation, while the blockwise audit summary assigns the primitive longitudinal carrier to the \(OO\) candidate.

Hence the fully honest statement is:

\begin{equation}

\text{the algebraic principal source is unambiguously }
\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3,

\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the current blockwise working interpretation assigns it to the }OO\text{ candidate.}
}

\section{Final Summary}

The actual longitudinal transport coefficient is extracted from

\section{Final Gate-2 Verdict with Transport/Calibration Split}

\section{Short explanation}

The longitudinal carrier problem is now reduced to a branch-sensitive finite audit.

The exact branch decision tree is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{first test }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)};
\qquad
\text{if it vanishes, test }\lambda_c.
}
\]

In the solved lowest-order complete realization,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\qquad \lambda_c\neq 0.
}
\]
Therefore the practical Gate-2 route is forced onto Branch B.

\section{1. Branch-B primitive seed}

Define
\[
\mathcal T_\xi:=i[P_B,\partial_\xi P_B],
\qquad
S_\xi:=(\Pi_Q\mathcal T_\xi^2\Pi_Q)_{\mathrm{tr}}.
\]
For the explicit defect representative,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_\xi=\frac12\,\theta'(\xi)^2\,\sigma_3.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the primitive longitudinal transport channel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel),\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3.
}
\end{equation}

Projecting to the shell-localized low modes gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the direct Branch-B implication is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:G2_branchB_direct}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Canonical source classification}

The principal first-order source table is
\[
\text{scalar/isotropic}\to \text{spectator},
\]
\[
\text{primitive commutator-square}\to n^\mu\sigma_3\to \lambda_c,
\]
\[
\text{transverse even}\to E^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\to \Lambda_E,
\]
\[
\text{transverse odd}\to J^\mu{}_a\sigma_a\to \Lambda_O,
\]
\[
\text{irreducible/forbidden}\to \text{projected out}.
\]

Thus, at principal order, the longitudinal source is unique in the current solved library.

\section{3. OO-candidate block interpretation}

Under the current blockwise working interpretation, the primitive longitudinal carrier is assigned to the \(OO\) candidate block.
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0;OO}^{(3)}=\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2},
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:G2_OO_transport}
\end{equation}

So the transport-level Gate-2 question is reduced to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0\ ?
}
\label{eq:G2_transport_question}
\end{equation}

\section{4. One-mediator Branch-B shell projection}

In the one-mediator Branch-B truncation, the shell-projected longitudinal coefficient is written as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3.
}
\label{eq:G2_onemediator_lambda}
\end{equation}

This is the same transport/calibration structure in a different notation:
\[
\text{transport amplitude}\times \text{Bloch overlap}\times \text{defect-profile overlap}.
\]

Hence a clean practical sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0.
}
\label{eq:G2_practical_sufficient}
\end{equation}

Under the identification of \(C_\parallel\) with the longitudinal Bloch normalization constant \(C_c\), this is equivalent to requiring
\[
C_c\neq0
\]
together with the nonzero transport branch amplitude and nonzero defect overlap.

\section{5. Final practical verdict}

Combining the Branch-B direct test and the shell-projected overlap form, the strongest practical Gate-2 statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Gate 2 passes if the current microscopic branch realizes Branch B with }
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,
\quad
I_3\neq0,
\quad
C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq0.
}
\label{eq:G2_final_practical_verdict}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the one-mediator notation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:G2_final_practical_verdict_alt}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Honest caveats}

Two honest caveats remain:

\paragraph{(i) Block-label drift}
Some local primitive formulas are written in a notation that resembles a \(TT\)-style block label, while the blockwise audit summary assigns the primitive longitudinal carrier to the \(OO\) candidate.

Therefore the fully honest statement is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{the algebraic primitive source is unambiguous, but the local block labeling is not yet fully cleaned up.}
}
\]

\paragraph{(ii) Final Bloch overlap evaluation}
The criterion
\[
C_\parallel\neq0
\quad\text{or equivalently}\quad
C_c\neq0
\]
is exact, but its actual refined locked Bloch evaluation remains to be inserted explicitly.

\section{7. Final Gate-2 closure statement}

Therefore the strongest honest current closure statement is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Transport level: Gate 2 is reduced to the single finite extraction }
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0.
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Full physical level: Gate 2 passes if }
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,\ I_3\neq0,\ C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq0.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final Summary}

The longitudinal gate is now reduced to a branch-sensitive transport/calibration split.

The exact branch decision tree is
\[
\boxed{
\text{first test }\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)};
\qquad
\text{if it vanishes, test }\lambda_c.
}
\]

In the solved lowest-order complete realization,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,\qquad \lambda_c\neq0,
}
\]
so the practical Gate-2 route is forced onto Branch B.

The primitive Branch-B transport seed is
\[
\boxed{
V^\mu_{(\parallel),\mathrm{tr}}(\xi)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\,\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\sigma_3,
}
\]
and therefore
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_c\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}\neq0.
}
\]

Under the current \(OO\)-candidate interpretation, the transport-level Gate-2 problem reduces to the single finite extraction
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0\ ?
}
\]

At the shell-projected one-mediator Branch-B level,
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{2M_X^2}\,C_\parallel\,I_3,
\qquad
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\]

Hence the strongest practical full Gate-2 sufficient condition is
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq0.
}
\]

Equivalently, in the one-mediator notation,
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_X\beta_X\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\]

Thus the strongest honest current closure statement is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{Transport level: Gate 2 is reduced to the single finite extraction }\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0;
}
\]
\[
\boxed{
\text{Full physical level: Gate 2 passes if }\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,\ I_3\neq0,\ C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq0.
}
\]

The remaining caveats are only:
\[
\boxed{
\text{block-label drift in some local notes,}
\qquad
\text{and the still-uninserted explicit Bloch evaluation of }C_\parallel.
}
\]

\section{Final Gate-3 Verdict with Transport/Calibration Split}

\section{Short explanation}

The transverse carrier problem is now reduced to a transport/calibration split,
completely parallel to the longitudinal Gate 2.

The transport-side question is whether the shell-adapted transverse witness pair survives:
\[
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0).
\]
The physical-side question is whether the surviving transport witness is not killed by the Bloch-frame overlap:
\[
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
\]

\section{1. Fixed reduced witness dictionary}

The reduced shell coefficients are already fixed by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
}
\label{eq:G3_reduced_dict_final}
\end{equation}
with
\[
I_\theta\neq0,\qquad I_{\theta'^3}\neq0.
\]

Therefore the transport-side transverse pass condition is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0)
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0)
\text{ before Bloch calibration.}
}
\label{eq:G3_transport_side}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Why the naive local \(JK\) shortcut is false}

Take the shell-adapted leading forms
\[
J\sim j\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
K\sim k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2.
\]
Then the simplest local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear reduces to
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)
+
(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
=
k_E\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}+k_O\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}=0.
\label{eq:G3_naive_JK_zero_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the naive local real Hermitian }JK\text{ term does not suffice.}
}
\label{eq:G3_no_naive_shortcut}
\end{equation}

Hence the honest microscopic frontier is not \(JK\) without momentum structure, but the derivative-resolved shell audit
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0}.
}
\label{eq:G3_true_frontier_final}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Explicit Class II compression}

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, the derivative bookkeeping compresses to the single Fourier convolution
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q'),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:G3_ClassII_overlap_final}
\end{equation}

In the minimal first-shell-dominant reduction, this further reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
\propto
iA_{G_*}(C_\alpha\!\cdot\!G_*),
\qquad
\alpha=1,2.
}
\label{eq:G3_firstshell_reduce_final}
\end{equation}

Therefore the strongest practical explicit branch-level sufficient test is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0.
}
\label{eq:G3_two_overlap_final}
\end{equation}

Under \eqref{eq:G3_two_overlap_final},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0)
}
\label{eq:G3_branch_realized_final}
\end{equation}
is realized in the current explicit Class II branch.

\section{4. Role of the \(K\)-sector}

At the explicit shell-adapted leading level, the intervalley \(K\)-sector harmonic has
\[
\mathcal K_\parallel^{a}(G_*;0)=0,
\]
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0,
}
\label{eq:G3_cparK_zero_final}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
c_E^{(K)}\neq0\ \text{in general},
\qquad
c_O^{(K)}\neq0\ \text{in general}.
}
\label{eq:G3_cEcO_K_final}
\end{equation}

So the \(K\)-sector is a direct transverse carrier, while pure axial \(JJ\) cannot generate the transverse pair by itself.
Hence the transverse witness must come from genuinely nontrivial \(JK\) and/or \(KK\) realization.

\section{5. Bloch calibration layer}

Even if the transport-side transverse witness survives, the physical coefficients still require the Bloch overlap layer:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O.
}
\label{eq:G3_bloch_norm_final}
\end{equation}

Thus the final physical transverse pass condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_bloch_pass_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, if
\[
(C_E,C_O)=(0,0),
\]
then the transverse witness is killed in the actual Bloch frame even if the transport-side branch realizes a nonzero \((c_E,c_O)\).

\section{6. Final practical verdict}

Combining transport and calibration, the strongest practical Gate-3 statement is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Gate 3 passes if the current microscopic branch realizes a nonzero derivative-resolved transverse source,}
}
\end{equation}
in practice by the explicit Class II branch test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
}
\label{eq:G3_practical_branch_final}
\end{equation}
together with the Bloch calibration requirement
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_calibration_final}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in reduced witness language,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0)
\Longrightarrow
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:G3_transport_calibration_split_final}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Honest caveat}

The final honest caveat is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{As a working-branch acceptance statement, Gate 3 is reduced to finite explicit overlap tests.}
}
\end{equation}
But
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{As a fully unconditional microscopic theorem, it still rests on the derivative-resolved }JK/KK\text{ shell audit.}
}
\end{equation}

So the correct wording is:
\[
\text{finite computation left on the explicit branch, with a structural caveat for unconditional closure.}
\]

\section{Final Summary}

The transverse gate is now reduced to a transport/calibration split exactly parallel to Gate 2.

The reduced witness dictionary is
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
}
\]
so the transport-side condition is
\[
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

However, the naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) term vanishes:
\[
\boxed{
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)
+
(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
=0.
}
\]
Therefore the honest microscopic frontier is
\[
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0}.
}
\]

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, this derivative bookkeeping compresses to
\[
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q'),
}
\]
and in the minimal first-shell-dominant reduction to the practical sufficient test
\[
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0.
}
\]

At the shell-adapted leading level, the \(K\)-sector is a direct transverse carrier:
\[
\boxed{
c_\parallel^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
c_E^{(K)}\neq0\ \text{in general},
\qquad
c_O^{(K)}\neq0\ \text{in general}.
}
\]

After Bloch calibration, the physical coefficients are
\[
\boxed{
\alpha=C_E g_E,
\qquad
\beta=C_O g_O,
}
\]
so the final physical transverse pass condition is
\[
\boxed{
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

Therefore the strongest practical Gate-3 verdict is
\[
\boxed{
\text{Gate 3 passes if }
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\quad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\quad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

Equivalently,
\[
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0),
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0)
\Longrightarrow
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

The honest caveat is:
\[
\boxed{
\text{as a working-branch acceptance statement, Gate 3 is reduced to finite explicit overlap tests,}
}
\]
but
\[
\boxed{
\text{as a fully unconditional microscopic theorem, it still rests on the derivative-resolved }JK/KK\text{ shell audit.}
}
\]

\section{Carrier-Level Acceptance Theorem Before Mass Protection}

\section{Goal}

We now combine Gate 2 and Gate 3 into a single carrier-level acceptance statement.
This theorem should decide whether the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch
already realizes a nondegenerate massless Dirac \emph{carrier candidate},
before the independent mass-protection audit of Gate 4.

\section{Fixed reduced witness dictionary}

Inside the shell seed basis, the reduced coefficients are exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 c_\parallel I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta,
}
\label{eq:carrier_reduced_dictionary}
\end{equation}
with
\[
I_{\theta'^3}\neq0,
\qquad
I_\theta\neq0.
\]

Therefore the carrier-level nondegeneracy condition is precisely
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:carrier_nondeg_target}
\end{equation}

\section{Gate 2: longitudinal Branch-B verdict}

The branch-sensitive longitudinal decomposition is
\begin{equation}
a_3(\xi)
=
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}\theta'(\xi)
+
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3
+
a_3^{\mathrm{higher}}(\xi).
\label{eq:long_branch_sensitive}
\end{equation}

In the solved lowest-order complete realization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
\qquad
\lambda_c\neq0.
}
\label{eq:branchA_dead_branchB_alive}
\end{equation}

Hence the practical longitudinal route is forced onto Branch B.

Under the current \(OO\)-candidate interpretation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0
}
\label{eq:transport_long_condition}
\end{equation}
is the transport-level longitudinal condition, and the reduced coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac{\lambda_{c;OO}}{2}I_3,
\qquad
I_3:=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3.
}
\label{eq:lambda_parallel_I3}
\end{equation}

After Bloch calibration, this requires
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_\parallel\neq0
\qquad
(\text{equivalently }C_c\neq0).
}
\label{eq:Cparallel_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Thus the practical Gate-2 verdict is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq0
\Longrightarrow
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\label{eq:gate2_practical_verdict}
\end{equation}

\section{Gate 3: transverse verdict}

The transverse reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=c_E I_\theta,
\qquad
\beta=c_O I_\theta.
}
\label{eq:trans_reduced_dictionary}
\end{equation}

So the transport-side transverse condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(c_E,c_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:trans_transport_condition}
\end{equation}

However, the naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) shortcut fails because
\begin{equation}
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)
+
(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3=0.
\label{eq:naive_JK_zero}
\end{equation}

Therefore the honest microscopic frontier is the derivative-resolved shell audit
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{0}.
}
\label{eq:trans_true_frontier}
\end{equation}

Inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II working branch, this compresses to the practical sufficient test
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0.
}
\label{eq:first_shell_two_overlap}
\end{equation}

After Bloch calibration, the physical transverse condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:CECO_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Hence the practical Gate-3 verdict is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0)
\Longrightarrow
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:gate3_practical_verdict}
\end{equation}

\section{Integrated carrier-level theorem}

Combining \eqref{eq:gate2_practical_verdict} and \eqref{eq:gate3_practical_verdict}, we obtain the strongest practical carrier-level acceptance theorem before mass protection:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq0,
}
\label{eq:carrier_long_block}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:carrier_trans_block}
\end{equation}

If both blocks hold, then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
}
\label{eq:carrier_nondeg_result}
\end{equation}
so the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is accepted as a viable microscopic \emph{carrier} for the anisotropic massless Dirac block.

\section{Equivalent compact form}

In the one-mediator Branch-B truncation, the practical closure can be summarized as
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_X C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\gamma_E C_E,\gamma_O C_O)\neq(0,0),
}
\label{eq:compact_closure_form}
\end{equation}
assuming the nonzero overlap data
\[
I_3\neq0,
\qquad
J_1\neq0,
\qquad
\beta_X\neq0.
\]

\section{Honest caveats}

Two caveats must still be stated honestly.

\paragraph{(i) Longitudinal block-label drift.}
The algebraic primitive source is unambiguous, namely the
\[
\theta'(\xi)^3\,n^\mu\Sigma_3
\]
channel, but some local notes still carry a different block-label convention than the current \(OO\)-candidate interpretation.

\paragraph{(ii) Transverse unconditional closure.}
As a working-branch statement, Gate 3 is reduced to finite explicit overlap tests.
As a fully unconditional microscopic theorem, it still rests on the derivative-resolved \(JK/KK\) shell audit.

\section{What remains after this theorem}

Once the carrier-level theorem is accepted, the only logically independent remaining gate is mass protection:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\label{eq:mass_protection_remaining}
\end{equation}
This is Gate 4.

\section{Final Summary}

The carrier-level acceptance problem before mass protection is now reduced to two practical blocks.

\paragraph{Longitudinal block.}
In the solved lowest-order class,
\[
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
}
\]
so the practical Gate-2 route is forced to Branch B.
Under the current \(OO\)-candidate interpretation, Gate 2 passes if
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,
\qquad
I_3=\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\theta'(\xi)^3\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq0.
}
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0.
}
\]

\paragraph{Transverse block.}
The naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) shortcut is false, so the honest frontier is the derivative-resolved \(JK/KK\) shell audit.
However, inside the explicit folded-Bragg Class II branch, Gate 3 is practically reduced to
\[
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\]
Then
\[
\boxed{
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

\paragraph{Integrated carrier-level theorem.}
Therefore the strongest practical carrier-level acceptance statement before mass protection is:
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{c;OO}\neq0,
\qquad
I_3\neq0,
\qquad
C_\parallel(=C_c)\neq0,
}
\]
and
\[
\boxed{
A_{G_*}(C_1\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
A_{G_*}(C_2\!\cdot\!G_*)\neq0,
\qquad
(C_E,C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\]
If these hold, then
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0),
}
\]
so the current refined locked \(+\) Class II branch is accepted as a viable microscopic \emph{carrier} for the anisotropic massless Dirac block.

\paragraph{Compact one-mediator form.}
Assuming
\[
I_3\neq0,\qquad J_1\neq0,\qquad \beta_X\neq0,
\]
the same closure is summarized by
\[
\boxed{
\alpha_X C_\parallel\neq0,
\qquad
(\gamma_E C_E,\gamma_O C_O)\neq(0,0).
}
\]

\paragraph{What remains.}
After this carrier-level theorem, the only logically independent remaining gate is mass protection:
\[
\boxed{
A_{\mathrm{res}}\cap\mathcal M_D=\{0\}.
}
\]
